Discussion Name: Should the US Recognize Palestine as a State?

1. The US Should Recognize Palestine as a State.
1.1. Con: The US should not support the two-state solution, as it is not the best outcome for the region.
1.1.1. Pro: A one-state solution encompassing both Israel and Palestine would allow both groups to inhabit the same space in peace.
1.1.1.1. Pro: Reports on polls indicate that more Israelis \(39%\) support a [joint state for the two peoples](https://knessetjeremy.com/2016/12/30/smith-poll-39-1-state-for-2-peoples-31-annex-settlement-blocks-30-2-states-for-2-peoples-based-on-1967-lines/) than support a two-state solution \(30%\).
1.1.1.1.1. Con: The [cited statistic](https://knessetjeremy.com/2016/12/30/smith-poll-39-1-state-for-2-peoples-31-annex-settlement-blocks-30-2-states-for-2-peoples-based-on-1967-lines/) implies that six out of ten Israelis \(61%\) prefer solutions other than a single state for both Palestinians and Israelis.
1.1.1.1.2. Pro: The former Israeli President, Reuven Rivlin, has said that he would rather [accept Palestinians as Israeli citizens](http://www.haaretz.com/israel-news/israel-official-accepting-palestinians-into-israel-better-than-two-states-1.287421) than accept the creation of a Palestinian state.
1.1.1.2. Con: The Arab citizens of Israel already experience large-scale discrimination and feel treated as second-class citizens or [even enemies](http://www.ynetnews.com/articles/0,7340,L-3391545,00.html), even though they are legally equal to other citizens. Judging from this, Israel has probably little interest in a joint state with Palestinians as equals.
1.1.1.2.1. Pro: Israel is characterized by inequality along ethnic lines. More than half of all Arab families in Israel are classified as poor compared to a fifth of Jewish households; the life expectancy of Arabs is about four years lower than that of Jews, their infant mortality about twice as high \([pp. 8-10](https://www.adalah.org/uploads/oldfiles/upfiles/2011/Adalah_The_Inequality_Report_March_2011.pdf)\).
1.1.1.2.1.1. Pro: 24% of Arab citizens believe that Israel is in good or very good condition, compared to 42% of Jews \([p. 1](http://www.pcpsr.org/sites/default/files/Table%20of%20Findings_English%20Joint%20Poll%20Dec%202016_12Feb2017.pdf)\). This indicates that Arab citizens are not satisfied with their situation in the state.
1.1.1.2.1.2. Pro: Arab towns and villages are heavily over-represented in the lowest socio-economic rankings of Israel, and the unrecognized Arab Bedouin villages in the Naqab are the [poorest communities](https://www.borgenmagazine.com/the-struggle-of-bedouin-poverty-in-the-israeli-negev/) in the state.
1.1.1.2.2. Pro: About [half of all Israeli Jews](http://www.pewresearch.org/fact-tank/2016/03/08/key-findings-religion-politics-israel/) voice in opinion polls that Arabs should be transferred or even expelled from Israel.
1.1.1.2.2.1. Pro: Right wing foreign minister [Avigdor Lieberman](http://www.aljazeera.com/palestinepapers/2011/01/2011124105622779946.html) already plans to swap Arab-Israeli villages in Israel with Jewish-Israeli settlements in the West Bank.
1.1.1.2.3. Con: Even if Israel has no intent of treating Palestinians as equals, increased global scrutiny on the state may pressure them into taking more positive actions.
1.1.1.2.4. Pro: Citizenship rights for Jewish and Arab citizens are not equal \([p. 16](https://www.adalah.org/uploads/oldfiles/upfiles/2011/Adalah_The_Inequality_Report_March_2011.pdf)\). This extends to laws around immigration and family unification.
1.1.1.2.4.1. Pro: The expulsions in Sheikh Jarrah in the summer of 2021 have highlighted the ways in which Israeli real estate legislation [directly discriminates](https://www.theguardian.com/commentisfree/2021/may/17/palestinians-sheikh-jarrah-jerusalem-city-identity) against those who would consider themselves Palestinian.
1.1.1.2.4.2. Pro: Inequalities between Arab and Jewish citizens of Israel are universal and enduring \([p. 7](https://www.adalah.org/uploads/oldfiles/upfiles/2011/Adalah_The_Inequality_Report_March_2011.pdf)\).
1.1.1.2.4.3. Pro: In 2010, [only](https://www.idi.org.il/media/4849/madad_2010_eng_abstract.pdf) 51% of the Jewish citizens of Israel supported equal rights between the Jewish and Arab citizens of the country \(p. viii\).
1.1.1.2.4.3.1. Pro: [Eight out of ten](http://www.pewresearch.org/fact-tank/2016/05/25/most-israeli-jews-do-not-see-a-lot-of-discrimination-in-their-society/) Israeli Arabs believe that there is already "a lot" of discrimination against Arabs taking place in Israel.
1.1.1.2.4.3.2. Con: The 2021 elections featured an Arab party in the [winning coalition.](https://www.nytimes.com/2021/06/14/opinion/israel-government-coalition.html?smid=url-share) This indicates that this attitude might be changing.
1.1.1.2.4.3.3. Pro: The [cited](https://www.idi.org.il/media/4849/madad_2010_eng_abstract.pdf)(The notion that citizenship is a legal status conferring equal •rights has been only partially internalized by the Israeli public: 51% of the general public support full equality of rights between Jews and Arabs. A breakdown of the Jewish public by level of religiosity shows that the greater the level of religious observance, the stronger the objection to equality of rights between Jews and Arabs: only 33.5% of secular Jews are opposed to such equal rights, in contrast to 51% of traditional Jews, 65% of religious Jews, and 72% \(!\) of ultra-Orthodox Jews. \(pg.viii\)) survey indicates that 72% of ultra-orthodox Jews believe this, whilst only 33.5% of secular Jews do. This is important as the ultra-orthodox are likely to be a [major voting block](https://foreignpolicy.com/2019/04/17/the-ultra-orthodox-will-determine-israels-political-future-haredi-likud-netanyahu-shas-deri-utj/) in Israel's future.
1.1.1.2.4.3.4. Pro: [86%](https://www.idi.org.il/media/4849/madad_2010_eng_abstract.pdf) believe that critical decisions for the state should be taken only by a Jewish majority \(p. v\).
1.1.1.2.4.3.5. Con: As of 2021, Israeli voters have become [more supportive](https://www.aljazeera.com/news/2021/7/2/analysis-can-united-arab-list-change-israeli-politics)(However, it was not merely the political landscape that has witnessed a change but also Israel’s society. In February 2020, polls indicated only 23 percent of Jewish voters would support the idea that the country’s Arab parties support an Israeli government. In April 2021, a poll found now 48 percent of Jewish voters had warmed up to the idea.\n\nRa’am thus became increasingly cognizant that it can achieve more within the system.\n\nUsually, the Palestine question would dominate the election programmes of the Arab parties, but turnout among the Arab community remained relatively low. This year’s turnout marked the worst in history, at 44.6 percent.) of Ra'am involvement in the governance of the Knesset. This indicates a positive change in attitude towards Arabs.
1.1.1.2.5. Pro: In 2021, the Supreme Court of Israel voted to [uphold](https://www.aljazeera.com/news/2021/7/8/israeli-supreme-court-upholds-contentious-jewish-state-law)(Proponents of the 2018 law claimed the legislation merely enshrined Israel’s existing Jewish character.\n\nCritics said it further downgrades the status of Israel’s Palestinian minority, which makes up about 20 percent of the country’s population.\n\nAdalah, a Palestinian rights group that tried to overturn the law, said the court upheld a law that “completely excludes those who do not belong to the majority group”. It said it would “continue to work internationally to expose the discriminatory and racist nature of this law”.) a 2018 law that downgrades the status of non-Jewish Israeli citizens.
1.1.1.3. Con: The popular Palestinian political [slogan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Greater_Palestine), "From the river to the sea, Palestine will soon be free," suggests that the [end goal](https://www.ajc.org/translatehate/From-the-River-to-the-Sea) is total Palestinian control, which some believe borders on [genocidal intent](https://www.jpost.com/diaspora/antisemitism/dutch-university-removes-from-the-river-to-the-sea-banner-after-protests-669847).
1.1.1.3.1. Con: Accusations of genocidal intent may not be born out by [historical record.](https://forward.com/opinion/415250/from-the-river-to-the-sea-doesnt-mean-what-you-think-it-means/?mc_cid=84b5599fab&mc_eid=f874fe4ad4)
1.1.1.4. Pro: Palestinians have a strong claim to the territory. Israel, therefore, shouldn't be given an exclusive right to the territory.
1.1.1.4.1. Pro: Palestinians want, first and foremost, a state of their own as Palestinian Arab people. In 1988 their parliament thus adopted a [declaration of independence](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palestinian_Declaration_of_Independence). Ever since, November 15 is celebrated as Independence Day in Palestine.
1.1.1.4.1.1. Pro: Indeed, among [all imaginable scenarios](http://www.peacepolls.org/peacepolls/documents/000571.pdf)(pg.4) for the region, none is more unpopular in Israel and only one is more unpopular among Palestinians than a joint state.
1.1.1.4.1.2. Con: The citizenship of Palestinians in a joint state with Israelis that ensures equal rights for everybody could deliver this independence.
1.1.1.4.1.3. Pro: Palestinian textbooks display a [world without Israel](http://www.jewishvirtuallibrary.org/new-palestinian-textbooks-present-a-world-without-israel-february-2007) and [incite](http://www.jewishvirtuallibrary.org/congressional-statement-on-palestinian-textbooks-july-2005) antisemitic feelings. This mindset precludes solution.
1.1.1.4.2. Con: [Israel's Proclamation of Independence](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israeli_Declaration_of_Independence), issued May 14, 1948, invited the Palestinians to remain in their homes and become equal citizens in the new state.
1.1.1.4.3. Con: Several [binding instruments](http://avalon.law.yale.edu/20th_century/palmanda.asp) of international law grant sovereign rights to the Jewish people in the land of Israel. Zero binding instruments of international law support the claims of the Palestinian Arabs.
1.1.1.4.4. Con: Jews have a stronger claim to the land; as the original inhabitants, they were [dispossessed and exiled by the Romans](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_the_Jews_in_the_Roman_Empire#Dispersion_of_the_Jews_in_the_Roman_Empire) in the first century. The land was subsequently invaded and occupied by several succeeding empires.
1.1.1.4.4.1. Pro: Before the [program of expulsion](http://www.meforum.org/263/why-jews-fled-the-arab-countries) from Arab countries, including Palestine, Jewish people had been living in the territory as well.
1.1.1.4.4.2. Con: The Jewish land claim is not incompatible with the claim of the Palestinians. Both states should be recognised because they both have legitimate claims to the land.
1.1.1.4.4.3. Pro: [Arabs invaded in the 7th century](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Muslim_conquest_of_the_Levant#Conquest_of_Palestine). The claim of the Palestinian Arabs is based on the principle that the descendants of invaders and occupiers have a greater right to inherit property than the descendents of the original owners.
1.1.1.4.4.4. Con: Using the original inhabitants theory is a [slippery slope fallacy](https://www.txstate.edu/philosophy/resources/fallacy-definitions/Slippery-Slope.html); one could easily argue that every country in Europe and the Americas should be given back to the natives that originally occupied the land.
1.1.1.4.5. Pro: The [vast majority](https://culturalatlas.sbs.com.au/palestinian-culture/palestinian-culture-religion)(The majority of Palestinians are Muslim, including those living overseas. All residents in the Palestinian Territories are required to declare a religion on an identification card issued by the Israeli government. According to this record, 98% of Palestinians identify as Sunni Muslims.1 Christianity is the main minority religion, with roughly 52,000 Palestinian Christians believed to be living across the occupied territories as of 2013.2 It is believed the numbers of religiously unaffiliated Palestinians \(i.e. atheist or agnostic\) in the West Bank and Gaza are very low.) of Palestinians, by virtue of being Muslims, have a strong religious connection to the territory.
1.1.1.4.5.1. Con: [Islam](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Islam#Muhammad_\(610%E2%80%93632\)) is a religion that historically started in Mecca, Saudi Arabia. [Judaism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Judaism#Origins) is a religion that can be historically traced to the Kingdom of Israel. Muslims have a very strong religious claim to Saudi Arabia and Jews have a very strong religious claim to Israel.
1.1.1.4.5.1.1. Con: Religious connections and claims to territory are not purely determined based on where a religion originated, as various widely-accepted examples illustrate.
1.1.1.4.5.1.1.1. Pro: Christianity has its origins in today's [Middle East](https://www.biblicalarchaeology.org/daily/biblical-topics/new-testament/the-origin-of-christianity/)(In BAR, Geza Vermes wrote: “Acts identifies the demographic watershed regarding the composition of the Jesus movement. It began around 40 C.E. with the admission into the church of the family of the Roman centurion Cornelius in Caesarea \(Acts 10\). Later came the gentile members of the mixed Jewish-Greek church in Antioch \(Acts 11:19–24; Galatians 2:11–14\), as well as the many pagan converts of Paul in Syria, Asia Minor and Greece. With them the Jewish monopoly in the new movement came to an end. Jewish and gentile Christianity was born.”). And yet the religion's link and claim to territories outside the region that became associated with it much later, like The [Vatican](https://www.history.com/topics/religion/vatican-city), are undisputed.
1.1.1.4.5.1.2. Pro: Muslims have [holy sites](https://guardian.ng/life/7-holiest-sites-in-islam/) that are located both in and outside Israel, but all Jewish [holy sites](https://www.worldatlas.com/articles/holy-sites-of-judaism.html) are located in Israel.
1.1.1.4.5.1.3. Pro: Because of their shared history, many of the sites that are sacred to Jewish people are sacred to [Christians](https://www.worldatlas.com/articles/holy-sites-of-christianity.html) too. Given that the US is a [Christian-majority](https://www.pewforum.org/religious-landscape-study/) country, they are unlikely to take actions that run counter to the tie between Israel and Judaism.
1.1.1.4.5.2. Pro: According to the Torah, Abraham had two sons: Ishmael and Isaac. Ishmael and Isaac are considered respectively the ancestors of the [Arab people](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ishmael#World_views) and the [Jewish people](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Isaac#Islamic_views). If the biblical ancestors of both Jewish and Arab people lived in Israel, both have a strong biblical/religious claim on the territory.
1.1.1.4.5.2.1. Pro: Their shared ancestry also implies that they are members of a large [family](https://www.sciencedaily.com/releases/2000/05/000509003653.htm)(If a common heritage conferred peace, then perhaps the long history of conflict in the Middle East would have been resolved years ago. For, according to a new scientific study, Jews are the genetic brothers of Palestinians, Syrians and Lebanese, and they all share a common genetic lineage that stretches back thousands of years.)--a fact and sentiment that could be highlighted to promote peace and reconciliation.
1.1.1.4.5.2.2. Con: If ancestry based on religious scriptures is enough to claim a territory, then all human beings should have a claim as both [Jews and Muslims](https://www.mtholyoke.edu/projects/lrc/arabic/women_deceit/texts/Adam_Eve.html) believe that all human beings are the descendants of Adam and Eve.
1.1.2. Pro: Promoting a two-state solution against resistance would repeat what has failed in the past. Smaller steps forward might be a more feasible alternative.
1.1.2.1. Con: Partition was [agreed upon by the UN](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_Nations_Partition_Plan_for_Palestine) and enjoys its [continued support](http://www.jpost.com/Arab-Israeli-Conflict/UN-chief-No-alternative-to-two-state-solution-for-Israel-Palestinians-481615).
1.1.2.1.1. Con: The UN view doesn't represent what Israelis and Palestinians think.
1.1.2.2. Pro: Many Palestinians do not themselves support the two-state plan the US will base its recognition on. This makes it unlikely that such a plan will ever be successfully adopted.
1.1.2.2.1. Pro: [Two thirds](https://mosaicmagazine.com/essay/2017/04/do-palestinians-want-a-two-state-solution/) of Palestinians reject the idea of East Jerusalem becoming the capital of a Palestinian state with West Jerusalem being controlled by Israel.
1.1.2.2.1.1. Pro: As of [2009](http://www.peacepolls.org/peacepolls/documents/000571.pdf)(pg.4), the establishment of a historic Palestine from the Jordan river to the sea elicited significantly more support among Palestinians than a two-state solution; more than half even saw this as "desirable" or "essential".
1.1.2.2.1.1.1. Con: By all standards this solution is unrealistic as it would require Israel to be subsumed into a Palestinian state. This would be acceptable neither to Israel nor the international community.
1.1.2.2.1.2. Con: In 2009, [two thirds of Palestinians](http://www.peacepolls.org/peacepolls/documents/000571.pdf)(pg.4) expressed in that a two-state solution would be at least acceptable.
1.1.2.2.1.3. Pro: According to a [2009 poll](http://www.peacepolls.org/peacepolls/documents/000571.pdf)(pg.11), nine out of ten Palestinians see it as "essential" that all of Jerusalem comes under Palestinian control; splitting the city according to the 1967 borders was "unacceptable" to half of all Palestinians
1.1.2.2.1.4. Pro: This issue is a major obstacle: eight out of ten Palestinians voiced in [2009](http://www.peacepolls.org/peacepolls/documents/000571.pdf)(pg.11) that no deal with Israel should proceed as long as there is no agreement on Jerusalem.
1.1.2.2.1.5. Con: Even if they do not support the American agenda as a whole, [nearly half](http://www.pcpsr.org/en/node/676) of all Palestinians believe that the primary goal of their nation should be to establish a Palestinian state with east Jerusalem as its capital, which is in line with the U.S. plans.
1.1.2.2.2. Pro: [Two thirds](http://www.pcpsr.org/en/node/676) of Palestinians believe that the two-state solution is no longer a viable way forward due to the already existing and expanding Israeli settlements.
1.1.2.2.3. Pro: There is [no clear support](http://www.pcpsr.org/en/node/636) for a two-state solution among Palestinians with roughly equal numbers expressing support and opposition to the idea.
1.1.2.2.4. Con: Palestinians would welcome a show of US resolve in this question. [As of 2009](http://www.peacepolls.org/peacepolls/documents/000571.pdf)(Pg.18), eight out of ten saw the American lack of resolve as a major contributor to the lack of progress in the peace process, second only to Israeli unwillingness.
1.1.2.2.4.1. Con: Only some [4%](http://www.pcpsr.org/sites/default/files/Table%20of%20Findings_English%20Joint%20Poll%20Dec%202016_12Feb2017.pdf)(Pg.7f) of Palestinians welcome a peace-process driven by the United States. They would rather see the negotiations be led by the EU, the UN, Russia and the US together, or Arab nations - or bilateral talks with Israel.
1.1.2.2.4.1.1. Con: This is likely coloured by the failure of US-led talks in the past. If the US were to recognise Palestine and actively engage in diplomatic and trade relations, Palestinian public opinion of the US will surely change.
1.1.2.2.4.2. Con: Almost [eight out of ten](http://www.pcpsr.org/sites/default/files/Table%20of%20Findings_English%20Joint%20Poll%20Dec%202016_12Feb2017.pdf)(Pg.8) Palestinians believe that the Trump administration is pro-Israel. Any American initiative will thus probably be received skeptically.
1.1.2.2.4.3. Con: [More than half](http://www.pcpsr.org/sites/default/files/poll%2062%20English%20full%20text.pdf)(Pg.13) of Palestinians want the Trump administration to stay out of the peace process.
1.1.2.2.5. Con: [59%](http://www.pcpsr.org/en/node/678) of Palestinians express support for a particular two-state plan, conditional on a peace deal between Israel and all nearby Arab states.
1.1.2.2.6. Con: As of 2009, a joint state with Palestinians and Israelis as equal citizens was unacceptable to a [minority](http://www.peacepolls.org/peacepolls/documents/000571.pdf)(PALESTINIANS ONLY\)\nOne joint state – A state in which Israelis and Palestinians are equal citizens \n\nEssential - 18\nDesirable - 13\nAcceptable - 10 \nTolerable - 12\nUnacceptable - 43 \(pg.4\)) of Palestinians; the majority would at least be willing to tolerate or even embrace this solution.
1.1.2.3. Con: The US can accelerate the peace process without directly interfering. For example, it could [neglect to veto](http://www.jewishvirtuallibrary.org/u-s-vetoes-of-un-security-council-resolutions-critical-to-israel) Security Council resolutions that punish Israeli behaviour counterproductive to peace, like settlement-building.
1.1.2.4. Pro: Getting Israel back to the negotiating table is vital for any real change to occur in the situation of Palestinians, this is highly unlikely.
1.1.2.4.1. Con: Israeli public opinion indicates that Israel has not given up on the two-state solution.
1.1.2.4.1.1. Pro: Even though the current Israeli government is not negotiating, the Israeli public [supports](https://www.jpost.com/arab-israeli-conflict/with-only-40-percent-support-israelis-still-think-2-states-best-option-poll-675838) the establishment of a Palestinian state - [even if](http://www.pcpsr.org/en/node/678) safeguards need to be established \(e.g. a multinational security force\).
1.1.2.4.1.1.1. Con: At the same time, only about [a third of Israelis](http://www.pcpsr.org/en/node/678) support the idea of splitting control over Jerusalem. This indicates that, although most Israelis are committed to a two-state solution in principle, in practice they are unwilling to make the concessions necessary to achieve such a solution.
1.1.2.4.1.1.2. Pro: Surveys emphasize that the support for a two-state solution would probably be at more than 70% in case of a referendum, as about a quarter of the population usually states that they are undecided or unsure \([p. 2](http://www.inss.org.il/uploadImages/systemFiles/No.%20916%20-%20Israeli%20on%20National%20Security%20Index.pdf)\).
1.1.2.4.1.2. Con: At the same time, issues other than national security and relations with Palestinians dominate Israeli elections. During the 2015 parliamentary vote, [a majority of voters](http://www.timesofisrael.com/cost-of-living-tops-list-of-election-issues-poll/) saw economic issues as most pressing; only a quarter gave priority to security issues.
1.1.2.4.1.3. Con: While the Israeli public may not oppose the creation of a Palestinian state, the political establishment does, and the political establishment decides what Israel's official stance on the creation of a Palestinian state is.
1.1.2.4.1.3.1. Pro: The previous leader of Israel, Benjamin Netanyahu, made it clear that there would never [be an independent Palestinian nation](https://www.washingtonpost.com/world/middle_east/on-final-day-of-campaign-netanyahu-says-no-palestinian-state-if-he-wins/2015/03/16/4f4468e8-cbdc-11e4-8730-4f473416e759_story.html?tid=a_inl&utm_term=.a1c826e38867) as long as he was in power; this may have worsened the situation in the region.
1.1.2.4.1.3.1.1. Con: Netanyahu later [denied](https://www.reuters.com/article/israel-election-netanyahu-idINKBN0MF1SP20150319) abandoning his commitment to the eventual creation of a Palestinian state. He claimed that the state could not be formed while the Palestinian Authority refused to recognise Israel as the homeland of the Jewish people and the Hamas militant group continued to control the Gaza Strip.
1.1.2.4.1.3.1.2. Pro: Even with Netanyahu ousted, the new political coalition is [unlikely](https://www.thenationalnews.com/mena/who-is-in-israel-s-new-coalition-government-1.1234863)(With the first test completed, the coalition – which brings together religious, secular, nationalist, leftist, centrist and Arab parties – now has to prove it can overcome its internal contradictions and differences to govern Israel.\n\nThe plan, hashed out in the days before the vote on Sunday night, will see the new government focus on internal issues and righting the economy after the Covid-19 pandemic.\n\nContentious issues, such as the Arab-Israeli peace process, will be put on the back burner, even as Egypt tries to broker a lasting ceasefire after an 11-day conflict in May between Israel and Hamas in Gaza.) to prioritise Palestine and independence.
1.1.2.4.1.3.1.2.1. Pro: This is likely to be because the 2021 coalition is [incredibly diverse](https://www.thenationalnews.com/mena/who-is-in-israel-s-new-coalition-government-1.1234863)(Israel’s new grand coalition has won the confidence of the Knesset and is now the official government – ending the 12-year premiership of Benjamin Netanyahu.\n\nWith the first test completed, the coalition – which brings together religious, secular, nationalist, leftist, centrist and Arab parties – now has to prove it can overcome its internal contradictions and differences to govern Israel.), with members across the political spectrum.
1.1.2.4.1.3.1.2.2. Pro: The coalition [approved](https://www.aljazeera.com/news/2021/6/15/israel-launches-air-raids-on-gaza-palestinian-security-sources)(The new government on Monday approved a “provocative” march by Israeli far-right nationalists and pro-settler groups through occupied East Jerusalem. Thousands of people, waving flags and some chanting “Death to Arabs” paraded in East Jerusalem on Tuesday, drawing anger and condemnation from Palestinians.\n\nIn another anti-Palestinian chant, Israeli demonstrators shouted: “May your village burn.”) an inflammatory far-right march through East Jerusalem that is likely to have inflamed tensions.
1.1.2.4.1.3.1.2.2.1. Con: Foreign minister Yair Lapid [spoke out against](https://www.aljazeera.com/news/2021/6/15/israel-launches-air-raids-on-gaza-palestinian-security-sources)(In a scathing condemnation on Twitter, Foreign Minister Yair Lapid said those shouting racist slogans were “a disgrace to the Israeli people”, adding: “The fact that there are radicals for whom the Israeli flag represents hatred and racism is abominable and unforgivable.”) the actions of those marching.
1.1.2.4.1.3.1.2.2.2. Con: Members of the coalition [recognised](https://www.aljazeera.com/news/2021/6/15/israel-launches-air-raids-on-gaza-palestinian-security-sources)(Mansour Abbas, whose United Arab List \(Ra’am\) party is the first Arab faction to join an Israeli coalition, said Tuesday’s march was “an attempt to set the region on fire for political aims,” with the intention of undermining the new government.\n\nAbbas said the police and public security minister should have canceled the event. “I call on all sides not to be dragged into an escalation and maintain maximum restraint,” he said.\n\nIn past years, the march passed through Damascus Gate and into the heart of the Muslim Quarter, a crowded Palestinian neighbourhood with narrow streets and alleys. But police changed the route on Tuesday to avoid the Muslim Quarter.) that the march should have been cancelled.
1.1.2.4.1.3.1.2.2.3. Pro: The Israeli police forcibly [removed](https://www.aljazeera.com/news/2021/6/15/gaza-protests-against-israeli-right-wing-march-through-jerusalem)(Ahead of the march, Israeli police forcibly removed dozens of Palestinians from outside the Old City’s Damascus Gate. At least 17 Palestinians were arrested and 33 others were wounded as Israeli police fired stun grenades in the surrounding areas of Damascus Gate.) those protesting the march.
1.1.2.4.1.3.1.3. Pro: Netanyahu's stubbornness led President Barack Obama to [state](https://www.washingtonpost.com/world/national-security/obama-says-the-prospect-of-israeli-palestinian-peace-seems-very-dim/2015/03/24/11206182-d241-11e4-a62f-ee745911a4ff_story.html?tid=a_inl&utm_term=.523e84e2be08) that there was little, if any, possibility of negotiations towards reducing tensions between Israel and Palestine.
1.1.2.4.1.3.1.4. Con: Netanyahu had [claimed](http://www.vox.com/2015/3/19/8258515/netanyahu-palestinian-walkback) that he principally supported the idea of a Palestinian state but that he didn't think it was capable of self-governing. This meant that there was potential to convince him to support the creation of an independent Palestinian state.
1.1.2.4.1.3.2. Pro: After Donald Trump was elected president, right-wing Israeli politicians [declared](http://www.jpost.com/US-Elections/Donald-Trump/Likud-MKs-react-to-Trumps-victory-in-US-Presidential-Election-472088) that the era of a Palestinian state was over.
1.1.2.4.1.3.2.1. Pro: Naftali Bennett, leader of the Jewish Home party - a lynchpin of Israel’s nationalist right and current coalition partner and Education Minister - stated that there will [never](http://www.timesofisrael.com/bennett-no-palestinian-state-even-if-world-penalizes-israel/) be a Palestinian state, even if the world penalises Israel.
1.1.2.4.1.3.3. Con: If the public supports a two-state solution, then if the political establishment maintains its opposition to the idea, it will likely be voted out in future elections.
1.1.2.4.1.3.3.1. Con: Often Israelis rank [security](https://www.aljazeera.com/news/2019/4/9/israel-elections-what-are-the-key-issues-for-voters)(Security, corruption and the economy are key issues for Israelis before the vote.\n\nThe top concern for voters is security, according to a poll conducted by political analyst Mitchell Barak of Keevon Strategies.) highly as a voting issue, however this does not mean that they would support two states as a resolution to this anxiety.
1.1.2.4.1.3.3.2. Con: Only [16%](http://www.timesofisrael.com/for-43-of-likely-voters-economic-issues-not-the-palestinians-or-iran-are-top-priority/) of Israeli voters ranked deterioration of relations with Palestinians as their most important issue in the 2013 elections. The two-state solution will likely not be the deciding factor in any election.
1.1.2.4.1.4. Pro: The Israeli public perceives the status quo as unsustainable in the long run; specifically, many Israelis believe that the current state of the conflict poses threats to [Israel's security](https://www.thechicagocouncil.org/commentary-and-analysis/blogs/americans-favor-two-state-solution-more-israelis-and-palestinians-do).
1.1.2.4.2. Pro: Israel has repeatedly waged war against the Gaza Strip in recent years. From the Israeli perspective, diplomacy is probably a lost cause in this conflict.
1.1.2.4.2.1. Pro: Israel has [repeatedly](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Operation_Defensive_Shield) [undertaken](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gaza_War_\(2008–09\)) [military operations](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Operation_Pillar_of_Defense) to stem the tide of Palestinian terrorism.
1.1.2.4.2.2. Con: Israel can wage war against the Palestinians because it knows it can rely on US support to deflect international criticism and scrutiny. American recognition of Palestine could force Israel to change the way it approaches the conflict.
1.1.2.4.3. Con: Israel is [ready](https://www.timesofisrael.com/report-pm-seeks-us-okay-to-annex-settlements-cede-arab-cities-to-palestinians/) to do land swaps with Palestine in order to make a secure border for the population of both future states.
1.1.2.4.4. Pro: Israel's unwillingness to engage in peace talks is due to [domestic political considerations](http://www.independent.co.uk/news/world/middle-east/us-offered-israel-secret-peace-deal-in-2016-but-netanyahu-walked-away-a7588526.html). A US declaration may empower small far-right parties, and exacerbate the domestic barriers to negotiating a two-state solution.
1.1.2.4.4.1. Con: Polls [indicate that](https://knessetjeremy.com/knessetjeremy-polling-average-the-israeli-poll-of-polls/) throughout the first half of 2017, Yesh Atid - which supports a two-state solution - has been either the most popular or second-most popular party among Israeli voters.
1.1.2.4.4.2. Pro: 42% of Israeli Jews consider settlements to be [beneficial](https://www.usnews.com/news/world/articles/2016-03-08/poll-plurality-of-israelis-think-settlements-help-security) towards Israel's security. Future governments will be constrained by the will of the public.
1.1.2.4.4.2.1. Con: Jewish settlers in Palestinian territory [regularly come under attack](https://www.nytimes.com/2016/07/01/world/middleeast/west-bank-kiryat-arba.html?_r=0) by Palestinian extremists.
1.1.2.4.4.3. Con: If domestic politics in Israel make any concessions to Palestinians impossible, this step needs to be taken in order to force the Israeli establishment into coming to the negotiating table.
1.1.2.4.4.4. Pro: This declaration could empower insular, far-right narratives about how [Israel is the only safe place for Jews](http://www.timesofisrael.com/netanyahu-to-french-jews-israel-is-your-home/) and that [the world hates Israel](http://www.newsweek.com/tel-aviv-diary-bibi-rails-against-world-536597). This would not encourage moderation or openness.
1.1.2.4.5. Con: Even if Israel did not follow suit and recognize Palestine, Palestinians would still see many benefits to US recognition.
1.1.2.4.5.1. Con: US recognition would up the pressure on all parties to find a solution for the conflict.
1.1.2.4.5.1.1. Pro: The [UN Security Council](https://www.un.org/press/en/2014/sc11722.doc.htm) resolution that called for a swift Israeli withdrawal from the territories captured in 1967 would have passed with US support.
1.1.2.4.5.2. Pro: Palestine would be able to [directly participate](http://www.huffingtonpost.co.uk/rosyln-fuller/palestinian-statehood-the_b_978245.html) in international organizations such as the UN and the World Bank.
1.1.2.4.5.2.1. Con: It is unlikely that participation in international organisations would have a notable effect on the political realities on the ground and the conditions under which Palestinians live.
1.1.2.4.5.2.2. Pro: Direct participation in international institutions increases Palestine's lobbying power.
1.1.2.4.5.2.2.1. Con: Power within many institutions is likely to be very small; even states like China have a proportionally small voting power share e.g. [4.4%](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_Bank#Voting_power) at the World Bank, and [6.4%](https://www.imf.org/external/np/sec/memdir/members.aspx) at the IMF.
1.1.2.4.5.2.2.2. Pro: If Palestine was a [member](https://www.worldbank.org/en/about/leadership/members)(The organizations that make up the World Bank Group are owned by the governments of member nations, which have the ultimate decision-making power within the organizations on all matters, including policy, financial or membership issues.\n\nMember countries govern the World Bank Group through the Boards of Governors and the Boards of Executive Directors. These bodies make all major decisions for the organizations.\n\nTo become a member of the Bank, under the IBRD Articles of Agreement, a country must first join the International Monetary Fund \(IMF\). Membership in IDA, IFC and MIGA are conditional on membership in IBRD.) of the World Bank, it could vote on the Bank's Executive Directors, influencing projects carried out in the West Bank and Gaza.
1.1.2.4.5.2.3. Pro: Although Israel does not recognise Palestine, statehood would allow Palestine to [appear](https://www.icj.org/palestine-icj-makes-submission-to-international-criminal-court-arguing-for-jurisdiction-over-serious-crimes/) before the International Court of Justice vis-à-vis other states to resolve any international disputes in a peaceful manner.
1.1.2.4.5.2.4. Pro: A majority of UN members [voted](https://www.rt.com/news/217975-unsc-palestine-statehood-vote/) in favour of supporting the establishment of a Palestinian state; it only failed in the UN Security Council when the US vetoed against it.
1.1.2.4.5.3. Pro: Recognition would allow Palestine to [easily trade on an international level](http://www.huffingtonpost.co.uk/rosyln-fuller/palestinian-statehood-the_b_978245.html) and independently broker foreign investment.
1.1.2.4.5.3.1. Con: The ability to negotiate trade agreements would be useless if Israel maintains its [blockades](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Blockade_of_the_Gaza_Strip) in Gaza, as it is likely to do.
1.1.2.4.5.3.1.1. Pro: The Gazan blockade is [necessary](https://www.brookings.edu/research/ending-gazas-perpetual-crisis-a-new-u-s-approach/)(Israel, with support from Egypt and, in recent years, from the Palestinian Authority \(PA\), has used a blockade to deter Hamas and deprive it of materiel. This dynamic has led to intermittent bouts of conflict. When the situation escalates, the international community has stepped in, led by Egypt and the U.N. Special Coordinator for the Middle East Peace Process \(UNSCO\), to negotiate fragile, temporary cease-fires and marginal economic relief for Gaza.) to prevent Hamas from growing stronger.
1.1.2.4.5.3.1.1.1. Con: With an arsenal of [tens of thousands of rockets](https://www.nytimes.com/2021/05/13/world/middleeast/gaza-rockets-hamas-israel.html) and other mortar projectiles, the current Gazan blockade is clearly useless; it is unlikely Hamas' capabilities would drastically change if the blockade were to be lifted.
1.1.2.4.5.3.1.2. Pro: The US has [also imposed sanctions](http://www.haaretz.com/news/u-s-imposes-sanctions-on-gaza-institutions-over-hamas-links-1.264983) on Gazan institutions as it realises the link between Hamas and the region. It may be difficult to persuade the US to remove these.
1.1.2.4.6. Pro: Israel is so heavily invested in its settlements and businesses in the Occupied Territories that it would never agree to negotiate a two-state solution.
1.1.2.4.6.1. Pro: -> See 1.1.2.4.4.2.
1.1.2.4.6.2. Con: There is a trend of [decreasing](http://www.haaretz.com/israel-news/.premium-1.599003) support among the Israeli public for the settlers. This will likely not be a constraining factor on future governments.
1.1.2.4.6.3. Pro: Israel has currently [established](http://www.haaretz.com/israel-news/.premium-1.772720) 14 economic zones in the West Bank that entrench its presence in the Palestinian territory.
1.1.2.4.6.3.1. Con: The [economy](http://www.timesofisrael.com/for-43-of-likely-voters-economic-issues-not-the-palestinians-or-iran-are-top-priority/) is the most important issue for most Israeli voters. As [the costs](http://www.haaretz.com/settlements-have-cost-israel-17-billion-study-finds-1.265190) of settlements increase, it is unlikely that settlements will swing the vote in favour of continued occupation. This is likely to stifle the continuation of Israeli economic zones in Palestine.
1.1.2.4.6.3.1.1. Pro: One study found that Israeli settlements in Palestine could cost up to [$17 billion by 2012](http://www.haaretz.com/settlements-have-cost-israel-17-billion-study-finds-1.265190). This has led to increasing opposition to settlements within Israeli society.
1.1.2.4.6.3.2. Pro: Israeli [blockades and draconian controls](https://www.theguardian.com/news/datablog/2013/oct/14/palestine-economy-how-does-it-work)(A complex web of checkpoints and roadblocks make it difficult for Palestinians to travel within the Palestinian Territories for jobs, to bank or to trade. Farmers whose land is now behind the barrier are required to apply for 'visitor permits' which Israel regularly rejects - in Akkaba it approved 49% of applications in 2011, and just 20% by 2012. More recently, a report from the World Bank found that Israeli restrictions in the West Bank alone cost the Palestinian economy $3.4bn \(£2.1bn\) a year, or 35% of its GDP.) make it difficult for the Palestinian people to find gainful employment.
1.1.2.4.6.3.3. Pro: Economic zones operate as a convenient way for Israel to get around the issue of legality of settlements: land is declared for industrial use, yet is often [populated](http://www.btselem.org/publications/summaries/201203_under_the_guise_of_legality) by settlements, and is not that important for the economy.
1.1.2.4.6.4. Pro: There are [406,000 Israeli settlers](http://www.israelnationalnews.com/News/News.aspx/213234) living in the West Bank, an increase of 29% since 2010. This is nearly 5% of Israel's population.
1.1.2.4.6.4.1. Pro: Ultra-orthodox Jews have [much higher birth rates](https://www.businessinsider.com.au/israel-has-the-highest-birth-rate-in-the-developed-world-and-thats-becoming-a-problem-2015-9?r=US&IR=T) than the general population. Given that [many settlers are ultra-orthodox](http://www.timesofisrael.com/a-look-at-israeli-settlers-by-the-numbers/), the number of Israelis in the Occupied Territories will continue increasing rapidly for the foreseeable future.
1.1.2.4.6.5. Con: The status quo involves nearly complete [alienation from the international community](http://www.haaretz.com/israel-news/1.735598).
1.1.2.5. Con: Israel can currently refuse to return to negotiations, despite strong international pressure, as it perceives US support as unconditional; US recognition of Palestine might counter this belief.
1.1.2.5.1. Pro: Israel believes that [under Republican administrations](http://www.vox.com/2016/3/8/11175136/donald-trump-benjamin-netanyahu-gop), it has free rein to do whatever it wants without any risk of jeopardizing its relationship with the US. Showing that a Republican president is willing to exert pressure for peace would force Israel to become more accountable.
1.1.2.5.2. Pro: The Obama administration's decision to [break](https://www.washingtonpost.com/world/national-security/us-declines-to-veto-un-security-council-resolution-for-israel-to-stop-jewish-settlement-activity/2016/12/23/cd4efe72-c939-11e6-bf4b-2c064d32a4bf_story.html?utm_term=.43b2a1267411) a long tradition of vetoing UN Security Council resolutions criticising Israel was seen as a [strong rebuke](https://www.nytimes.com/2016/12/23/world/middleeast/israel-settlements-un-vote.html) of Israel, and if the Obama administration had remained in office, it would have been seen as a major shift in US policy towards Israel.
1.1.2.5.2.1. Con: The Obama administration could afford to allow the resolution to pass because it was near the end of the administration's tenure, and because the election had already happened. Under [normal circumstances](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_the_UN_resolutions_concerning_Israel_and_Palestine), an American administration would never have the political support to do something like this.
1.1.2.5.3. Con: Recognition of Palestine is largely symbolic, and a willingness to do so does not signal a willingness to more substantively exert pressure on Israel \(for example, by cutting military aid\), so Israel will continue to act with impunity.
1.1.2.5.3.1. Pro: The US's unfailing support for Israel is the product of a set of [political factors](http://www.vox.com/2014/7/24/5929705/us-israel-friends) that will remain for the foreseeable future, so it is highly unlikely that the US will ever substantively reduce the degree of its support for Israel.
1.1.2.5.3.2. Con: The symbolic gesture in question is massive and unprecedented; a willingness to do it signals a general shift in attitude towards Israel on the part of the US, and Israel would be very worried about that shift in attitude.
1.1.3. Con: [Decoupling](https://www.psychologytoday.com/blog/the-five-percent/201205/the-decade-peace-in-israel-palestine) the Israeli-Palestine conflict from larger regional and world political issues \(e.g. relations with Iran\) could simplify the peace process.
1.1.3.1. Con: Decoupling would lead to a [failed policy](https://theweichertreport.com/2017/05/28/the-linkage-between-the-israeli-palestinian-conflict-and-iran/); Israel's oppressive counter-terrorism and security measures are the result of an Iranian threat. They will not leave until this is resolved.
1.1.3.2. Pro: Analyses of resolutions of similar conflicts in other world regions, such as Mozambique, suggest that peace is more likely to follow when force and authority are replaced with "[weak power](https://www.psychologytoday.com/intl/blog/the-five-percent/201205/the-decade-peace-in-israel-palestine)(Case studies of intractable conflicts like Mozambique in the 1980s-90s where sustainable resolutions eventually emerged have taught us that forceful interventions by powerful authorities or third-parties rarely help for long. Paradoxically, they have shown that it is often weaker third-parties who employ softer forms of power \(are trust-worthy, unthreatening, reliable, and without a strong independent agenda\) who often are most effective as catalysts for change.)."
1.1.4. Pro: As no workable alternative is in sight, the only viable option for Israel and Palestine is the continuation and mutual acceptance of the political status quo.
1.1.4.1. Pro: As of 2009, three-quarters of Israelis found the continuation of the status quo at least tolerable and more than half found it to be acceptable or even desirable \([p. 4](http://www.peacepolls.org/peacepolls/documents/000571.pdf)\).
1.1.4.1.1. Con: Israelis [benefit the most](https://www.middleeastmonitor.com/20210806-the-status-quo-is-being-reinforced-for-israels-benefit/) by maintaining the status quo; their attitudes should not be considered especially important when evaluating if things should change.
1.1.4.1.1.1. Pro: Israel currently [controls](https://www.aljazeera.com/news/2021/7/15/water-war-palestinians-demand-more-water-access-from-israel)(Israel directly controls 85 percent of water resources in the West Bank and has a say in how the rest is distributed, Palestinian officials told Al Jazeera. The Palestinian Authority, meanwhile, is seeking Israeli licenses to dig additional wells in the West Bank to fill the enormous need for more water.\n\nAdel Yassin, director-general of strategic planning at the Palestinian Water Authority, told Al Jazeera the Israeli water company Mekorot that supplies the occupied territories controls 42 water wells, 34 of which are located in the Jordan Valley.\n\n“The problem is not a shortage of water but the occupation’s control of our water,” said Yassin.) most of the water supply within the West Bank.
1.1.4.1.1.2. Pro: A lack of economic pressure on Israel also [reinforces the status quo](https://www.stuff.co.nz/the-press/opinion/119288551/lack-of-economic-pressure-lets-israel-maintain-status-quo) and inspires very little change.
1.1.4.1.2. Pro: The intractability of the conflict \([pp. 610-619](https://www.researchgate.net/publication/228642446_Why_Does_Fear_Override_Hope_in_Societies_Engulfed_by_Intractable_Conflict_as_It_Does_in_the_Israeli_Society)\) between Palestinians and Israel \([p. 71](https://www.researchgate.net/publication/227657606_Socio-Psychological_Barriers_to_Peace_Making_The_Case_of_the_Israeli_Jewish_Society)\) has been linked to underlying emotions and collective emotional \([pp. 447-450](https://citeseerx.ist.psu.edu/viewdoc/download?doi=10.1.1.319.8432&rep=rep1&type=pdf)\) orientations that fuel thinking and beliefs which make any progress next to impossible, especially as strong emotions are often [immune](https://www.jstor.org/stable/pdf/40607979.pdf?refreqid=excelsior%3A9d7e89b17ec5614b927244689024ed89)(Revolutionary research in the brain sciences has overturned conventional views of the relationship between emotion, rationality, and beliefs. Because rationality depends on emotion, and because cognition and emotion are nearly indistinguishable in the brain, one can view emotion as constituting and strengthening beliefs such as trust, nationalism, justice or credibility. For example, a belief that another's commitment is credible depends on one's selection \(and interpretation\) of evidence and one's assessment of risk, both of which rely on emotion. Observing that emotion and cognition co-produce beliefs has policy implications: how one fights terrorism changes if one views credibility as an emotional belief.) to logical argumentation.
1.1.4.1.3. Pro: As evidenced by the weakened position of the Israeli left and the sustained strength of the right-wing conservative agenda, the Israeli people are [not interested in changing the status quo](https://asiatimes.com/2019/02/israeli-voters-think-the-status-quo-is-just-fine/).
1.1.4.2. Con: The status quo has resulted in [at](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gaza_War_\(2008%E2%80%9309\)) [least](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Operation_Pillar_of_Defense) [three](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2014_Israel%E2%80%93Gaza_conflict) wars fought in Palestine within the last decade alone. They resulted in the deaths of thousands of civilians and destruction of significant amounts of critical infrastructure.
1.1.4.3. Con: Israel violates international law; therefore, maintaining the political status quo is not likely to be a good outcome.
1.1.4.3.1. Pro: The effective annexation of East Jerusalem by Israel in 1967 was and continues to be illegal.
1.1.4.3.1.1. Con: [Customary international law](http://www.unrod.org/docs/ICJ-Advisory2004.pdf)(p. 7) defines Israel's actions as an 'occupation,' not an 'illegal occupation' or occupation which would be considered 'against international law.'
1.1.4.3.1.1.1. Pro: Israeli occupation of Palestine has never been judged to be illegal in the 52 years of its existence as [governed by](https://www.icc-cpi.int/CourtRecords/CR2020_01501.PDF)(paragraph 2) the 'regulations annexed to the Hague Convention respecting the Laws and Customs of War on Land.'
1.1.4.3.1.1.2. Con: [A number of](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/International_law_and_Israeli_settlements) United Nations [resolutions](http://unscr.com/en/resolutions/446) affirm that Israel, the occupying power, engages in acts that violate international law within Palestine. This suggests that the illegality stems from the coincidence of illegal action with occupation \(even if occupation was legal\).
1.1.4.3.1.2. Pro: The International Court of Justice found that Israel [effectively annexed](http://opil.ouplaw.com/view/10.1093/law/9780199588893.001.0001/law-9780199588893-chapter-8) East Jerusalem with the 1980 Jerusalem Law.
1.1.4.3.1.2.1. Con: The extension of Israeli law over East Jerusalem [did not equate to annexation](https://www.polisci.upenn.edu/sites/default/files/Lustick_Has%20Israel%20Annexed%20Jerusalem_1997.pdf)(p. 40). Israel had not annexed East Jerusalem, but merely extended its norms and laws over the eastern half of the city.
1.1.4.3.1.3. Pro: Numerous [UN Security Council](http://opil.ouplaw.com/view/10.1093/law/9780199588893.001.0001/law-9780199588893-chapter-8) and General Assembly resolutions regard Israeli presence in East Jerusalem as "invalid".
1.1.4.3.1.3.1. Pro: The 1980 [Jerusalem Law](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jerusalem_Law), which proclaimed the whole city of Jerusalem as Israel's capital, was condemned as a "[violation of international law](https://unispal.un.org/DPA/DPR/unispal.nsf/0/DDE590C6FF232007852560DF0065FDDB)" by the UN Security Council.
1.1.4.3.2. Pro: Israeli actions are [in breach](https://www.wrmea.org/2021-august-september/destruction-as-a-tool-of-oppression-in-the-u.s.-and-israel.html)(The extent and destructiveness of Israel’s demolition/removal plans are striking. The Israeli Committee Against House Demolitions estimates that from the beginning of the occupation in 1967 up to 2019, Israel has razed 49,532 Palestinian structures, displacing hundreds of thousands of Palestinians. Although Israel’s home demolitions are illegal under international law, the government uses them as a tool for territorial expansion. \n\nOccupied East Jerusalem, Galilee and the Negev \(the Naqab to Palestinians\) are Israel’s most recent targets—labeled by state planners as “at risk” because of the high number of Palestinians living there.) of the material preconditions based in Articles 50 and 51, such as respect for fundamental human rights, or [proportionality](https://www.theguardian.com/world/2021/may/17/israel-gaza-conflict-200-palestinians-killed-in-a-week-say-officials) of actions.
1.1.4.3.3. Pro: Israeli actions violate [Articles 52 and 53](https://legal.un.org/ilc/texts/instruments/english/draft_articles/9_6_2001.pdf)(p. 14) of the International Law Commission. Notably, countermeasures should end once attacks stop, but the occupation has continued even when attacks have stopped.
1.1.4.3.3.1. Pro: Fatah [pledged to stop attacks](https://www.theguardian.com/world/2002/sep/11/israel) on Israel in 2002. Thus, Palestine complied with the demands of Israel.
1.1.4.3.4. Con: Israel has [the right](https://www.jstor.org/stable/2198669?origin=crossref&seq=2#metadata_info_tab_contents) to occupy and annex Palestine as it was legally captured by Israel.
1.1.4.3.4.1. Pro: The collapse of the Ottoman Empire left a gap in the [de jure](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/De_jure) chain of sovereign custody, stifling application of the law. As the [de facto](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/De_facto) occupying power, Israel bears responsibility to those under its authority, but the appropriate disposition of lands must be negotiated.
1.1.4.3.4.2. Con: Palestine has been illegally occupied since 1967, the acting Chairman of the UN Committee on the Exercise of the Inalienable Rights of the Palestinian People, Falilou Kane expressed in an [official letter](https://www.un.org/unispal/document/auto-insert-185589/) in 1980 to the President of the Security Council.
1.1.4.3.4.3. Pro: Contrary to the UN Committee on the Exercise of the Inalienable Rights of the Palestinian People, the ICC [considers](https://www.icj-cij.org/en/case/131) the West Bank as 'Occupied Territories' not as 'illegally occupied'.
1.1.4.3.4.3.1. Con: Neither Gaza nor the West Bank are under the control of a hostile army as required to be classified as 'occupied' by [Art. 42](https://ihl-databases.icrc.org/applic/ihl/ihl.nsf/ART/195-200052?OpenDocument) of the Hague Convention.
1.1.4.3.4.3.1.1. Con: [50.4% of people surveyed in Palestine](http://www.pcpo.org/index.php/polls/124-poll-no-200) support a third Intifada \(uprising\) against Israel, suggesting the majority of the population sees the country as a hostile force, even if the IDF's military presence is accepted by the Palestinian Authority.
1.1.4.3.4.3.1.2. Pro: The presence of Israeli military forces on the ground in the West Bank was agreed upon by the 1995 interim agreement in [Art. 10](https://peacemaker.un.org/sites/peacemaker.un.org/files/IL%20PS_950928_InterimAgreementWestBankGazaStrip%28OsloII%29.pdf).
1.1.4.3.4.3.1.2.1. Con: The Palestinian Authority is [no longer representative](http://www.jpost.com/Magazine/Suspended-democracy-for-Palestinians-468995) of the Palestinian people since elections have not happened for the past 10 years. In a democratic Palestine, Palestinians may have voted in support for revoking that treaty.
1.1.4.3.4.3.1.2.2. Pro: The US ended the formal occupation of Iraq with an interim agreement in 2004, despite troops remaining in the country \([p. 4](http://jcpa.org/text/occupation-sharon.pdf)\). These soldiers were no longer considered hostile or combatant because their presence was agreed upon. This is analogous to the Israeli-Palestinian agreement.
1.1.4.3.4.3.2. Pro: In an advisory opinion the [International Court of Justice](http://www.unrod.org/docs/ICJ-Advisory2004.pdf) refers to the 'occupied territories' \(p. 1\).
1.1.4.3.4.4. Con: Although the occupation in 1967 may have been legal, the continuing belligerent occupation of Palestine for more than 50 years goes against other elements of international law, such as the right of Palestinians to self-determination \([Article 2](https://legal.un.org/repertory/art2.shtml)\).
1.1.4.3.5. Pro: Israel has continued to build settlements in the West Bank which [entrenches](https://www.aljazeera.com/program/the-stream/2017/2/2/entrenching-israeli-settlements-in-palestinian-land) its position in Palestine. These settlements are illegal.
1.1.4.3.5.1. Con: The verdict that settlements are illegal is more influenced by the general [unpopularity](https://www.commentarymagazine.com/articles/the-illegal-settlements-myth/) of them rather than a close legal scrutiny.
1.1.4.3.5.1.1. Pro: Legal judgements of actors are often influenced by public perception. The general court of the EU, for example, took [Hamas](https://www.theguardian.com/world/2014/dec/17/hamas-taken-off-eu-terror-blacklist) off the EU's terror list, arguing that the inclusion was not based on sound legal reasoning but media reports.
1.1.4.3.5.2. Con: Article 6 of the [League of Nations' 1922 Palestine Mandate](https://www.washingtonpost.com/opinions/israeli-settlements-on-the-west-bank-are-disputed-not-illegal/2016/10/03/523c0196-872e-11e6-b57d-dd49277af02f_story.html?utm_term=.6bb3e2ac010c) encourages Israeli settlements west of the Jordan River. [Article 80](https://legal.un.org/repertory/art80.shtml) of the UN Charter accepts this provision and carries it over into current international law.
1.1.4.3.5.2.1. Con: Palestine was never part of the UN trusteeship system and as such Art 80 does not apply here. The closest Palestine came to trusteeship status was the [unsuccessful](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/American_trusteeship_proposal_for_Palestine) attempt by Harry Truman in 1948.
1.1.4.3.5.2.2. Con: Israel has not held itself [answerable to the United Nations](https://www.foreignpolicyjournal.com/2010/01/27/rogue-state-israeli-violations-of-u-n-security-council-resolutions/), the body which replaced the League of Nations, as such Israel expanding to fulfill instructions by an international body is simply opportunistic.
1.1.4.3.5.3. Con: Settlements are merely a [return](http://observer.com/2017/01/united-nations-jewish-settlements-arent-illegal-and-have-nothing-to-do-with-peace/) of Jewish settlers that were expelled by Arabs before 1947.
1.1.4.3.5.3.1. Pro: Settlements like [Gush Etzion](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gush_Etzion) or [Naharayim](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Naharayim) were destroyed by Arab legions prior to 1948. Israel is merely rebuilding these settlements currently.
1.1.4.3.5.3.2. Con: This claim is at least partially not true, as the Jewish population in the whole of Historic Palestine in [1946 was 602,586](https://www.researchgate.net/publication/248723811_Justin_Mccarthy_The_population_of_Palestine_population_statistics_of_the_late_Ottoman_period_and_the_Mandate_Institute_for_Palestine_Studies_Series_xxvii_242_pp) \(31%\). As of December 2015, [altogether over 800,000](http://www.israelnationalnews.com/Articles/Article.aspx/18210#.VpK885scTIU) Israeli Jews resided over the 1949 Armistice Lines \(including east-Jerusalem neighborhoods\).
1.1.4.3.5.4. Pro: The UN Security Council [declared](https://www.un.org/press/en/2016/sc12657.doc.htm) that Israel’s establishment of settlements in Palestinian territory occupied since 1967, including East Jerusalem, had no legal validity, constituting a flagrant violation of international law and a major obstacle to the vision of two states.
1.1.4.3.5.5. Pro: Israeli settlements are often built on [private](http://www.washingtonpost.com/wp-dyn/content/article/2006/11/21/AR2006112100482.html) Palestinian [land](http://www.reuters.com/article/us-israel-palestinians-settlements-vote-idUSKBN15L2F3) which is illegally acquired, often by evicting Palestinians from their homes. This reduces the land owned by Palestinians, narrowing the potential space that could be allotted to a future Palestinian state.
1.1.4.3.5.5.1. Pro: 70 per cent of \(Israel-administered\) [Area C land](http://www.btselem.org/area_c/what_is_area_c) in the West Bank is [off-limits for Palestinian construction](https://unispal.un.org/DPA/DPR/unispal.nsf/0/71A1FD027B82B40D852580EA0064468F) and development. This makes Israeli settlements more egregious as the Palestinians cannot likewise expand.
1.1.4.3.5.5.2. Con: In many instances, Palestinians do not have legal title to the land.
1.1.4.3.5.5.2.1. Pro: Land outside cities often don't have [land titles](http://www.npr.org/sections/parallels/2015/04/24/401282811/clearing-the-tangled-path-for-land-ownership-in-the-west-bank). This makes Palestinian land outside of cities an easy target for settlement expansions.
1.1.4.3.5.5.2.2. Con: Historically, from Ottoman rule to the British mandate to Jordanian annexation, [registration of land ownership has been rare](http://www.npr.org/sections/parallels/2015/04/24/401282811/clearing-the-tangled-path-for-land-ownership-in-the-west-bank); when undertaken, it has been done inefficiently. It is wrong to confiscate land from innocent Palestinians for the administrative failures of their previous rulers.
1.1.4.3.5.5.2.3. Pro: The World Bank noted that in one of their projects, only [7000 out of 22,000](http://www.npr.org/sections/parallels/2015/04/24/401282811/clearing-the-tangled-path-for-land-ownership-in-the-west-bank) hectares of Palestine have land deeds.
1.1.4.3.5.5.2.4. Pro: The Jewish settler group Nahalat Shimon was able to evict Palestinian families from their homes in [East Jerusalem](http://www.refworld.org/docid/4a82b72328.html) because they did not own titles to the land.
1.1.4.3.5.5.3. Con: In cases where Palestinians are able to show land ownership, as around [Amona](http://www.al-monitor.com/pulse/originals/2016/09/israel--palestinian-struggle-against-new-amona-settlement.html), this obstructs further settlements.
1.1.4.3.5.5.3.1. Con: Attempts to remove Israeli settlers from the small settlement of Amona resulted in [violent clashes](https://www.thestar.com/news/world/2017/02/01/israel-evicts-west-bank-outpost-as-new-settlements-approved-day-before.html) and pressure for a [bill to legalize settlements](http://www.timesofisrael.com/facing-backlash-over-amona-jewish-home-leaders-vow-to-pass-legalization-bill/).
1.1.4.3.5.5.3.1.1. Pro: Removal of Israeli settlers from Gaza led to violent clashes with the IDF and an [emotive backlash](http://www.haaretz.com/israel-news/1.667736) from the settlers.
1.1.4.3.5.5.3.2. Pro: Eventually, the settlement of Amona was removed because it was found to be [illegal](https://www.aljazeera.com/news/2017/2/1/israel-evacuates-settlers-from-illegal-amona-outpost).
1.1.4.3.5.5.4. Pro: Land taken by Israel through military requisition orders was declared [illegal](http://www.btselem.org/download/201007_by_hook_and_by_crook_eng.pdf)(p. 22) by the Israel High Court of Justice, yet these orders have not been stopped, nor has the land previously been seized returned.
1.1.4.3.5.6. Pro: The International Court of Justice in its Advisory Opinion on Israel’s Separation Wall in 2004 reaffirmed the illegality of settlements \([p. 196](http://www.icj-cij.org/docket/files/131/1671.pdf)\).
1.1.4.4. Pro: As of 2009, a majority of Palestinians were willing to accept or even embrace a continuation of the political status quo under the condition that the Palestinian territories would be able to develop economically \([p. 4](http://www.peacepolls.org/peacepolls/documents/000571.pdf)\).
1.1.4.4.1. Pro: Asked about the most serious problems confronting Palestinian society today, slightly more Palestinians name unemployment and poverty than occupation and settlements. The economy is thus of at least as much relevance to Palestinians as the political situation \([pp. 1-2](http://www.pcpsr.org/sites/default/files/Table%20of%20Findings_English%20Joint%20Poll%20Dec%202016_12Feb2017.pdf)(Table P20)\).
1.1.4.4.1.1. Con: Economic problems are the [result](http://www.ps.undp.org/content/papp/en/home/countryinfo.html) of occupation and settlements; so in fact, concern about the economy indicates that the political status quo is of great importance to Palestinians.
1.1.4.4.1.1.1. Pro: Economic mobility within the West Bank is hindered substantially by a system of [blockades and checkpoints](https://www.theguardian.com/news/datablog/2013/oct/14/palestine-economy-how-does-it-work). Given that these are maintained for security reasons to prevent terrorist attacks, Israel will never agree to lift them.
1.1.4.4.1.1.2. Pro: Gaza's economic development is crippled by the [Israeli blockade](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Blockade_of_the_Gaza_Strip), which is maintained for security reasons; lifting it would result in increased rocket and terrorist attacks so it will never be lifted, forcing economic dependence on Israel.
1.1.4.4.1.1.2.1. Pro: Gazans are, on average, [worse off than in the 1990s](http://www.bbc.co.uk/news/world-middle-east-20415675).
1.1.4.4.1.1.2.1.1. Pro: The [poverty rate in Gaza](https://databank.worldbank.org/data/download/poverty/33EF03BB-9722-4AE2-ABC7-AA2972D68AFE/Global_POVEQ_PSE.pdf) is greater than 50% and increasing. In contrast, the poverty rate in West Bank is less than 15% and improving \(p. 1\).
1.1.4.4.1.1.2.1.2. Pro: The unemployment rate is significantly [higher in Gaza](https://gisha.org/en/gaza-unemployment-rate-soars-to-50-2-in-months-following-may-escalation/) \(50%\) - particularly among [young Gazans](https://www.bbc.com/news/world-middle-east-20415675) - than in [West Bank](https://reliefweb.int/report/occupied-palestinian-territory/gaza-unemployment-rate-second-quarter-2020-491).
1.1.4.4.1.1.2.2. Pro: The Israeli blockade of Gaza [hampers](http://www.un.org/apps/news/story.asp?NewsID=30948#.WPapC1KZORt) UN relief work. Important construction material required for rebuilding houses and roads is not allowed to enter Gaza.
1.1.4.4.2. Con: The attitude of Palestinians has probably changed dramatically since 2009, especially considering major events since then like the [2014 war in Gaza](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2014_Israel%E2%80%93Gaza_conflict).
1.1.4.4.3. Con: [More than half](http://www.pcpsr.org/en/node/676) of Palestinians support the return to an armed intifada.
1.1.4.4.4. Pro: "[Israeli-imposed economic restrictions continue to constrain sustainable economic growth](http://www.ps.undp.org/content/papp/en/home/countryinfo.html)" in Palestine. By removing these restrictions, it would be possible to promote economic growth without large-scale political change.
1.1.4.5. Pro: Palestinians have been consistently responsible for the failure of peace processes, forcing Israel to maintain an occupying force in order to protect itself.
1.1.4.5.1. Pro: Palestinian militants are a threat to Israel.
1.1.4.5.1.1. Con: The number of Israelis killed by Palestinian militants is so [small](http://www.jewishvirtuallibrary.org/total-casualties-arab-israeli-conflict) - less than 100 Israelis per year - that it could not be considered a legitimate security concern.
1.1.4.5.1.2. Pro: When Israel withdrew from the Gaza Strip in 2005, it was taken over by Hamas, which then used the territory to launch [numerous missile attacks](http://www.bbc.com/news/world-middle-east-32053999) on Israeli civilian targets. The same would happen in the case that Israel ends its presence in Palestinian territory.
1.1.4.5.1.2.1. Con: Israel already easily defends itself from these missile attacks from Gaza using the [Iron Dome missile defense system](http://www.haaretz.com/israel-news/1.604039). The success of this system makes obsolete the need for continued occupation.
1.1.4.5.1.2.1.1. Con: Iron Dome is still not a perfect defense. In the 2014 Gaza War, [Israeli civilians were still killed](https://www.amnesty.org.uk/unlawful-and-deadly-palestinian-rocket-attacks-gaza) by rocket fire from Gaza.
1.1.4.5.1.2.1.2. Pro: Iron Dome can intercept [approximately 90%](http://aviationweek.com/defense/iron-dome-blunts-90-enemy-rockets) of all projectiles fired from Gaza.
1.1.4.5.1.2.1.3. Con: Each interceptor missile [costs](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iron_Dome#Cost) $20,000-$50,000 USD. Continually utilizing missile defense would drain the Israeli security budget.
1.1.4.5.1.2.2. Pro: If Israel does not militarily control the West Bank then it would have to take [military actions](https://www.idfblog.com/facts-figures/rocket-attacks-toward-israel/) to curb missile attacks, as was carried out in Gaza in 2008, and 2012. This results in excessive civilian casualties, and the destruction of infrastructure.
1.1.4.5.1.3. Pro: [Every year](http://www.jewishvirtuallibrary.org/comprehensive-listing-of-terrorism-victims-in-israel) Israelis die from terror attacks committed by Palestinians or launched from Palestinian territory.
1.1.4.5.2. Pro: Palestinians list [preconditions](http://www.jpost.com/Arab-Israeli-Conflict/PA-Only-precondition-for-talks-is-that-Israel-announce-commitment-to-two-states-499991) to engage in peace talks. If a party needs to be brought back to the negotiation table, it is Palestine.
1.1.4.5.3. Pro: Israel has offered Palestine sovereignty on multiple occasions, these offers have been consistently rejected.
1.1.4.5.3.1. Con: Abbas has consistently, and [recently](http://foreignpolicy.com/2017/05/03/remember-the-two-state-solution-abbas-does/), accepted the two-state solution. Rejection of individual peace plans because of their flaws is not the same as rejecting the two-state solution itself.
1.1.4.5.3.2. Con: Israel has also rejected peace plans, yet that does not mean it has rejected the two-state solution.
1.1.4.5.3.2.1. Pro: Netanyahu [rejected](http://www.jpost.com/Arab-Israeli-Conflict/Report-Netanyahu-rejected-peace-plan-proposed-by-Kerry-at-secret-2016-meeting-481969) a peace plan proposed by former US Secretary of State John Kerry in a secret 2016 meeting.
1.1.4.5.3.2.2. Pro: Israel [rejected](http://www.telegraph.co.uk/news/worldnews/1547036/Israel-rejects-Arab-peace-initiative.html) an Arab peace initiative in 2007.
1.1.4.5.3.3. Pro: [Almost two thirds](http://www.pcpsr.org/en/node/676) of Palestinians support abandoning the Oslo Accords, and thereby the foundations of the American-supported peace talks.
1.1.4.5.3.4. Pro: Abbas rejected a peace proposal made by Olmert in [2008](http://www.timesofisrael.com/abbas-admits-he-rejected-2008-peace-offer-from-olmert/).
1.1.4.5.3.4.1. Con: Olmert's offer lacked [transparency](http://www.jpost.com/Diplomacy-and-Politics/Details-of-Olmerts-peace-offer-to-Palestinians-exposed-314261) as he was unwilling to provide a map of the envisioned partition of Jerusalem. Therefore, the offer was difficult to accept.
1.1.4.5.3.4.2. Con: [Olmert blames](http://www.jpost.com/Diplomacy-and-Politics/Details-of-Olmerts-peace-offer-to-Palestinians-exposed-314261) the failure of the peace process on Israeli ministers Tzipi Livni and Ehud Barak.
1.1.4.5.3.5. Pro: After disillusionment with Israel's refusal to negotiate and arrive at a peace treaty, Mahmoud Abbas, the president of the Palestinian Authority, sought to [bypass the peace process](https://www.foreignaffairs.com/articles/middle-east/2011-08-19/palestine-goes-un) with Israel, showing that he believed it to be beyond recovery.
1.1.4.5.3.6. Pro: US officials blame Abbas for '[shutting down](https://www.theatlantic.com/international/archive/2014/07/indyk-netanyahu-and-abbas-loathe-each-other/373922/)' during the 2014 peace negotiations, even though Israel was prepared for an agreement.
1.1.4.5.3.6.1. Con: Abbas had [no choice](https://newrepublic.com/article/118751/how-israel-palestine-peace-deal-died) but to walk away from those negotiations as Israel refused to stop expanding its settlements, a move designed to undermine Abbas and portray him as having made a peace deal by selling off Palestinian land.
1.1.4.5.3.7. Pro: A US-European draft resolution at the UN Security Council that would have extended the Palestinian Authority's authority to the Gaza Strip and stipulated the immediate start of reconstruction was [rejected](https://www.middleeastmonitor.com/20150227-pa-rejects-draft-resolution-to-extend-its-control-of-the-gaza-strip/) by the Palestinian Authority itself.
1.1.4.5.4. Con: If the occupation had reasons to believe in a serious threat, Israeli civilians would not be allowed to settle there.
1.1.4.5.4.1. Pro: Settlers often [say](https://www.bbc.co.uk/news/world-middle-east-38458884)(Settlers themselves choose to live in these communities for a range of reasons - from economic, encouraged by government subsidies, to religious, based on the belief that God gave the land to the Jewish people.) they live in occupied Palestine because the land was promised to them by God.
1.1.4.5.5. Con: The Oslo Accords were a land-for-peace deal. Israeli settlement expansions and the creation of a security barrier that encroached on Palestinian land were clear indications of Israel's [non-compliance](https://www.theguardian.com/commentisfree/2013/sep/12/oslo-israel-reneged-colonial-palestine) with the peace agreement.
1.1.4.5.6. Con: The failure of the Camp David negotiations in 2000 were the result of Israel's unacceptable demands.
1.1.4.5.6.1. Pro: Barak's offer was not sufficient as it only envisioned a gradual control over only 92% of the West Bank \([p. 16](http://www.belfercenter.org/sites/default/files/legacy/files/pressman.pdf)\).
1.1.4.5.6.2. Pro: Israel demanded a demilitarized state \([p. 16](http://www.belfercenter.org/sites/default/files/legacy/files/pressman.pdf)\). This would have abrogated Palestine's right to self-determination.
1.1.4.5.6.3. Pro: In an interview, Barak admitted that a "[razor-thin](http://www.nybooks.com/articles/2002/06/13/camp-david-and-after-an-exchange-1-an-interview-wi/)" strip of territory between Jerusalem and the Jordan River would have been transferred to Israeli control. This would have cut the West Bank apart and therefore was not acceptable to the Palestinians.
1.1.5. Con: Previous peace talks have failed due to random, unpredictable, external setbacks, not internal factors. US recognition of Palestine is required to force Israel back to the negotiating table.
1.1.5.1. Pro: The [Taba Summit](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Taba_Summit#End_of_the_negotiations) in 2001 by Clinton almost reached a final settlement, however upcoming Israeli elections meant that they could not be continued.
1.1.5.2. Pro: [2017 negotiations](http://www.haaretz.com/israel-news/.premium-1.775258) between Netanyahu and the Israeli leader of the opposition indicated plans for dramatic moves towards territorial compromise and peace, but the Amona Crisis destroyed the negotiations.
1.1.5.2.1. Con: The negotiations failed when Netanyahu [consciously decided](http://www.independent.co.uk/news/world/middle-east/us-offered-israel-secret-peace-deal-in-2016-but-netanyahu-walked-away-a7588526.html) not to allow the opposition party into his coalition.
1.1.5.3. Pro: The Oslo Accords, signed in 1993 and 1995, ultimately failed due to [Yitzhak Rabin's assassination](http://www.newyorker.com/magazine/2015/10/26/shot-in-the-heart).
1.1.5.4. Con: The [decline](https://freedomhouse.org/country/gaza-strip/freedom-world/2020)(In March, the Hamas-led government cracked down on peaceful demonstrations against economic hardship, arresting more than 1,000 and beating a number of participants in what amounted to an escalation in repressive tactics.) in democratic norms within Palestine [limits](https://carnegieeurope.eu/2021/04/23/halting-palestine-s-democratic-decline-pub-84383)(The weakness of the Palestinian leadership has been a fundamental impediment that has further skewed the power dynamic in Israel’s favor.) strong and representative leadership.
1.1.5.4.1. Pro: Israelis have also indicated a [willingness](https://www.nytimes.com/2016/12/29/world/middleeast/israel-palestinians-two-state-solution.html)(Jewish Israelis became much less likely to say that Israel should be “Jewish and democratic,” with growing factions saying that it should be democratic first or, slightly more popular, Jewish first.) to tradeoff democracy in order to preserve the Jewish nature of their state; this is unlikely to be palatable to the Palestinians.
1.1.5.4.2. Con: Though the PA may have abandoned democracy, Palestinians are still willing to take [peaceful, unified action](https://www.nytimes.com/2021/05/18/world/middleeast/palestine-strike.html)(But on Tuesday, they came together in a general strike to protest their shared treatment by Israel, in what many Palestinians described as a rare show of political unity.\n\nMustafa Barghouti, an independent politician who attended a rally in central Ramallah on Tuesday morning, said the protests constituted “a very significant day.”\n\n“It reflects how Palestinians now have a unified struggle against the same system of apartheid,” he added.) to defend their rights, and assert their desire for a state.
1.1.5.4.3. Con: As the [de facto](https://www.nytimes.com/2021/05/19/opinion/israel-palestine.html?action=click&module=RelatedLinks&pgtype=Article)(Many diplomats and analysts around the world I have spoken to in recent years understand that the two-state solution is dead. Israel has killed it. When I ask why they don’t call for equal rights for Palestinians to end what is increasingly obviously a de facto apartheid system, they point out the official Palestinian position remains for a separate state. When they ask me what the Palestinian leadership is waiting for, I have no good answer.) position of Palestine is a two state solution, it is unclear why any renewed leadership is necessary.
1.1.5.4.4. Pro: Approximately half of Palestinians have [never voted](https://carnegieeurope.eu/2021/04/23/halting-palestine-s-democratic-decline-pub-84383)(Ninety-three percent of eligible voters across Gaza and the West Bank have registered—of which roughly half \(ages eighteen to thirty-three\) have never voted. For some Palestinians, it is a moment of hope; for the EU, it is a moment of sobriety.) as the last elections were held in 2006.
1.1.5.5. Con: The contested Jerusalem is likely to remain a [hot button issue](https://www.nytimes.com/2016/12/29/world/middleeast/israel-palestinians-two-state-solution.html)(Both sides claim Jerusalem as their capital and consider it a center of religious worship and cultural heritage. The two-state solution typically calls for dividing it into an Israeli West and a Palestinian East, but it is not easy to draw the line — Jewish, Muslim and Christian holy sites are on top of one another. Israel has declared Jerusalem its “undivided capital,” effectively annexing its eastern half, and has built up construction that entrenches Israeli control of the city.) that waylays peace talks, particularly as Israel has annexed the Eastern half.
1.1.5.5.1. Pro: 2021 evictions from Sheikh Jarrah in East Jerusalem [spurred](https://www.nytimes.com/article/israel-gaza-what-we-know.html?action=click&module=RelatedLinks&pgtype=Article)(The root of the latest violence is an intense dispute over East Jerusalem, which is predominantly Palestinian. Protests had gone on for days ahead of a Supreme Court ruling, originally expected on May 10 but then postponed, on the eviction of several Palestinian families from East Jerusalem. Israeli officials described it as a dispute over real estate. Many Arabs called it part of a wider Israeli campaign to force Palestinians out of the city, describing it as ethnic cleansing.\n\nThe protests sharply intensified after Israeli police prevented Palestinians from gathering near one of the Old City’s ancient gates, as they have customarily done during the holy month of Ramadan. The police responded on May 10 by raiding the Aqsa Mosque compound, one of Islam’s holiest sites, to keep Palestinian protesters from throwing stones, they said.
