Hundreds of Palestinians and a score of police officers were wounded in the skirmish.) protests from the Palestinians which escalated to 11 days of intense fighting between Israel and Hamas.
1.1.5.6. Con: The US should demand Palestinian recognition of Israel as a Jewish state before recognizing Palestine.
1.1.5.6.1. Pro: Recognising Palestine unconditionally gives away a valuable bargaining tool the US has to bring Palestine to the negotiating table.
1.1.5.6.1.1. Pro: Once a Palestinian state is recognised, the Palestinian Authority has little incentive to negotiate with the US or Israel.
1.1.5.6.1.2. Con: With the international community finally on its side, it makes little sense for the Palestinian Authority to act belligerent and uncooperative, laying waste to the diplomatic goodwill shown by the US in recognising it as a state.
1.1.5.6.2. Pro: Palestinians do not recognize Israel as a Jewish state which is an obstacle to the peace process.
1.1.5.6.2.1. Con: Recognition of Israel as a Jewish state could make Arab residents of Israel feel unwelcome and marginalized. This may cause domestic issues.
1.1.5.6.2.1.1. Con: Israel is already accepted as a Jewish state [legally](https://www.bbc.co.uk/news/world-middle-east-44881554)(The "nation state" law says Jews have a unique right to national self-determination there and puts Hebrew above Arabic as the official language.\n\nArab MPs reacted furiously in parliament, with one waving a black flag and others ripping up the bill.\n\nIsrael's prime minister praised the bill's passage as a "defining moment".\n\n"A hundred and twenty-two years after \[the founder of modern Zionism Theodore\] Herzl made his vision known, with this law we determined the founding principle of our existence," Benjamin Netanyahu said.\n\n"Israel is the nation state of the Jewish people, and respects the rights of all of its citizens."). It is not clear that tensions could worsen.
1.1.5.6.2.2. Pro: Once a Jewish state is recognized, the Jewish people will feel less [threatened](https://www.washingtoninstitute.org/media/3372) by Palestine; opposition to a Jewish state is seen as continuing opposition to Israel.
1.1.5.6.2.2.1. Con: Israel [threatens](https://www.timesofisrael.com/netanyahu-no-palestinian-state-under-my-watch/) the [creation](https://www.reuters.com/article/us-israel-palestinians-kerry/israel-seeks-u-s-block-of-palestinian-statehood-drive-idUSKBN0JT1A020141216) of a [Palestinian State](https://www.csmonitor.com/World/Middle-East/2009/1115/p01s01-wome.html/%28page%29/2) encouraging [illegal settlements](https://www.cbsnews.com/news/group-israel-controls-42-of-west-bank/)(Jewish settlements control more than 42 percent of the West Bank.) in the area. Israel should practice what it preaches should it wish for a deescalation of conflict with Palestine.
1.1.5.6.2.2.2. Pro: Israeli ex-PM, [Netanyahu](https://www.haaretz.com/1.5163334), has supported the idea that all that lies between Palestine and a two-state solution is recognition of the Jewish character of Israel.
1.1.5.6.2.2.3. Con: Recognition of Jewish statehood is required only from the Palestinians, not the international community. There is no reason why Palestinian recognition of a Jewish state is what validates the existence of a Jewish homeland.
1.1.5.6.2.3. Con: Not all Israelis demand that Palestine recognises Israel as Jewish.
1.1.5.6.2.3.1. Pro: Haredi Jews, who make up 10% of Israel's population, and are expected to make up 25% of the population within a few decades, are, oftentimes violently, [opposed](https://www.theguardian.com/commentisfree/belief/2016/may/12/for-haredi-jews-secular-zionism-remains-a-religious-heresy) to the idea of a Jewish state.
1.1.5.6.2.3.2. Pro: [Shimon Shamir](http://www.haaretz.com/ask-mustafa-khalil-1.282123), former ambassador to Egypt and Jordan, regards the Jewishness of Israel as an internal matter that should not be put in front of the international community.
1.1.5.6.2.3.3. Pro: [Yonatan Touval](http://www.nytimes.com/2009/05/13/opinion/13iht-edtouval.html), director of international affairs at Tel Aviv University, criticized the demand as an obstacle to peace and as a danger to Arab-Israelis.
1.1.5.6.2.3.4. Con: For many [Jews in Israel](https://www.brookings.edu/research/the-2011-public-opinion-poll-of-jewish-and-arab-citizens-of-israel/), Palestinian recognition of their state as the [Jewish homeland](https://www.reuters.com/article/us-palestinians-israel-jewish-idUSTRE53F4TS20090416) is far more important than a peace deal.
1.1.5.6.3. Con: Continued annexation has weakened Palestine such that it has [very little](https://www.nytimes.com/2021/05/27/opinion/israel-palestinians-two-state-solution.html)(The Trump administration supported efforts of the Israeli government to move toward annexation of land. Had all those efforts come to pass, we would have reached the point of no return. The land would no longer be divisible, and the political future of two states would have been closed to us forever. Further, this policy weakened and delegitimized the Palestinian Authority and included cutting off financial support.) bargaining power; forcing it to recognise the Jewish character of Israel would remove their last bargaining chip.
1.1.5.7. Pro: Peace talks [in 2008](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israeli%E2%80%93Palestinian_peace_process#Israeli.E2.80.93Palestinian_talks_in_2007_and_2009) failed in part because of Olmert's [resignation on charges of corruption](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ehud_Olmert#Stepping_down).
1.1.6. Con: There is political support for the two state solution indicating that it could be a positive end goal for the region.
1.1.6.1. Con: The Israeli-Palestinian conflict possesses an almost uniquely problematic combination of ethnic, religious, ideological and nationalist animosity, making it particularly difficult to solve.
1.1.6.2. Con: Calls for a two-state solution were significantly weakened in 2021, with a shift amongst experts towards believing a one-state solution is [likely](https://www.nytimes.com/2021/05/19/opinion/israel-palestine.html?action=click&module=RelatedLinks&pgtype=Article)(Among scholars and experts on the Middle East, one recent poll found, 66 percent say there is a one-state reality. There is also a growing shift in mainstream organizations that have been hesitant to call for greater change: The Carnegie Endowment for International Peace recently released a report calling for a break from the two-state approach.).
1.1.6.2.1. Pro: As of early 2021, Palestinians in the Gaza Strip had begun to indicate a preference for a [prioritisation](https://www.nytimes.com/2021/05/15/world/middleeast/israel-palestinian-gaza-war.html?action=click&module=RelatedLinks&pgtype=Article)(In Gaza, where the Israeli blockade has contributed to an unemployment rate of about 50 percent, Hamas’s popularity was dwindling as Palestinians spoke increasingly of the need to prioritize the economy over war.) of their economy over political nationhood.
1.1.6.2.2. Pro: Amongst Jewish Israelis, the two state solution [dwindled](https://www.vox.com/policy-and-politics/22442052/israel-palestine-two-state-solution-gaza-hamas-one)(A 2020 poll found that a scant 10 percent of Jewish Israelis supported a one-state solution in which Palestinians and Jewish Israelis are equal citizens. And only 13 percent of Israel’s Arab citizens supported such an option. By contrast, 42 percent of Jewish Israelis and 59 percent of Arab Israelis supported two states — with much of the opposition among Jews stemming from a sense that two states were not currently achievable rather than a principled unwillingness to compromise.) in support, though this was largely due to a belief that it was not feasible rather than a poor principled stance.
1.1.6.3. Pro: Many world leaders have established support for a two state solution.
1.1.6.3.1. Con: The normalisation of Israeli and Arab economic links has [reduced](https://www.nytimes.com/2021/05/11/opinion/jerusalem-rockets-israel.html?action=click&module=RelatedLinks&pgtype=Article)(The Israeli government, the surrounding Arab nations and the Palestinian Authority all desperately want the answer to be “no” — Israel because it would find little support from a left-leaning White House, let alone the rest of the world, for a big crackdown on Palestinians; the Arab governments because most of them want to do business with Israeli tech-makers, not get mired defending Palestinian rock-throwers; and the Palestinian leadership because it would expose just how little it controls the Palestinian street anymore.) political support for the Palestinian cause.
1.1.6.3.1.1. Pro: As of 2021, the Palestinian conflict had [dropped off](https://www.nytimes.com/2021/05/11/opinion/jerusalem-rockets-israel.html?action=click&module=RelatedLinks&pgtype=Article)(The most obvious and important point is that a dangerously naïve consensus has emerged in Israel in recent years suggesting that Israel basically has the Palestinian conflict suppressed and those Palestinians living in the West Bank and East Jerusalem are basically resigned to living under permanent Israeli control. This consensus was so powerful that in all four of Israel’s recent elections, the question of peace with the Palestinians — how to achieve it and what happens if it is ignored — was not on the agenda.\n\nThe Abraham Accords engineered by the Trump administration, normalizing relations between Israel and the United Arab Emirates, Bahrain, Sudan and Morocco — while valuable in helping to stabilize the region — also reinforced the notion that the Palestinian cause is basically yesterday’s news.) the radar as an important political issue for voting Israelis.
1.1.6.3.2. Pro: US President, Joe Biden \(2021-\), believes that the two state solution is the [only viable outcome](https://www.aa.com.tr/en/middle-east/biden-says-two-state-solution-only-answer-to-israel-palestine/2250673)("There is no shift in my commitment to the security of Israel. Period. No shift, not at all. But I'll tell you what there is a shift in. The shift is that we still need a two-state solution. It is the only answer. The only answer," Biden said at a news conference with South Korean President Moon Jae-in.\n\nHis remarks came after a group of progressive lawmakers and others in the Democratic Party called for a halt to military sales to Israel because of its bombardment of Gaza Strip, Palestine.\n\nBiden said he spoke to Palestinian President Mahmoud Abbas and told him his plans for Palestine that includes providing security in the West Bank.\n\n"And recently we renewed the security commitment, as well as an economic commitment to the people on the West Bank," said Biden. "I also indicated to the Israelis that I thought it was very important that they stop in Jerusalem this inner communal fighting, it has to end.”) for the region. This is likely to maintain pressure on negotiations.
1.1.6.3.2.1. Pro: Secretary of State \(2021-\), Joe Blinken, said that he [supported](https://www.france24.com/en/middle-east/20210525-us-pledges-support-for-gaza-truce-but-without-benefit-for-hamas)("Ultimately, there's a possibility of resuming the effort to achieve a two-state solution, which we continue to believe is the only way to truly assure Israel's future as a Jewish and democratic state, and of course to give the Palestinians the state they're entitled to," he said in Jerusalem.\n\nDuring Tuesday's visit, Blinken vowed to rebuild US relations with Palestinians by reopening a consulate in Jerusalem and giving millions in aid to help the war-ravaged Gaza Strip.\n\nThose announcements signalled a clean break with US policy under former president Donald Trump who had shuttered the diplomatic mission for Palestinians in 2019 and slashed aid to the Palestinian Authority.) the two-state solution.
1.1.6.3.3. Pro: King Abdullah of Jordan [confirmed](https://www.jordantimes.com/news/local/king-reaffirms-two-state-solution-only-way-forward)(The King said, prior to his meeting as the first leader from the region with US President Joe Biden, he held talks with Palestinian and Israeli leaders aiming to "unify messaging" as part of efforts to bring the two sides back to the negotiation table. \n\n"... I came out of those meetings feeling very encouraged, and I think we have seen in the past couple of weeks, not only a better understanding between Israel and Jordan, but the voices coming out of both Israel and Palestine that we need to move forward and reset that relationship," the King said.) his support for the two state solution in 2021.
1.1.6.3.3.1. Pro: King Abdullah's support for the two state solution came after the Israeli right wing indicated a [desire](https://www.jpost.com/middle-east/jordan-cant-be-palestinian-homeland-in-two-state-solution-king-abdullah-674941)(“Jordan is Jordan,” Abdullah said in response to a question about Israeli right-wing proposals to resolve the Israeli-Palestinian conflict by transforming Jordan into a Palestinian homeland. It’s a scenario that appears plausible to the Israeli Right, given that a majority of Jordanians are ethnically Palestinian.\n\nAbdullah, however, emphatically nixed the idea, describing his country as one with “a mixed society from different ethnic and religious backgrounds.”\n\n“The Palestinians do not want to be in Jordan,” Abdullah said. “They want their lands, they want their football team. They want their flag to fly above their houses.”\n\nThroughout the interview he underscored the importance of a two-state resolution to the Israeli-Palestinian conflict. Jordan’s vision for that plan is two states based on the pre-1967 lines, in which east Jerusalem and all of the West Bank would be within the final borders of a Palestinian state.) to make Jordan a Palestinian homeland. This indicates that other solutions are not considered viable.
1.1.6.3.4. Con: External support for the two state solution is unlikely to meaningfully alter the willingness of Israel or Palestine to negotiate.
1.1.6.3.4.1. Pro: Palestinians have indicated a desire to [continue violence](https://www.washingtoninstitute.org/policy-analysis/palestinians-and-two-state-solution-hard-data-hardest-questions)(Instead, the majority advocated regaining all of historic Palestine. Further, 58% in the West Bank and 62% in Gaza said that even if a two-state solution is reached, conflict with Israel should continue until the Palestinians regain all territory.) if a two state solution is agreed upon; this is likely to stymie a willingness from Israel to co-operate.
1.1.6.3.5. Pro: The UAE sees a two state solution as the [best outcome](https://www.thenationalnews.com/mena/2021/07/29/uae-two-state-solution-is-the-only-answer-to-situation-in-palestinian-territories/) for the region.
1.1.6.3.5.1. Con: The UAE recently forged a peace deal with Israel; it lost the capacity to advocate with and for Palestine at this stage as the PA feels [betrayed](https://www.aljazeera.com/economy/2021/5/28/profits-or-palestine-uae-israel-deals-likely-to-continue-quietly)(“MBZ seems to be looking to demonstrate that his now-tarnished relationship with Israel has some redeeming value beyond the purely commercial. With much of the world outraged over Israeli behaviour, the UAE’s diplomatic concession is looking foolish,” Jim Krane, a research fellow at Rice University’s Baker Institute and the author of Dubai: The Story of the World’s Fastest City, told Al Jazeera.\n\n“Now that Abu Dhabi has formal ties with Israel, it finds itself with less leverage with the Israelis and no credibility among Palestinians,” Krane added.\n\nWhile the UAE is under pressure from other Arab nations to show support for Palestinian rights, it seems unlikely to cancel any deals with Israel to do so, Krane said.).
1.1.6.3.5.2. Pro: The UAE may make this more politically feasible as it has recently forged [stronger political ties](https://www.bbc.co.uk/news/world-middle-east-54151712) with Israel.
1.1.6.4. Pro: Leaders of Arab parties in the Knesset, as of 2021, [support](https://www.vox.com/policy-and-politics/22442052/israel-palestine-two-state-solution-gaza-hamas-one)(Ayman Odeh and Mansour Abbas, the leaders of the major Arab factions in Israel’s Knesset, its parliament, are both two-staters.) a two state solution.
1.2. Pro: Recognition of a Palestinian state may end the [destabilising](https://www.studentisraelity.com/post/the-deterioration-of-quality-of-life-in-the-palestinian-territories) Israeli [occupation](https://www.politico.com/magazine/story/2016/06/israel-palestine-occupation-violence-213957/).
1.2.1. Con: Palestinian territories are not occupied but [disputed territories](http://www.webcitation.org/6Vo9QW33E?url=http://mfa.gov.il/MFA/ForeignPolicy/FAQ/Pages/FAQ_Peace_process_with_Palestinians_Dec_2009.aspx).
1.2.1.1. Pro: [Occupied territories](http://mfa.gov.il/MFA/MFA-Archive/2003/Pages/DISPUTED%20TERRITORIES-%20Forgotten%20Facts%20About%20the%20We.aspx) are territories captured in war from an established and recognized sovereign nation. Israeli presence in the West Bank does not meet this criterion.
1.2.1.1.1. Con: The argument that the lack of a previous sovereign invalidates the description of the status quo as an occupation is known as the "[missing reversioner thesis](http://www.jurist.org/forum/2010/04/us-israel-standoff-over-settlements.php)." It is neither consistent with legal opinion nor accepted by the international community.
1.2.1.1.2. Pro: None of the armistice agreements after the 1948 war created political borders; this task was supposed to be taken care of by later negotiations. As such, the current borders are illegitimate.
1.2.1.1.2.1. Pro: The boundaries marked by the [1949 Armistice Agreement](http://www.jewishvirtuallibrary.org/israel-egypt-armistice-agreement-1949) signed by Israel and Egypt after the 1948 war were [simply indicative](https://www.jewishvirtuallibrary.org/israel-egypt-armistice-agreement-1949)(No provision of this Agreement shall in any way prejudice the rights, claims and positions of either Party hereto in the ultimate peaceful settlement of the Palestine question) of where the Egyptian and Israeli armies were. This left the territories up for negotiation.
1.2.1.1.2.2. Pro: The [Jordanian annexation of the West Bank](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jordanian_annexation_of_the_West_Bank) after the 1948 war was not recognized by the international community. Thus, the West Bank never belonged to a sovereign state and, therefore, cannot be said to be occupied.
1.2.1.1.3. Con: The occupation was the result of Israel's "[war of aggression and conquest](https://theintercept.com/2017/06/05/a-50-year-occupation-israels-six-day-war-started-with-a-lie/)" and not, as oftentimes argued, of a preventive and legitimate war for the purpose of self-defense.
1.2.1.1.3.1. Pro: Israel [attempted](http://www.haaretz.com/israel-news/1.783429) to actively conceal laws that it had passed to effectively take over East Jerusalem; the Israeli Foreign Ministry told its ambassadors to refer to the annexation as "municipal fusion."
1.2.1.1.3.2. Con: Israel intended to return land to Jordan, in exchange for peace, as indicated by [Resolution 242](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council_Resolution_242). This demonstrates that the objective of the Six-Day War was not territorial acquisition.
1.2.1.1.3.2.1. Con: If Israel wanted to only attack Egypt and not capture any territory in Palestine, it could have given the captured territories back to Jordan after the war. By keeping these territories, Israel showed that capturing them was a desired end.
1.2.1.1.3.2.2. Con: Israel has since made peace with [Egypt](https://www.history.com/this-day-in-history/israel-egyptian-peace-agreement-signed) and [Jordan](https://www.brookings.edu/blog/order-from-chaos/2019/10/23/25-years-on-remembering-the-path-to-peace-for-jordan-and-israel/) but has still not given back the territory of Palestine.
1.2.1.1.3.2.3. Pro: Jordan, Egypt, and Syria refused to meet with Israel after the war, making peace impossible. This stopped negotiation during the [Khartoum Resolution](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Khartoum_Resolution).
1.2.1.1.3.2.4. Pro: The government of Israel attempted by all means necessary to avoid any war with Jordan.
1.2.1.1.3.2.4.1. Con: In 1966, after a Palestinian land mine attack inside its territory, Israel conducted [military reprisal operations](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Samu_incident) on a large scale on Jordan-controlled territory.
1.2.1.1.3.2.4.1.1. Pro: UN Security Council [Resolution 228](https://undocs.org/S/RES/228\(1966\)) classified Israel's actions as a violation of the Armistice Agreement between Jordan and Israel.
1.2.1.1.3.2.4.1.2. Con: The [Samu incident](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Samu_Incident) was a legitimate reprisal operation against the Arabs planting mines in Jordan, which killed 3 Israeli soldiers.
1.2.1.1.3.2.4.1.3. Pro: The King of Jordan had previously [told](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Samu_incident#Background) high-ranking Israeli government officials that he could not "absorb a serious retaliatory raid" by Israel. That Israeli raid, the Samu incident, is considered to be one of the aggravating factors that led to the Six-Day War.
1.2.1.1.3.2.4.2. Pro: Israel had issued a [strict order](https://www.washingtoninstitute.org/policy-analysis/view/the-six-day-war-and-its-enduring-legacy) that there was to be no shooting at the Jordanians. Israel did not want to open up a second front along its longest border.
1.2.1.1.3.2.4.3. Pro: [Levi Eshkol](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Levi_Eshkol#Six-Day_War) the Prime Minister at the time attempted, by all means, to avoid attacking Jordan.
1.2.1.1.3.2.4.3.1. Pro: Shortly after dealing with the Egyptian forces, the Israeli PM requested King Hussein not to enter the war through their shared [UN contact](https://www.bbc.com/news/world-middle-east-39960461) to protect Jordan. However, a couple of hours later, Jordan began shelling civilian infrastructure in Jerusalem. Following extensive attacks from Jordan, [Israel](https://uk.reuters.com/article/uk-israel-palestinians-1967-factbox/factbox-israel-swept-to-victory-in-6-days-40-years-ago-idUKL3030253620070606) [decided](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Six-Day_War#West_Bank) to [retaliate](https://www.aljazeera.com/news/2009/7/13/1967-arab-israeli-war-timeline).
1.2.1.1.3.3. Pro: Israel [refused](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_Nations_Emergency_Force#UNEF_I) to have UN peacekeeping forces stationed on its side of the border with Egypt to deescalate the conflict; Egypt had similar UN regiments stationed on its border from 1948 to 1967. Thus, Israel had the means to deescalate the conflict but actively decided against it.
1.2.1.1.3.4. Con: Many believe that Israel acted in self-defense in the Six-Day War.
1.2.1.1.3.4.1. Pro: Before Israel struck the Arab forces, it was surrounded by approximately 250,000 troops, more than two thousand tanks, and seven hundred aircraft \([p. 51](http://www.jewishvirtuallibrary.org/jsource/images/mf2017.pdf#page=43)\). The Israeli army could not indefinitely remain fully mobilised; it had [no choice](https://www.e-ir.info/2014/03/16/pre-emption-and-israeli-decision-making-in-1967-and-1973/) but to attack.
1.2.1.1.3.4.1.1. Pro: Israel would not have had [time](http://www.e-ir.info/2014/03/16/pre-emption-and-israeli-decision-making-in-1967-and-1973/) to mobilise its reserve troops in case of a surprise attack, reducing its ability to defend itself against a first strike by the Arab nations.
1.2.1.1.3.4.1.2. Con: The CIA assessed that Mossad's claim about being outgunned by the Arab nations was a deliberate attempt to influence the US into providing support for Israel and placing more pressure on the Egyptian President Nasser \([p. 5](https://www.cia.gov/static/d5a4d18e0fecdc17091a38eaea78e8e2/Analysis-Arab-Israeli-War.pdf)\).
1.2.1.1.3.4.1.3. Pro: There was a significant amount of Arab aggression in the region from [Syria](http://www.sixdaywar.co.uk/timeline.htm)(Feb 22nd 1967\n\nPresident Attassi of Syria: “it is the duty of all of us now to move from defensive positions to offensive positions and enter the battle to liberate the usurped land…Everyone must face the test and enter the battle to the end.”), [Iraq](http://www.sixdaywar.org/content/threats.asp)("The existence of Israel is an error which must be rectified. This is our opportunity to wipe out the ignominy which has been with us since 1948. Our goal is clear – to wipe Israel off the map. We shall, God willing, meet in Tel Aviv and Haifa."), and [Palestinian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_attacks_against_Israeli_civilians_before_1967) [fedayeen](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palestinian_fedayeen), forcing Israel's hand prior to the Six-Day War.
1.2.1.1.3.4.2. Con: While a defensive war to destroy enemy military capabilities might have been necessary, there was no need to continue occupying the land after the war.
1.2.1.1.3.4.3. Pro: The only nation to be pre-emptively struck was [Egypt](https://www.aljazeera.com/news/2009/7/13/1967-arab-israeli-war-timeline), which had moved their most threatening army to the Israeli border. Nations that controlled Palestine were not targeted.
1.2.1.1.3.4.4. Pro: The government of Israel believed that the Six Day War was one of [self-defense](https://mfa.gov.il/MFA/ForeignPolicy/FAQ/Pages/FAQ_Peace_process_with_Palestinians_Dec_2009.aspx#Settlements1).
1.2.1.1.3.4.4.1. Pro: It was only after [Jordan had blocked off Jerusalem's roads](https://thejewishnews.com/2017/05/31/jordan-not-attacked-israel-1967/) and cut off their access to water that Israel responded and captured the city.
1.2.1.1.3.4.4.1.1. Pro: Israel tried to [keep Jordan out](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Origins_of_the_Six-Day_War#Jordan_joins_Egypt) of the war with Egypt to avoid fighting a two-front war.
1.2.1.1.3.4.4.1.1.1. Con: Fighting a two-front war would have split Israeli forces, weakening them.
1.2.1.1.3.4.4.1.2. Con: Jordan was bound by a [mutual defense treaty](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Origins_of_the_Six-Day_War#Jordan_joins_Egypt) with Egypt and as such was obliged to act when Israel attacked Egypt. The war over the West Bank was, therefore, not a defensive one for Israel.
1.2.1.1.3.4.4.2. Con: Both Israeli and US intelligence believed that the chances of Nasser striking first were [slim](https://www.nytimes.com/2017/06/07/opinion/how-the-kgb-started-the-war-that-changed-the-middle-east.html).
1.2.1.1.3.4.4.2.1. Con: Nasser [sent](https://history.state.gov/milestones/1961-1968/arab-israeli-war-1967) large numbers of troops to the Sinai Peninsula, threatened to destroy Israel, and called for preparations for the "[final battle in Palestine](http://www.sixdaywar.org/content/threats.asp)." These acts clearly indicated that he was about to wage war with Israel.
1.2.1.1.3.4.4.2.2. Con: Egypt had [closed](https://israeled.org/nasser-closes-straits-of-tiran/) the Straits of Tiran, blocking Israel's only supply route with Asia and stopping its main supply of oil from Iran, placing incredible pressure on Israel.
1.2.1.1.3.4.4.2.3. Pro: Michael B Oren, the former ambassador of Israel to the US, has [stated](http://globetrotter.berkeley.edu/people5/Oren/oren-con4.html) that Nasser did not want bloodshed in 1967.
1.2.1.1.3.4.4.2.4. Pro: Yitzhak Rabin, a General at the time of the Six-Day War and the future Prime Minister of Israel, [believed](https://avrammeitner.wordpress.com/general-rabin-does-not-think-that-nasser-wanted-war/) that Nasser did not want war.
1.2.1.1.3.4.4.3. Pro: The Israeli strike was considered, at the time and in the minutes of the Israeli government, as a preemptive strike within the context of a defensive war \([pp. 220-221](https://kar.kent.ac.uk/1547/1/Kurtulus.pdf)\).
1.2.1.1.4. Pro: Israel has withdrawn from [Sinai](https://www.nytimes.com/1982/04/26/world/israeli-completes-pullout-leaving-sinai-to-egypt.html) and [South Lebanon](https://www.theguardian.com/world/2000/may/24/israelandthepalestinians.lebanon), which were occupied during the Six-Day War, but not from the [West Bank](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/West_Bank), which it began occupying in 1948, when it was not under any sovereign state.
1.2.1.2. Pro: Similar territories are [recognised](http://www.jcpa.org/jl/vp470.htm) as disputed; yet, only the West Bank is designated as an occupation.
1.2.1.2.1. Pro: Kashmir, just like Palestine, was [disputed](https://www.bbc.com/news/10537286)(Even before India and Pakistan won their independence from Britain in August 1947, the area was hotly contested.) from its [very inception](https://theconversation.com/kashmir-conflict-is-not-just-a-border-dispute-between-india-and-pakistan-112824)(The Kashmir issue has caused tension and conflict in the Indian subcontinent since 1947, when independence from Britain created India and Pakistan as two sovereign states. Jammu and Kashmir – the full name of the princely Himalayan state, then ruled by Maharaja Hari Singh – acceded to India in 1947, seeking military support after tribal raids from Pakistan into the state’s territory. The two countries have fought three wars over the region since.). The conflict's origins overlap conceptually.
1.2.1.2.2. Con: The disputed status of Kashmir does not imply that India or Pakistan is not a state. Likewise, the disputed territories of the West Bank and Gaza are disputed between two states: Israel and Palestine.
1.2.1.2.3. Con: There are particular regions of Jammu and Kashmir that are referred to as "[Pakistan-occupied Kashmir](https://www.indiatoday.in/education-today/gk-current-affairs/story/pakistan-occupied-kashmir-pok-history-facts-1580398-2019-08-13)" and "[India-occupied Kashmir](https://www.e-ir.info/2014/05/20/indian-occupied-kashmir/)."
1.2.1.3. Con: Israeli occupation of Palestinian territories has been repeatedly acknowledged by [international](https://www.dfa.ie/travel/travel-advice/a-z-list-of-countries/israel-and-the-occupied-territories/) [institutions](https://www.icrc.org/en/where-we-work/middle-east/israel-and-occupied-territories), such as the UN, and the [international](https://www.oxfam.org/en/what-we-do/countries/occupied-palestinian-territory-and-israel) [community](https://ecfr.eu/special/mapping_palestinian_politics/opt/).
1.2.1.3.1. Pro: [UN Security Council Resolution 242](https://unispal.un.org/unispal.nsf/0/7d35e1f729df491c85256ee700686136) following the Six-Day War demanded the "withdrawal of Israel armed forces from territories occupied in the recent conflict." This implies that the territories were considered as occupied.
1.2.1.3.1.1. Con: Under [UN Security Council Resolution 242](https://unispal.un.org/unispal.nsf/0/7d35e1f729df491c85256ee700686136), Israel is only expected to withdraw "from territories," not from "the territories" or "all the territories" captured during the Six-Day War, as noted by the then-British Foreign Secretary [George Brown](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council_Resolution_242#The_negotiating_and_drafting_process)(It does not call for Israeli withdrawal from “the” territories recently occupied, nor does it use the word “all”.).
1.2.1.3.1.2. Pro: The guiding principle framing the text of the resolution in its preamble emphasizes "[the inadmissibility of the acquisition of territory by war](https://unispal.un.org/DPA/DPR/unispal.nsf/0/7D35E1F729DF491C85256EE700686136)". This principle is unequivocal and incompatible with the claim that a partial withdrawal by Israel was considered acceptable.
1.2.1.3.1.3. Pro: In response to the deliberate attempt to obfuscate the language of the resolution, the Indian delegate to the UNSC [remarked](https://unispal.un.org/DPA/DPR/unispal.nsf/0/9F5F09A80BB6878B0525672300565063) that an approved resolution would necessitate total withdrawal of Israeli forces from all the territories occupied by Israel since 5 June 1967. Several other UNSC members concurred emphatically.
1.2.1.3.1.3.1. Con: Regarding the issue of partial withdrawal, a US State Department [report](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council_Resolution_242#The_negotiating_and_drafting_process) concluded, "Support for the concept of total withdrawal was widespread in the Security Council, and it was only through intensive American efforts that a resolution was adopted which employed indefinite language in the withdrawal clause."
1.2.1.3.1.3.2. Pro: If the resolution was content with partial Israeli withdrawal from the occupied territories, they would have likely used phrases such as "some" or "at least some" of the occupied territories.
1.2.1.3.1.3.3. Con: The omission of the word "the" was [intended to be vague](https://yamm.finance/wiki/UNSC_Resolution_242.html)(There was much bickering over whether that resolution should say from "the" territories or from "all" territories. In the French version, which is equally authentic, it says withdrawal de territory, with de meaning "the." We wanted that to be left a little vague and subject to future negotiation because we thought the Israeli border along the West Bank could be "rationalized"; certain anomalies could easily be straightened out with some exchanges of territory, making a more sensible border for all parties. We also wanted to leave open demilitarization measures in the Sinai and the Golan Heights and take a fresh look at the old city of Jerusalem. But we never contemplated any significant grant of territory to Israel as a result of the June 1967 war. On that point we and the Israelis to this day remain sharply divided. This situation could lead to real trouble in the future.); any claim to the contrary, that anything is explicitly specified, cannot be true.
1.2.1.3.1.3.4. Con: Despite several UNSC members proposing that "territories" be revised as "all-territories", the [UN Security Council](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council_Resolution_242#Interpretations) decided to use the former term.
1.2.1.3.1.3.4.1. Pro: The original authors of the UN Security Council Resolution 242 did not intend for the phrase to mean "all" \([p. 4](http://www.acpr.org.il/pp/pp173-grief-E.pdf)(The notable omissions – which were not accidental – in regard to withdrawal are the words “the” or “all” and “the June 5, 1967 lines”. In other words, there is lacking a declaration requiring Israel to withdraw from “the” or “all the” territories occupied by it on and after June 5, 1967.)\).
1.2.1.3.2. Pro: UN Security Council Resolution 2334 explicitly [names](https://undocs.org/S/RES/2334\(2016\)) Israel as "the occupying power" and refers to "Palestinian territories occupied since 1967, including East Jerusalem."
1.2.1.3.3. Pro: The UN Security Council's established unequivocal principle of acquisition makes inadmissable the [acquisition of territory by war](https://unispal.un.org/DPA/DPR/unispal.nsf/0/7D35E1F729DF491C85256EE700686136) and leaves no room for dispute. Israel acquired Palestinian territories in 1967 by war and its claim to them is, therefore, illegitimate.
1.2.1.3.4. Con: There are a variety of contexts in which acquisition through war is [permissible](https://docs.house.gov/meetings/GO/GO06/20180717/108563/HHRG-115-GO06-Wstate-KontorovichE-20180717.pdf)(The U.N. Charter prohibits war for most purposes. When the use of force is illegal, it is natural to \nconclude that any territorial gains from such aggression cannot be recognized as well. Thus the \nillegality of conquest arises from the presumptive illegality of the use of force. But crucially, the \nU.N. Charter does not make all war illegal. Indeed, it expressly reaffirms the legality of a \ndefensive war. Since defensive war is not illegal, it follows that the defender’s territorial gains \nfrom such a war would not be illegal.), according to the UN charter \(p. 2\).
1.2.1.3.4.1. Pro: [Scholars](https://chicagounbound.uchicago.edu/cgi/viewcontent.cgi?article=1685&context=cjil)(Title by conquest remains a valid title in those cases in which the conquering State is not bound by the Charter of the United Nations . . . or when although when so bound, the resort to war on its part is not, in the particular case, unlawful.) have noted that, when engaging in a lawful war, [acquisition is allowed](https://chicagounbound.uchicago.edu/cgi/viewcontent.cgi?article=1685&context=cjil)(footnote 102).
1.2.1.3.4.2. Con: The [Declaration of Principles of International Law concerning Friendly Relations and Cooperation among States \(UNGA resolutions 1970\)](https://www.un.org/ga/search/view_doc.asp?symbol=A/RES/2625\(XXV\))(The territory of a State shall not be the object of acquisition by another State resulting from the threat or use of force. No territorial acquisition resulting from the threat or use of force shall be recognized as legal.) includes the unqualified prohibition of the acquisition of territory by threat or use of force.
1.2.1.3.5. Con: International law is not retroactive; thus, the events that occurred in 1967 cannot be interpreted in the light of laws instituted at a later time as is often done when Palestinian territories are designated as occupied \([p. 377](https://books.google.co.kr/books?id=GR4xDwAAQBAJ&printsec=frontcover&redir_esc=y#v=onepage&q&f=false)\).
1.2.1.4. Pro: According to the [views](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israeli-occupied_territories#Israeli_legal_and_political_views) of most adherents of Religious Zionism and to certain streams of Orthodox Judaism, "occupied territories" do not and cannot exist because all of the Land of Israel belongs to the Jews.
1.2.1.4.1. Pro: An extreme [position](https://www.huffingtonpost.com/rick-steves/settlements-in-the-west-b_b_3240616.html) held by many conservative Jews as well as conservative Christians is that the presence of Palestinians in the West Bank impedes God’s will.
1.2.1.4.2. Pro: [The Land of Israel](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Land_of_Israel) concept has been invoked by the founders of the State of Israel. It often surfaces in political debates on the status of the West Bank.
1.2.1.4.3. Con: The essence of Zionism is its support for an [independent Jewish state](https://www.annefrank.org/en/topics/antisemitism/are-all-jews-zionists/). As such, arguing that, because Zionists do not recognize Israeli occupation of Palestinine, the area is not occupied, is tautological.
1.2.1.5. Con: Disputed territories can still be under military [occupation](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Military_occupation). As long as Israel uses the military to [control](https://www.britannica.com/topic/military-government) an enemy's territory, Palestine can be considered occupied.
1.2.1.6. Con: In a 2004 ruling, the Supreme Court of Israel noted that Israel had held the West Bank "[in belligerent occupation](https://www.refworld.org/cases,ISR_SC,4374ac594.html)" since 1967.
1.2.2. Pro: Israeli occupation leads to significant harms for Palestinian people.
1.2.2.1. Pro: Severe [human rights violations](http://www.amnestyusa.org/our-work/countries/middle-east-and-north-africa/israel-and-occupied-palestinian-territories) occur under Israeli occupation.
1.2.2.1.1. Pro: Israel has been accused of [institutionalizing statelessness](https://academic.oup.com/ijrl/article-abstract/24/2/202/1538062/Institutionalizing-Statelessness-The-Revocation-of) in East Jerusalem. This violates the right to a nationality as enshrined in [Article 15](http://www.claiminghumanrights.org/udhr_article_15.html) of the Universal Declaration of Human Rights \(UDHR\).
1.2.2.1.1.1. Con: The [UDHR](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Universal_Declaration_of_Human_Rights) is not legally binding.
1.2.2.1.1.1.1. Con: Portions of the UDHR have [been incorporated](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Universal_Declaration_of_Human_Rights)(Although not legally binding, the contents of the UDHR have been elaborated and incorporated into subsequent international treaties, regional human rights instruments, and national constitutions and legal codes.) into international treaties, constitutions, and legal codes.
1.2.2.1.1.2. Con: Israel [offered citizenship](https://academic.oup.com/ijrl/article-abstract/24/2/202/1538062/Institutionalizing-Statelessness-The-Revocation-of)(pg.209) to East Jerusalemites in 1967 but Palestinians rejected it.
1.2.2.1.1.2.1. Con: About [60%](http://www.pcpsr.org/sites/default/files/Table%20of%20Findings_English%20Joint%20Poll%20Dec%202016_12Feb2017.pdf)(pg.10) of Palestinians and about [70%](http://www.peacepolls.org/peacepolls/documents/000571.pdf)(pg.4) of Israelis now oppose the idea of a joint state with equal rights for all citizens.
1.2.2.1.1.2.2. Con: Israel was founded in order to provide a safe haven to Jews, and its ability to fulfill this function is contingent on political control being maintained by Jews. A one-state solution would now threaten Jewish maintenance of political control.
1.2.2.1.1.2.2.1. Pro: If able to choose one among a democratic Israel, peace, a Greater Israel, and Israel with a Jewish majority, the [latter](http://www.pcpsr.org/sites/default/files/Table%20of%20Findings_English%20Joint%20Poll%20Dec%202016_12Feb2017.pdf)(pg.14) is the most popular option among Israeli Jews.
1.2.2.1.1.2.2.2. Con: The purpose for which Israel was founded has been fulfilled, and should no longer determine the political state of Israel. Jews no longer need a safe haven in the way they did back when Israel was established.
1.2.2.1.1.2.2.2.1. Con: Jews still need a safe haven. Anti-Semitism is [rising in Europe](http://www.independent.co.uk/news/world/europe/pope-francis-anti-semitism-european-jewish-congress-moshe-kantor-populism-donald-trump-hitler-a7544886.html) and hate crimes against Jews are [still frequent in the US](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Antisemitism_in_the_United_States#Hate_crimes_against_Jews_in_the_U.S.).
1.2.2.1.1.2.2.3. Pro: Israel would [never](http://www.timesofisrael.com/in-israel-the-demographic-issue-gains-resonance/) agree to granting citizenship to all Palestinians since that would threaten the ability of Israel to remain a politically Jewish state by [massively increasing](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palestinian_territories#Demographics) the number of Arab Israeli citizens.
1.2.2.1.1.2.2.3.1. Pro: There are currently more than three million Palestinian refugees registered with the UN in [Jordan](https://www.unrwa.org/where-we-work/jordan), [Lebanon](https://www.unrwa.org/where-we-work/lebanon) and [Syria](https://www.unrwa.org/where-we-work/syria). If only a fraction of those return, this will tip the population balance in favor of Arabs.
1.2.2.1.1.2.3. Pro: Many key rights could have been delivered to Palestinians if they had taken on Israeli citizenship.
1.2.2.1.1.2.3.1. Pro: Many Palestinians are [eligible for Israeli citizenship](http://www.timesofisrael.com/more-east-jerusalem-palestinians-seek-israeli-citizenship/)(Asking for an Israeli passport still carries the stigma of implied acceptance of Israeli control, and only about 15,000 Palestinians have requested one since 2003; of those, fewer than 6,000 were reportedly approved.), yet they remain stateless for [ideological reasons](https://www.al-monitor.com/originals/2020/05/palestinians-jerusalem-israel-citizenship-pa-hamas-turkey.html).
1.2.2.1.1.2.3.2. Con: Israeli citizenship applies [only](https://www.al-monitor.com/originals/2022/01/palestinians-seek-israeli-citizenship-jerusalem) to Palestinians living in East Jerusalem, not the millions living in the rest of the occupied territories.
1.2.2.1.1.2.3.3. Con: Making Israeli citizenship the only means through which Palestinians can access rights coerces them into accepting citizenship in a nation that has repeatedly committed atrocities against them. This is reprehensible.
1.2.2.1.1.2.3.4. Con: There are [discriminatory laws](https://abcnews.go.com/International/uprisings-palestinians-israeli-citizenship/story?id=77741627) in place within Israel that afford particular rights only to Jewish citizens; this means that key rights may not be delivered.
1.2.2.1.1.3. Pro: The "center of life" policy was introduced to asses the [residency rights](https://oldwebsite.palestine-studies.org/jq/fulltext/78495)(Whether studying or working abroad or simply living in a nearby suburb outside Jerusalem’s municipal boundaries due to the housing squeeze in East Jerusalem, Israel has revoked the permanent residency rights of these Palestinians – 0.5% of the Arab population of the city – on the allegation that their “center of life” is no longer in Jerusalem. The arbitrary standard on which this policy is based exceeds the bounds of Israel’s written law and violates international law. The reality in Jerusalem – a result of the “center of life” policy – is the institutionalization of statelessness and forced displacement of thousands of Palestinian East Jerusalemites.) of individual Palestinians. This policy requires a high burden of proof to continue living in East Jerusalem and is biased such that it disproportionately strips Palestinians of their residency rights.
1.2.2.1.1.3.1. Pro: Children born to Palestinians in East Jerusalem do not automatically receive residence rights but must apply for it in a [procedure](https://academic.oup.com/ijrl/article-abstract/24/2/202/1538062/Institutionalizing-Statelessness-The-Revocation-of)(pg.217) that is highly uncertain. If rejected, the children are stateless.
1.2.2.1.1.4. Pro: It has been proposed by Israeli leaders that [naturalization](https://academic.oup.com/ijrl/article/24/2/202/1538062)(click on "PDF" to download:\np. 220) as a tool to secure permanent residency should require East Jerusalemites to [take an oath](https://www.reuters.com/article/us-israel-palestinians-jerusalem-insight-idUSKCN0Q81HP20150803) to Israel as a Jewish and democratic state. This is institutionalized racism as Jewish immigrants do not need to take a similar oath.
1.2.2.1.1.5. Pro: The [Convention on the Reduction of Statelessness](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Convention_on_the_Reduction_of_Statelessness) commits signatory states to reduce the incidence of statelessness. Israel has signed this multilateral treaty.
1.2.2.1.2. Pro: Israel's policies in the West Bank are analogous to the [crime of apartheid](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Crime_of_apartheid#ICC_definition_of_the_crime_of_apartheid) as defined by the Rome Statute, which includes crimes such as "deportation or forcible transportation of population."
1.2.2.1.2.1. Pro: A [UN report](https://unispal.un.org/DPA/DPR/unispal.nsf/0/71A1FD027B82B40D852580EA0064468F) has accused Israel of mass evictions and forced relocation of Palestinians in the Zone C areas of the West Bank.
1.2.2.1.2.1.1. Pro: Israeli authorities have been accused of [acquiring grazing land](https://english.palinfo.com/news/2017/03/15/Permitted-for-Israeli-settlers-prohibited-for-Palestinians) in the Jordan Valley under the pretenses of protecting the wildlife, then distributing it to settlers or using it for military exercises.
1.2.2.1.2.2. Pro: Israel's oppressive tactics in the West Bank qualify as an "[institutionalised regime of systematic oppression](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Crime_of_apartheid#ICC_definition_of_the_crime_of_apartheid) and domination by one racial group \(Jews\) over any other racial group \(Palestinians\) committed with the intention of maintaining that regime."
1.2.2.1.2.2.1. Pro: Israeli settlers in the West Bank are subject to civil law, while Palestinians are subject to [harsh military orders](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israeli_Military_Order).
1.2.2.1.2.2.2. Pro: Israeli extremists often [do not receive punishment](https://www.theguardian.com/world/2021/jun/24/amnesty-catalogue-of-violations-by-israeli-police-against-palestinians)(At least 2,150 people – 90% of them Palestinian – have been arrested, most for allegedly insulting or assaulting a police officer or taking part in an illegal gathering rather than for violent offences, while rightwing Jewish extremists have for the most part continued to organise freely.\n\nOn at least two occasions in Haifa and Nazareth, witness accounts and verified videos showed police attacking groups of unarmed protesters without provocation, Amnesty reported.) for violence, whilst their Palestinian counterparts are treated harshly by the police.
1.2.2.1.2.2.3. Pro: [Naftali Bennett](https://apnews.com/article/naftali-bennett-israel-middle-east-religion-technology-20678c93611da0fee71fbccac80759d5), the Israeli Prime Minister \(2021-\), [directly supports](https://www.aljazeera.com/opinions/2021/7/22/why-it-is-crucial-to-keep-a-spot-light-on-israels-apartheid)(Indeed, Bennett has always been open about his desire to officially annex occupied Palestinian territories and rid Palestinians of any rights they have in Israel. And unlike his predecessor Benjamin Netanyahu, who maintained that he believed in “two states for two peoples” while pursuing apartheid policies, he has never been interested in even appearing to support the two-state solution. As Yousef Munayyer, a nonresident senior fellow at the Arab Center, recently argued in an op-ed for the Washington Post, “Bennett unabashedly embraces apartheid, while Netanyahu at least understood the value of pretending otherwise before the international community.”) the disempowerment of Palestinians, and the centrality of Jewishness to Israeli law.
1.2.2.1.2.3. Pro: Israeli security forces have carried out extra-judicial killings of Palestinians, even when they no longer pose any threat.

Con: The Palestinian Authority is associated with [extra-judicial killings](https://www.theguardian.com/world/2021/jun/24/amnesty-catalogue-of-violations-by-israeli-police-against-palestinians)(On Thursday news emerged that Nizar Banat, a well-known critic of the PA, died during an arrest by Palestinian security forces in the city of Hebron. A large demonstration in Ramallah in response to his death, calling for PA officials to resign, was met with teargas and use of metal batons from Palestinian security forces.\n\nBanat, who had planned to run in cancelled parliamentary elections this year, had called on western countries to cut off aid to the PA because of growing human rights violations and endemic corruption.\n\nLast month, gunmen he claimed were loyal to the PA president, Mahmoud Abbas, attacked his house with bullets, stun grenades and teargas while his wife and children were inside.), and policing abuses in reponse to protests.
1.2.2.1.2.4. Pro: Those who have experienced Apartheid in the past have said that Israel's conduct in the West Bank is similar to Apartheid.
1.2.2.1.2.4.1. Pro: [34 South African activists](https://mronline.org/2008/05/19/apartheid190508-html/), including government ministers, published an open letter saying, "We fought apartheid; we see no reason to celebrate it in Israel now!"

1.2.2.1.2.5. Con: Unlike the apartheid that occurred in South Africa, the West Bank is nominally self-governed by Palestinians, giving them some degrees of freedom [absent from South Africa](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel_and_the_apartheid_analogy)(Opponents of the analogy reject the comparison of Israel's occupation of the West Bank and Gaza Strip with apartheid South Africa, arguing that as the two territories are not part of sovereign Israel and governed by the Palestinian Authority and Hamas government in Gaza, they cannot be compared to the internal policies of apartheid South Africa.) under apartheid.
1.2.2.1.2.6. Con: Israel's mistreatment of Palestinians in the West Bank is predicated on the need for self defence, rather than the domination of one racial group over another.
1.2.2.1.2.6.1. Con: Under international law, claims to self-defense are required to be [proportional](https://www.open.edu/openlearn/society-politics-law/the-use-force-international-law/content-section-1.3.1)(Furthermore, the ICJ held in the Nicaragua Case \(Merits\) that ‘self-defence would warrant only measures which are proportional to the armed attack and necessary to respond to it’ \(para. 176\). This statement sets out two important principles in international law concerning the use of force: the principle of proportionality and the principle of necessity. In this context, proportionality means that the response to an armed attack must be reflective of the scope, nature and gravity of the attack itself. On the other hand, the principle of necessity guards against the use of measures which are excessive and not necessary in response to an armed attack.), which Israeli retaliations to Palestinian attacks are [not](https://www.bbc.co.uk/news/world-middle-east-44167900).
1.2.2.1.2.6.1.1. Pro: The sophisticated [Iron Dome](https://www.nytimes.com/article/israel-gaza-what-we-know.html?action=click&module=RelatedLinks&pgtype=Article)(The Iron Dome missile defense system became operational in 2011 and got its biggest first test over eight days in November 2014, when Gaza militants fired some 1,500 rockets aimed at Israel.\n\nWhile Israeli officials claimed a success rate of up to 90 percent during that conflict, outside experts were skeptical. The system’s interceptors — just 6 inches wide and 10 feet long — rely on miniature sensors and onboard computer processors to zero in on short-range rockets.\n\nIsrael has suffered casualties and the psychological terror of incoming rockets, but the system is clearly winnowing out much of the daily rocket fire.) deters the vast majority of Hamas' attacks.
1.2.2.1.2.7. Con: Major geopolitical players, like the USA, [do not recognise](https://www.aljazeera.com/opinions/2021/7/22/why-it-is-crucial-to-keep-a-spot-light-on-israels-apartheid)(. After the publication of the damning HRW report, for example, a spokesperson for the US State Department simply said: “It is not the view of \[the Biden\] administration that Israel’s actions constitute apartheid.”) that apartheid is ongoing in the region.

The occupation does not deprive Palestinians of important resources, but rather Hamas does.

1.2.2.1.4. Con: Israel's human rights violations should not be used as an argument in favor of recognising Palestine as their governments do not have a better track record.

Pro: A [Human Rights Watch report](https://www.hrw.org/report/2018/10/23/two-authorities-one-way-zero-dissent/arbitrary-arrest-and-torture-under) in 2018 showed that [arbitrary arrests](https://www.france24.com/en/20190913-reporters-hamas-fatah-brothers-war-palestinine-west-bank-gaza-israel), intimidation and even torture by Fatah and Hamas are commonplace, both in Gaza and the West Bank.
1.2.2.1.4.5.1. Pro: Hamas has [beaten and arrested](https://www.amnesty.org/en/latest/news/2019/03/gaza-hamas-must-end-brutal-crackdown-against-protesters-and-rights-defenders) peaceful protesters and rights defenders.
1.2.2.1.4.5.2. Pro: The military branch of Hamas [tortured and killed](https://www.amnesty.org/en/latest/news/2015/05/gaza-palestinians-tortured-summarily-killed-by-hamas-forces-during-2014-conflict/) numerous Palestinians during the 2014 outbreak of conflict.
1.2.2.1.4.6. Con: If recognising Palestine leads to fewer Israeli human rights abuses, then that is [good on net](https://www.bbc.co.uk/ethics/introduction/consequentialism_1.shtml).
1.2.2.1.4.6.1. Pro: Israeli human rights abuses are [facilitated](https://www.amnesty.org/en/countries/middle-east-and-north-africa/israel-and-occupied-palestinian-territories/report-israel-and-occupied-palestinian-territories/) by the ongoing occupation of Palestine; if Palestine was seen as a legitimate state, then these would be less likely.
1.2.2.1.4.7. Con: If Palestine is a legitimate state, then it is easier to hold to account as the US can insist on free and fair elections and political accountability.
1.2.2.1.4.7.1. Pro: Palestine would no longer be able to [blame](https://carnegieeurope.eu/2021/04/23/halting-palestine-s-democratic-decline-pub-84383)(There are also many other potential spoilers of the elections, including Israel, which is already trying to deter voting in annexed East Jerusalem by carrying out arrests—thereby providing a good cover for Abbas to postpone the contests, as seems increasingly likely.) a lack of democracy on Israel if it is recognised as a state, and has its borders respected.
1.2.2.1.4.7.2. Pro: Abbas may no longer find it necessary to [cement](https://carnegieeurope.eu/2021/04/23/halting-palestine-s-democratic-decline-pub-84383)(Democratic advances, including elections, would give the Palestinian leadership a more coherent, credible voice. That could be useful in negotiating with Israel and the international community, offering some way out of the political deadlock. The peace process is moribund, primarily due to Israeli policy, particularly settlement expansion in the West Bank and the closure of Gaza. But some responsibility also lies with Abbas, who has deliberately weakened Palestinian national unity to protect his own position, notably by refusing to reconcile with Hamas.) his own political position at the cost of democracy, if Palestine achieves state recognition from the US.
1.2.2.1.4.7.3. Pro: One current [roadblock](http://www.xinhuanet.com/english/2021-04/05/c_139860071.htm) to elections is Israel's intervention in East Jerusalem. If the US recognises Palestine, this may be less feasible for Israel to sustain.
1.2.2.1.4.7.4. Con: US involvement in democracy is rarely successful; this can be seen through the loss of democratic norms in [Afghanistan](https://thediplomat.com/2019/10/is-democracy-dying-in-afghanistan/).
1.2.2.1.4.7.5. Con: Roadblocks such as [Republican support](https://thehill.com/policy/national-security/554120-republican-resolution-supporting-israel-signals-growing-divide-with)(The resolution is led by Sen. Rick Scott \(R-Fla.\), and signed by 19 other GOP lawmakers reinforcing U.S. support for Israel to defend itself by “whatever means necessary.” It also condemns Hamas as an Iranian-backed terrorist organization responsible for the loss of innocent lives. \n\nThe U.S. designated Hamas a terrorist organization in 1997. \n\nThe resolution signals the growing divide between Republicans and Democrats in Congress on the relationship between U.S. and Israel that historically garners bipartisan support, but that has fractured in recent years over Democrats' opposition to the policies of Prime Minister Benjamin Netanyahu related to the Palestinians and Iranians.) for Israel, and President Biden's new [dovish disposition](https://www.fpri.org/article/2020/11/in-search-of-the-biden-doctrine/)(Since 2003, Biden has been generally skeptical about the use for force. He opposed the surge of troops in Iraq in 2006-2007, the surge in Afghanistan in 2009, and the Libyan War in 2011. He raised doubts about the raid to kill Osama Bin Laden in 2011, as well as the decision to draw a red line against the use of chemical weapons in Syria. Biden did back the campaign against ISIS and favored the escalation of drone warfare, but he criticized Trump’s decision to kill Iranian General Qasem Soleimani.\n\nHave we finally found Biden’s true nature? Perhaps—but again, his dovish turn is bound up with the wider “Iraq syndrome” in American society, where even Donald Trump and the Republican Party rail against forever wars. Biden is no kite in the wind, however. As vice president, he was consistently more dovish than Obama—on Afghanistan, on Bin Laden, on Syria, and on Libya \(an intervention that Obama later called his biggest mistake\).) may limit the application of political pressure on Palestine to act democratically.
1.2.2.1.4.7.6. Con: Democracy [may not](https://scholars.org/contribution/why-democracy-does-not-always-improve-human-rights)(In a democracy, ordinary citizens who themselves feel threatened may be less likely to hold the government accountable for human rights violations. For example, preliminary survey research suggests that Americans are more accepting of government torture when it is directed at an individual with an Arabic name.) lead to a reduction in human rights abuses.
1.2.2.1.5. Pro: Freedom of movement is often restricted for Palestinians.
1.2.2.1.5.1. Pro: Israel's numerous [controls, checkpoints and 'closed roads'](https://www.btselem.org/freedom_of_movement/checkpoints_and_forbidden_roads) within the West Bank are [in breach of Article 13](http://www.claiminghumanrights.org/udhr_article_13.html#at14) of the UN Declaration of Human Rights, which states that individuals ought to have freedom of movement within the borders and a right to leave.
1.2.2.1.5.1.1. Pro: The large wall running through parts of the West Bank, known as the 'separation barrier', has been [claimed by Human Rights Watch](https://www.hrw.org/news/2004/02/22/israel-west-bank-barrier-violates-human-rights) to be an illegal impediment to Palestinians' movement.
1.2.2.1.5.1.2. Pro: Palestinians are denied entry to Israeli settlements and [are violently prohibited](http://www.btselem.org/topic/settler_violence) from inhabiting these areas, constituting a breach of [Article 13](https://www.nichibenren.or.jp/library/ja/kokusai/humanrights_library/treaty/data/HRC_GC_27e.pdf)(pg.9), which explicitly forbids restrictions predicated on race and religion.
1.2.2.1.5.1.3. Con: These checkpoints are necessary to ensure the safety of civilians living in Israel, and are thus legal under [Article 12](http://www.claiminghumanrights.org/freedom_movement_definition.html) of the International Covenant on Civil and Political Rights.
1.2.2.1.5.1.3.1. Con: It is unjust to make innocent Palestinians suffer because of the threat a tiny proportion of them pose to Israel. This violates the [proportionality principle](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Proportionality_\(law\)) and is therefore illegal.
1.2.2.1.5.1.3.1.1. Pro: This sort of collective punishment is [illegal](http://www.crimesofwar.org/a-z-guide/collective-punishment/) under international law.
1.2.2.1.5.1.3.1.2. Pro: In [Hawara](http://www.haaretz.com/israel-news/.premium-1.740789), the Israeli Defense Force blocked all but one road into the town leading to massive problems because of some 'stone-throwers'.
1.2.2.1.5.1.3.1.3. Pro: Of the people who were killed by Israeli military forces or settlers in the West Bank during the past two years, [all were civilians](https://www.ochaopt.org/content/monthly-figures) as defined by the UN.
1.2.2.1.5.1.3.1.3.1. Con: The UN definition of a civilian is rather broad: they included [armed attackers](https://www.i24news.tv/en/news/israel/diplomacy-defense/135359-170117-west-bank-israeli-forces-kill-palestinian-who-tried-to-stab-soldier) who [tried to kill Israeli policemen](http://www.reuters.com/article/us-israel-palestinians-idUSKBN13X0O0) as civilians.
1.2.2.1.5.1.3.2. Pro: Checkpoints and blockades are necessary because violent attackers blend into civilian crowds. For example, a [bomb](http://www.haaretz.com/bomb-found-in-red-crescent-ambulance-1.49189) was found in an ambulance at the fifth checkpoint.
1.2.2.1.5.1.3.3. Con: There are many other means by which Israel can protect its national security and safeguard public order. The most obvious is to withdraw to its recognised borders and protecting the areas they encompass.
1.2.2.1.5.1.3.4. Pro: There were nearly [500](https://www.idfblog.com/2013/05/06/reality-check-the-truth-behind-crossings-in-judea-and-samaria/) attempts to smuggle weapons that checkpoints discovered.
1.2.2.1.5.1.4. Pro: Israel places blockades on [Route 60](https://www.theguardian.com/world/2005/oct/20/israel) - the main road connecting the northern and southern ends of Palestine. This causes harm to Palestinians \(e.g., [splitting](http://www.nytimes.com/2006/11/18/world/middleeast/18westbank.html) up their families, restricting access to jobs\) on a daily basis.
1.2.2.1.5.1.5. Con: The [number of checkpoints](http://www.aipac.org/-/media/publications/policy-and-politics/aipac-analyses/issue-memos/2009/10/aipac_memo_israeli_measures_in_west_bank_easing_palestinian_travel_boosting_economy.ashx) have reduced from 41 to 14. Despite terror threats, Israel aims to allow the maximum freedom of movement possible.
1.2.2.1.5.2. Con: Freedom of movement is [not an absolute right](https://www.ag.gov.au/rights-and-protections/human-rights-and-anti-discrimination/human-rights-scrutiny/public-sector-guidance-sheets/right-freedom-movement#can-the-right-to-freedom-of-movement-be-limited); restrictions can be imposed in national interest, such as to ensure national security. Thus, these restrictions do not ipso facto constitute a human rights violation.
1.2.2.1.5.3. Con: Freedom of movement is restricted in [some countries](https://freedomhouse.org/country/saudi-arabia/freedom-world/2021)(The government punishes activists and critics by limiting their ability to travel outside the country, and reform advocates are routinely stripped of their passports. Family members of activists can also be banned from travel.\n\nGender segregation restricts freedom of movement for both men and women, but male guardianship and other factors have historically imposed especially onerous constraints on women.) with recognized statehood. Thus, recognition does not guarantee that restrictions limiting freedom of movement will be lifted.
1.2.2.1.5.3.1. Pro: Strongly religious Muslim countries fare worse on [freedom indices](https://www.cato.org/sites/cato.org/files/2020-08/EDB_33_v3.pdf)(p. 1). Given the close association between [Islam and Palestine](https://www.history.com/news/why-jews-and-muslims-both-have-religious-claims-on-jerusalem), it is unlikely that Palestine will afford its citizens greater freedom.
1.2.2.1.5.4. Pro: Israel [denies passports](https://www.cfr.org/backgrounder/what-know-about-arab-citizens-israel)(After annexing East Jerusalem following the 1967 Six-Day War, Israel offered the hundreds of thousands of Palestinians living there Israeli citizenship. Most declined but were given permanent resident status. Today, roughly 90 percent of the 330,000 Palestinians in East Jerusalem hold this status, which allows them to live, work, and travel freely within Israel, as well as access its health insurance and social services. However, they do not get Israeli passports \(many have Jordanian ones\) and cannot vote in national elections.) to many Palestinians, including those with Israeli citizenship status; this prevents them from traveling freely. A lifting of the occupation would allow Palestinians to issue their own passports and travel around the world.
1.2.2.1.6. Pro: Palestinians suffered brutal suppression under Israel during the two [Intifadas](http://www.vox.com/cards/israel-palestine/intifadas).
1.2.2.1.6.1. Con: The second Intifada also [led to significant suffering for Israelis](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Second_Intifada), especially the civilian population that was frequently targeted by Palestinians.
1.2.2.1.6.2. Pro: Both the [First Intifada](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/First_Intifada#General_causes) and [Second Intifada](https://journals.lib.unb.ca/index.php/jcs/article/view/220/378) were direct results of Israeli occupation of the West Bank and the Gaza Strip. Recognizing Palestine might be a step toward preventing this from happening again.
1.2.2.1.6.2.1. Con: Support for a Third Intifada is only likely if other less violent mechanisms don't work. [Many Palestinians](http://www.pcpsr.org/en/node/676) support peaceful ways of resolving the conflict which means future violence is less likely.
1.2.2.1.6.2.2. Pro: The lack of progress in the conflict between Israel and Palestine could [cause](http://www.newyorker.com/news/news-desk/fear-of-a-third-intifada) a [Third Intifada](https://www.theguardian.com/world/2015/oct/05/third-palestinian-intifada-on-way-or-already-begun) as people are increasingly frustrated with the status quo.
1.2.2.1.6.2.3. Pro: -> See 1.1.4.4.3.
1.2.2.1.6.3. Pro: While the Intifadas were not peaceful, they were met with overwhelming [force from Israel](https://www.aljazeera.com/news/2020/9/28/palestinian-intifada-20-years-later-israeli-occupation-continues)(The first days of the uprising were characterised by large non-violent demonstrations that included civil disobedience and some stone-throwing. \[...\] During the first few days of the second Intifada, it is estimated Israeli soldiers fired about 1.3 million rounds of ammunition, as revealed by Amos Malka, then-director of Israeli military intelligence. This occurred despite the fact that violence by Palestinians in the early weeks was minimal.\n\n“The Israeli violence showed that the Israelis were not interested in a quick end to the conflict,” Abu Yusuf said. “The fact that Israel shot over a million bullets, caused great losses to Palestinian lives, and stepped over the Muslim holy places all shows that Israel wanted to militarise the Intifada. The excessive use of force that the Israeli army exercised was intended to drag the Palestinians into a military confrontation.”).
1.2.2.1.6.3.1. Con: Comparative death totals say little about the morality of the various sides in a conflict. For example, the most conservative estimates of WWII deaths place the [ratio](https://www.nationalww2museum.org/students-teachers/student-resources/research-starters/research-starters-worldwide-deaths-world-war) of German to American casualties at 16 to 1.
1.2.2.1.6.3.2. Con: Given its vastly superior military, Israel had the means to gain unilateral control over the disputed regions. Thus, Israel demonstrated moral restraint by not exercising this option.
1.2.2.1.6.3.2.1. Con: Israel’s restraint may have been motivated by fear of backlash from the international community to such an action.
1.2.2.1.6.3.2.2. Pro: Israel receives [substantial military assistance](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel%E2%80%93United_States_military_relations) from the US—more than any other country in the world. This military nexus significantly empowers Israel to use military force to achieve the desired outcomes.
1.2.2.1.6.3.3. Pro: The Intifadas led to significantly more [Palestinian](http://www.btselem.org/statistics/first_intifada_tables) than [Israeli](http://news.bbc.co.uk/1/hi/world/middle_east/3694350.stm) deaths, cementing the suppression of the former by the latter.
1.2.2.2. Con: Continued Israeli occupation of the West Bank prevents the authoritarian Islamist group Hamas from taking over the area.
1.2.2.2.1. Pro: Israeli [security forces](http://www.aipac.org/-/media/publications/policy-and-politics/aipac-analyses/issue-memos/2009/10/aipac_memo_israeli_measures_in_west_bank_easing_palestinian_travel_boosting_economy.ashx) are training their Palestinian peers to be more effective in fighting terror in Palestine.
1.2.2.2.2. Pro: -> See 1.1.2.4.2.1.
1.2.2.2.3. Con: The occupation of the West Bank fuels anti-Israel sentiment and [promotes](https://www.independent.co.uk/news/world/middle-east/hamas-gaza-abbas-ramallah-israel-b1853025.html)(“In this conflict Hamas projected itself as representing Palestinians in Jerusalem and the West Bank, not just Gaza. And to a large extent they succeeded. Many more people were carrying the green flag in Jerusalem and Ramallah. This hasn’t happened before with such clear expression of support.\n\n“People are saying, look, all these Arab and Muslim regimes and armies do nothing. But a small group with minimal means took the battle to Israel. It sends a message that we are alive, and we will not lose the spirit of resistance.) Hamas.
1.2.2.2.4. Con: Hamas has reclaimed Gazan land several times, [since 2007](https://www.nytimes.com/2021/05/21/world/middleeast/israel-gaza-war-ceasefire.html)(On three occasions since Hamas took full control of Gaza in 2007, Israel has launched major offensives aimed at degrading the group’s military capabilities, only to see Hamas rebuild and to achieve little success in actually changing the situation. This time, Prime Minister Benjamin Netanyahu vowed, would be different.\n\nArmed with extensive war plans, Israel’s military leaders methodically went down a list of targets, trying to inflict maximum damage on Hamas’s military abilities and its commanders. Yet, even now, the top echelons of the Israeli military acknowledge that their efforts may not prevent another round of fighting, perhaps even in the near future.), despite Israel's intervention. This indicates that efforts to disempower the group are quite ineffective.
1.2.2.3. Con: The security provided by Israeli forces in the West Bank allows for [foreign investment](http://www.aipac.org/-/media/publications/policy-and-politics/aipac-analyses/issue-memos/2009/10/aipac_memo_israeli_measures_in_west_bank_easing_palestinian_travel_boosting_economy.ashx) to pour into the area.
1.2.2.3.1. Con: [Foreign investment](https://pij.org/articles/535/israeli-impediments-to-investment-in-palestine) in businesses in Palestinian territories is limited because of Israeli policies that stifle the Palestinian economy.
1.2.2.3.2. Pro: When Israeli forces withdrew in 2005, their withdrawal was quickly followed by [a resurgence of violence](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israeli_disengagement_from_Gaza#Aftermath).
1.2.2.4. Con: Israel [continues](http://www.jewishvirtuallibrary.org/israel-s-quot-blockade-quot-of-gaza) to supply electricity and water to the Palestinian people, despite the fact that these facilities are often hit by rockets fired by Hamas.
1.2.2.4.1. Con: Gaza's only power plant was [destroyed](https://www.theguardian.com/world/2014/jul/29/gaza-power-plant-destroyed-israeli-airstrike-100-palestinians-dead) in one of Israel's most intense air strikes in the occupied territory.
1.2.2.5. Pro: Israeli occupation has a deleterious impact on the physical and mental health of Palestinians.
1.2.2.5.1. Pro: Israeli occupation limits Palestinians' access to health care.
1.2.2.5.1.1. Pro: The occupation has fragmented the West Bank into dozens of ‘islands’ separated by settlements, military zones and controlled roads. This restricts the ability of Palestinians to travel freely, thereby reducing or complicating access to health care \([p. 6](http://www.who.int/hac/crises/international/wbgs/opt_field_assessment_health_conditions_1april2015.pdf)\).
1.2.2.5.1.1.1. Pro: [Ambulances carrying patients](https://apps.who.int/gb/ebwha/pdf_files/WHA66/A66_INF1-en.pdf)(In 2011, only 5% of Palestinian Red Crescent ambulances in the West Bank were allowed to enter Jerusalem, 95% had to drop off patients at the barrier to be transferred to ambulances with Israeli licence plates \(back-to-back\). In 2012, only 9% of Palestinian ambulances were allowed to enter Jerusalem.) requiring care from hospitals in Jerusalem are often not permitted to enter Jerusalem \(p. 14\).
1.2.2.5.1.1.2. Pro: Construction of the Israeli West Bank Barrier [isolated](http://apps.who.int/gb/ebwha/pdf_files/WHA66/A66_INF1-en.pdf) many Palestinian communities from medical clinics \(p. 15\). In 2013, it was estimated that, once completed, more than 1.2 million Palestinians would be directly or indirectly affected.
1.2.2.5.1.2. Con: Palestinians have poor healthcare access because the Palestinian Authority has failed to allocate sufficient [budgets for medicines](https://www.ohchr.org/Documents/Issues/SForum/SForum2015/MahmoudDaher.pdf) \(p. 7\).
1.2.2.5.1.2.1. Con: The Palestinian Authority can only spend based on its tax income; as this is often [interrupted](http://www.sciencediplomacy.org/perspective/2013/health-challenges-in-palestine) by Israel, it is hard to plan.
1.2.2.5.1.2.2. Pro: The Ministry of Health is currently in debt to [pharmaceutical suppliers](https://www.ohchr.org/Documents/Issues/SForum/SForum2015/MahmoudDaher.pdf)(Current debt to pharmaceutical suppliers is NIS 270 million.) \(p. 7\).
1.2.2.5.1.2.3. Pro: In 2013, the [Palestinian Authority](https://www.sciencediplomacy.org/perspective/2013/health-challenges-in-palestine) cut its allocation for the Ministry of Health by 30 percent.
1.2.2.5.1.3. Pro: Israeli Defence Forces have deliberately attacked [health workers](https://www.amnesty.org/en/latest/news/2014/08/mounting-evidence-deliberate-attacks-gaza-health-workers-israeli-army/), [UNRWA Gaza shelters](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2014_Israeli_shelling_of_UNRWA_Gaza_shelters) and [hospitals](http://www.nbcnews.com/storyline/middle-east-unrest/another-gaza-hospital-hit-israeli-strike-four-dead-40-hurt-n161086). These attacks severely impair the ability of the Palestinian healthcare system to operate effectively.
1.2.2.5.1.4. Pro: Palestinians are [unable](http://www.bbc.co.uk/news/world-middle-east-20415675) to leave Gaza to seek health care treatment unavailable in Gaza, and medical supplies are unable to cross the border because of the blockade.
1.2.2.5.1.4.1. Pro: An inability to access healthcare outside of Gaza or to let supplies inside is likely to [overburden](https://apps.who.int/gb/ebwha/pdf_files/WHA66/A66_INF1-en.pdf)(pg.19) existing medical facilities.
1.2.2.5.1.5. Con: Projects by Israeli organizations help Palestinians to improve their medical training and business development.
1.2.2.5.1.5.1. Con: Charitable Israeli organizations can continue to improve Palestinian healthcare infrastructure, even in the absence of Israeli occupation.
1.2.2.5.1.5.2. Pro: The [Peres Center](https://www.peres-center.org/en/the-organization/projects/medicine/) has extended life-saving treatments to more than 12,000 Palestinian and Syrian children.
1.2.2.5.2. Pro: Israeli occupation has contributed to high rates of mental health issues amongst Palestinians \([p. 19](http://apps.who.int/gb/ebwha/pdf_files/WHA66/A66_INF1-en.pdf)\).
1.2.2.5.2.1. Pro: Following [Israel's attacks on Gaza](https://apps.who.int/gb/ebwha/pdf_files/WHA66/A66_INF1-en.pdf)(p. 19), there was a significant increase in the prevalence of those treated for "psychological shocks and post-conflict disorders," and almost half of them were children below the age of nine.
1.2.2.5.3. Pro: Recognizing Palestine would improve the work of the UN on the ground in the Palestinian territories.
1.2.2.5.3.1. Pro: Currently, UN organisations who work with Palestine can be penalised; this would no longer be the case if the US were to recognise Palestine.
1.2.2.5.3.1.1. Con: US recognition would not improve the work of UNESCO experts whom Israel does not allow to travel to sites in [Jerusalem](https://www.usatoday.com/story/news/world/2016/10/18/unesco-expected-adopt-controversial-jerusalem-resolution/92346718/).
1.2.2.5.3.1.2. Pro: [UNESCO](https://www.theguardian.com/world/2013/nov/08/us-unesco-voting-funds-palestine-decision) was penalised when the US withheld 22% of its budget due to the admission of Palestine as a voting member state.
1.2.2.5.3.2. Con: Even though Palestine is not a member of several UN organizations, they can still operate there. UNIDO, for example, runs several projects with regards to [food safety](https://www.unido.org/sites/default/files/files/2020-09/RAB-12054_SAFE_TE-2019_FINAL_NewNo.pdf)(p. xi) and regulations in the [marble stone](https://www.unido.org/fileadmin/user_media_upgrade/Resources/Evaluation/Palestine_TVET_Evaluation_Final_Report__.pdf) industry \(p. 12\).
1.2.2.5.4. Con: An analysis comparing different possible solutions to the Israel-Palestine conflict predicted that [withdrawal by Israel](https://www.rand.org/pubs/research_reports/RR740-1.html)(Unilateral withdrawal by Israel from the West Bank would impose large economic costs on Israelis unless the international community shoulders a substantial portion of the costs of relocating settlers. Intangible factors, such as each party's security and sovereignty aspirations, are critical considerations in understanding and resolving the impasse.
