[Studies](http://sciencemag.org/news/2000/10/jews-and-arabs-share-recent-ancestry) [show](https://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/12820706) [that](https://link.springer.com/article/10.1007%2Fs004390000426) both Jews and Palestinians Arabs share an important common ancestor of paternal descent that inhabited the region.
1.3.3.2.3. Con: Recognition of Palestine would prevent the right of return of Jews to their historic homeland.
1.3.3.2.3.1. Con: Replacing the rulers of territory does not imply that others would have to leave that territory. They would just not be in power anymore.
1.3.3.2.3.2. Con: Displaced Palestinians are [not free to return](https://jewishcurrents.org/teshuvah-a-jewish-case-for-palestinian-refugee-return/)(Opponents of Palestinian return have rejoinders to these documents. They argue that General Assembly Resolutions aren’t legally binding. They claim that since Israel was only created in May 1948, and Palestinian refugees were never its citizens, they would not be returning to “their country.” But these are legalisms devoid of moral content. In the decades since World War II, the international bodies that oversee refugees have developed a clear ethical principle: People who want to return home should be allowed to do so. Although the pace of repatriation has slowed in recent years, since 1990 almost nine times as many refugees have returned to their home countries as have been resettled in new ones. And as a 2019 report by the UN High Commissioner for Refugees \(UNHCR\) explains, resettlement is preferred only when a refugee’s home country is so dangerous that it “cannot provide them with appropriate protection and support.”) to Israel.
1.3.3.2.3.3. Pro: It is likely that recognition of Palestine would prevent Jews from visiting their holy sites in Palestine. This has [historical precedent](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Temple_Mount_entry_restrictions).
1.3.3.2.3.3.1. Pro: [Ongoing](https://www.bbc.co.uk/news/world-middle-east-34547523) [violence](https://www.bbc.co.uk/news/world-middle-east-13179865) against Jews, as well as [statements](http://www.algemeiner.com/2015/09/18/abbas-filthy-jews-feet-not-allowed-on-temple-mount/) by the Palestinian authorities indicate that Palestinians would severely restrict or prevent Jews from accessing their holy sites
1.3.3.2.3.3.2. Pro: For centuries, since the [Muslim conquest](https://archive.org/details/cityofstonehidde00benvrich/page/76) of Jerusalem \(638 A.D.\), Muslims [banned](https://archive.org/details/cityofstonehidde00benvrich/page/77) Jews from entering their holy places such as the Temple Mount.
1.3.3.2.3.3.3. Pro: The Cave of the Patriarchs is the [second holiest site](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cave_of_the_Patriarchs) for Jewish people; Muslims [banned Jewish people](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cave_of_the_Patriarchs#Mamluk_period) from the Cave for [700 years](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cave_of_the_Patriarchs#Israeli_control).
1.3.3.2.3.3.4. Con: Israeli authorities often [block](https://www.nationalgeographic.com/history/article/jerusalem-sacred-sites-combustible-mix-religion-politics) Palestinians from accessing important cultural sites.
1.3.3.2.3.3.4.1. Pro: Following violence on Temple Mount in 2019, [some commented](https://www.jpost.com/Arab-Israeli-Conflict/Police-prohibits-entrance-of-Jews-to-Temple-Mount-as-thousands-protest-598295)(“Israel bears full responsibility for storming al-Aqsa and fueling religious tensions in Jerusalem,” said PLO official Hanan Ashrawi. She attacked Israeli politicians, claiming that: “To score points in election season, Israeli politicians are competing as to who can exhibit higher levels of aggression and hostility against the Palestinian people during this important religious holiday.” She threatened that events could “plunge the region in sectarian war.”\nMK Ofer Cassif, a member of the Hadash-Ta’al list, accused Jewish visitors of “not seeking holiness, but rather incitement.\n“This incitement is not the result of a religious conflict, but a planned continuation of the rampage of occupation forces in east Jerusalem, which kidnap children, beat protesters, steal evidence and destroy homes,” he said.) that actions taken by Israeli officials could be constructed as incitement of violence.
1.3.3.3. Pro: In the past, Jews have been killed and expelled from the territory now known as Palestine. Recognizing Palestine could legitimize the atrocities carried out previously and jeopardise Israel.
1.3.3.3.1. Pro: [Spoliation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Antisemitism_in_the_Arab_world#Nineteenth_century) [and](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nebi_Musa_riots) [massacres](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1929_Hebron_massacre) of Jews in Israel-Palestine can be [traced](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1834_looting_of_Safed) to the 19th century Ottoman Empire and culminated to the complete Jordanian ethnic cleansing of half of Palestine.
1.3.3.3.1.1. Pro: Due to the prevention of any Jewish return to the region, Jewish people experienced gross atrocities with little capacity to escape.
1.3.3.3.1.1.1. Pro: In 1943, the leader of the Palestinian movement [stated](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Amin_al-Husseini#The_Holocaust)("It is the duty of Muhammadans... to drive all Jews from Arab and Muhammadan countries. Germany is also struggling against the common foe who oppressed Arabs and Muhammadans in their different countries. It has very clearly recognized the Jews for what they are and resolved to find a definitive solution for the Jewish danger that will eliminate the scourge that Jews represent in the world.") his support for the eradication of Jews.
1.3.3.3.1.1.2. Con: The Muslim rule at times didn't fully enforce the traditional [Dhimmi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_the_Jews_under_Muslim_rule#During_the_Caliphates) status of Jews and sometimes, as in eleventh-century Granada, they were not considered second class citizens.
1.3.3.3.1.1.2.1. Con: Relative equality for Jews in Granada ended in 1066 when Muslims [massacred](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1066_Granada_massacre) the Jewish community.
1.3.3.3.1.1.3. Pro: In the Arab World, [ethnic cleansing](https://www.jewishvirtuallibrary.org/the-treatment-of-jews-in-arab-islamic-countries) often happened to the Jewish Diaspora as Muslims stifled any right of return to Israel.
1.3.3.3.2. Con: It is not clear how recognising self-determination for Palestinians would legitimise historical violence and anti-Semitism.
1.3.3.4. Con: Violence against Israel is often motivated by continued occupation, rather than a lack of it. A condition of [ceasefires](https://www.bbc.co.uk/news/world-middle-east-28654229) is often the removal of Israeli troops.
1.3.3.4.1. Con: In 2006, Israel [withdrew](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israeli_disengagement_from_Gaza#Aftermath) from Gaza and part of West Bank, yet the government of Gaza began firing rockets the day after. Recognizing Palestine and withdrawing from the territory might spark similar violence.
1.3.3.4.2. Pro: Previous post-withdrawal violence came from Palestinian frustration that Israel's withdrawal [didn't allow them control](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israeli_disengagement_from_Gaza#Aftermath) over their borders, air space, or waters.
1.3.3.4.3. Con: An independent Palestine would likely [force the displacement](https://www.jpost.com/Middle-East/Abbas-wants-not-a-single-Israeli-in-future-Palestinian-state-321470) of [760,000 Jews](https://www.timesofisrael.com/west-bank-settlements-report-rapid-growth-in-2019/) currently living in the territory in order to secure their land.
1.3.3.4.3.1. Pro: Article 7 of the Rome Statute of the International Criminal Court considers the forced deportation of an entire population as a [crime against humanity](https://legal.un.org/icc/statute/99_corr/cstatute.htm). Enabling Palestine to commit a crime against humanity is neither the right nor the moral thing to do.
1.3.3.4.3.2. Con: No one would be forcibly displaced unless the government were to specifically allow for that to happen.
1.3.3.4.3.2.1. Pro: All the Jewish people currently living on what would become Palestinian land would be able to chose whether to continue living in Palestine or not.
1.3.3.5. Con: The legitimacy of one state \(here: Palestine\) does not depend on whether its recognition might have collateral effects for its neighbors \(such as Israel\).
1.3.3.5.1. Pro: The widely accepted criteria for statehood are "a permanent population, a defined territory, a government, and the capacity to conduct international relations", as laid out in [the Montevideo Convention of 1933](https://www.britannica.com/topic/international-law/States-in-international-law#ref233506).
1.3.3.5.1.1. Con: The Montevideo Convention criteria define the minimum standards that have to be met for an entity to be considered a state, but they say little about the legitimacy of that status and are not necessarily sufficient to provide legitimacy.
1.4. Pro: The US has an obligation to recognise Palestine as a state.
1.4.1. Pro: Given that recognizing Palestine as a state will benefit the US, they have an obligation to act in the best interests of their citizens.
1.4.1.1. Pro: The negative perception of Israel's defiance of international law, occupation of Palestinian territories and military engagements with surrounding countries, reflects poorly on the US as the "[principal enabler](http://www.theamericanconservative.com/articles/americas-misadventures-in-the-middle-east/)" of this behavior.
1.4.1.1.1. Pro: Surveys from countries like Britain show Israel's unpopularity. Among non-European countries, British people feel more unfavorable only towards North Korea; even Iran is perceived as more favorably than Israel \([pp. 10-11](https://www.chathamhouse.org/sites/default/files/field/field_document/20150129YouGovRaines.pdf)\).
1.4.1.1.2. Pro: About as many Germans hold a negative opinion about Israel as a positive one. The [most common attributes](https://de.statista.com/statistik/daten/studie/226525/umfrage/umfrage-zum-bild-der-deutschen-von-israel/) associated with Israel by the majority of Germans are ruthlessness and aggressiveness \([p. 31](https://www.bertelsmann-stiftung.de/fileadmin/files/BSt/Publikationen/GrauePublikationen/Studie_LW_Germany_and_Israel_today_2015.pdf)\).
1.4.1.1.3. Con: National interests often override potential public relations damage, otherwise the US would not have supported [regimes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_authoritarian_regimes_supported_by_the_United_States) that are far worse and more unpopular than Israel.
1.4.1.1.4. Pro: Recognizing Palestine, and thus taking a more moderate stance on the conflict, would serve to dissociate the US from Israel's actions.
1.4.1.1.5. Con: Given the long history of the US providing unwavering support for Israel, one largely symbolic move by a single administration wouldn't substantially affect the international perception of the country.
1.4.1.1.6. Con: Negative perceptions of Israel do not exist in a vacuum, so they should be taken with a grain of salt.
1.4.1.1.6.1. Pro: Negative views of Israel don't stem solely from their defiance of international law, but also from widespread anti-Semitism. Due to the link between anti-Semitism and negative perceptions of Israel, the U.S should not be guided by the latter.
1.4.1.1.6.1.1. Pro: Given their history of [allyship and common interests](https://www.vox.com/2018/11/20/18080080/israel-palestine-us-alliance), the US will continue to maintain close ties with Israel regardless of whether it recognizes Palestine. Therefore, recognizing Palestine as a state is unlikely to change any reputational damage that the US suffers from its association with Israel.
1.4.1.1.6.1.2. Con: US recognition of Palestine will be perceived not just as a dissociation from Israel's actions towards their neighbour, but also as a general repudiation of Israel as an actor. Even if negative perceptions of Israel are based on anti-Semitism, the US's image will improve.
1.4.1.1.6.2. Pro: [Some believe](https://www.theatlantic.com/international/archive/2014/11/how-the-media-makes-the-israel-story/383262/) that, as the international media tends to assign blame for the region's conflict primarily to Israel, it has become "an amplifier for the propaganda" of radical Palestinian forces.
1.4.1.1.6.2.1. Pro: Reporting by Al-Arabiya and Al-Jazeera often casts Palestinians as victims and Israelis as aggressors. Palestinian perspectives and suffering are emphasized over the Israeli experience \([p. 16](https://www.researchgate.net/publication/270634159_Al-Jazeera_and_Al-Arabiya_framing_of_the_Israel-Palestine_conflict_during_war_and_calm_periods)\).
1.4.1.1.6.2.2. Pro: Some evidence demonstrates that American television stations and newspapers are biased in their reporting on the Israel-Palestine conflict by casting Israel as the sole aggressor \([pp. 113-114](https://www.washingtoninstitute.org/policy-analysis/covering-intifada-how-media-reported-palestinian-uprising)\).
1.4.1.1.6.2.3. Con: Previous research that decries media coverage of Israel and Palestine was conducted by a group [connected with](http://foreignpolicy.com/2010/04/09/robert-satloff-doth-protest-too-much/) American Israel Public Affairs Committee \(AIPAC\) - the country's largest pro-Israel lobbying group \([p. 12-13](https://www.washingtoninstitute.org/media/3544)\). Its publications should be seen as agenda-driven.
1.4.1.1.6.3. Con: An [analysis](https://www.trtworld.com/magazine/mind-your-language-how-anti-palestinian-bias-is-framed-in-us-media-47049) of 33,000 New York Times articles featuring Israel found that the newspaper often cast Israel in a favorable light.
1.4.1.1.6.4. Con: Palestinian voices are [actively silenced](https://www.aljazeera.com/opinions/2021/5/13/social-media-companies-are-trying-to-silence-palestinian-voices) across a variety of social media sites and communication platforms.
1.4.1.1.6.4.1. Pro: Zoom [cancelled](https://www.thefire.org/zoom-cancels-another-academic-event-with-leila-khaled-again-raising-questions-about-companys-role-in-the-classroom/) an academic webinar to be held by a Palestinian activist.
1.4.1.1.6.4.1.1. Con: The Palestinian activist in question is a known [terrorist](https://www.vice.com/en/article/9k99k7/leila-khaled-first-female-hijacker-profile) and could have been planning to propagate certain ideas or behaviors that run contrary to Zoom's terms and conditions.
1.4.1.1.6.4.2. Pro: Research has shown that YouTube, Google, and Facebook have all [systematically blocked](https://www.business-humanrights.org/en/latest-news/paper-alleges-systematic-efforts-to-silence-palestinian-content-on-social-media/) Palestinian content on their sites.
1.4.1.1.7. Pro: Recognition of Palestine would undermine the belief that the US only respects international rules and UN institutions when it can take advantage of them.
1.4.1.1.7.1. Con: In light of other actions taken by the US, recognising Palestine will not convince anyone that the US respects international law when it does not benefit itself.
1.4.1.1.7.1.1. Con: That the US has not recognized the legitimacy of other national or international courts does not mean that it should not. Indeed, the treaties and conventions that have established International Law are in principle [binding](https://www.hg.org/international-law.html) on the US.
1.4.1.1.7.1.2. Pro: The US has [prevented](https://www.bbc.com/news/world-asia-47912140) an investigation of alleged war crimes by the US Army in Afghanistan.
1.4.1.1.7.1.3. Pro: Former US President Donald Trump [declared](https://www.timesofisrael.com/trump-says-israelis-should-be-immune-from-international-criminal-court/) that Israel and other allies should be immune to the ICC, and [threatened](https://www.bbc.com/news/world-us-canada-45474864) the ICC with sanctions should they go ahead with investigations.
1.4.1.2. Con: Israel's withdrawal from occupied areas following US recognition of Palestine will create a political and military vacuum that could open the doors for militant groups to take control of the state.
1.4.1.2.1. Con: The Palestinian economy has seen a trajectory of "[strong growth](http://documents.worldbank.org/curated/en/137111468329419171/West-Bank-and-Gaza-Area-C-and-the-future-of-the-Palestinian-economy)" in the past despite massive challenges. This demonstrates an economic dynamism that would make it unlikely to collapse into a failed state.
1.4.1.2.1.1. Con: Economic growth alone is by no means a predictor of whether a state can descend into domestic turmoil. All major states of the Arab Spring - [Tunisia](https://tradingeconomics.com/tunisia/gdp-growth-annual), [Egypt](https://tradingeconomics.com/egypt/gdp-growth-annual), [Libya](https://tradingeconomics.com/libya/gdp-growth-annual), [Yemen](https://tradingeconomics.com/yemen/gdp-growth-annual), [Syria](https://tradingeconomics.com/syria/gdp-growth-annual) and [Bahrain](https://tradingeconomics.com/bahrain/gdp-growth-annual) - experienced steady and moderate economic growth of around 4% prior to the events of 2011.
1.4.1.2.1.2. Pro: GDP growth in Palestine is expected to [return to 3.5%](https://www.worldbank.org/en/country/westbankandgaza/publication/economic-update-april-2021) in 2021.
1.4.1.2.1.2.1. Con: Growth tends to be cyclical and dynamic; a [2017 report](https://www.imf.org/en/News/Articles/2017/02/13/pr1746-IMF-Staff-Concludes-Visit-to-West-Bank-and-Gaza) from the IMF spoke of "increasingly difficult conditions" for the Palestinian economy and mentioned that the "outlook for the economy is daunting." This is hardly an optimistic evaluation of Palestine's prospects.
1.4.1.2.2. Pro: Naftali Bennett, the current PM of Israel, has argued that this a resurgence in violence is exactly what would happen should Israel withdraw. He cited [historical precedent](https://www.nytimes.com/2014/11/06/opinion/naftali-bennett-for-israel-two-state-is-no-solution.html), as proof.
1.4.1.2.2.1. Pro: -> See 1.2.2.3.2.
1.4.1.2.2.2. Con: The violence cited by Bennett could have been caused by the respective Israeli occupations causing a surge in support for radical parties, not subsequent withdrawal.
1.4.1.2.3. Con: The current conditions of the Palestinian territories are what provides radical groups a foothold. By providing Palestinians with the right to live in their own state, they will have little need to turn to radical Islamists.
1.4.1.2.4. Pro: Hamas and Fatah, the two dominant groups in control of Gaza and the West Bank respectively, will never be able to work with each other. This could increase conflict in the region.
1.4.1.2.4.1. Pro: Hamas is often considered an [extremist](https://www.state.gov/j/ct/rls/other/des/123085.htm) group, and would would never accept a power-sharing agreement.
1.4.1.2.4.1.1. Con: Many radical groups have accepted power-sharing agreements and joined the political systems of recognized governments.
1.4.1.2.4.1.1.1. Pro: The post-Apartheid government of South Africa is led by the ANC \(African National Congress\), an organization the [US had formerly labeled](http://www.nbcnews.com/news/other/us-government-considered-nelson-mandela-terrorist-until-2008-f2D11708787) as a terrorist group.
1.4.1.2.4.1.1.2. Pro: The Kosovo Liberation Army \(KLA\) was [described as a terrorist group by US officials](https://www.cfr.org/backgrounder/terrorist-groups-and-political-legitimacy) before eventually forming part of the government and armed forces of the \(partially recognized\) country.
1.4.1.2.4.1.1.3. Con: 71% of attempted power-sharing agreements in Asia between 1989 and 2006 [failed due to a resumption of fighting](http://www.pewresearch.org/fact-tank/2014/09/05/study-half-of-government-rebel-power-sharing-agreements-fail/).
1.4.1.2.4.1.1.4. Pro: Maoist rebels in Nepal [now successfully share power](https://www.files.ethz.ch/isn/117620/Nepal%20Policy%20Brief.pdf) in the country's government, through an agreement that ended a long-running civil war.
1.4.1.2.4.1.1.4.1. Con: Though the party formed by the former Maoist rebels is now the most popular one in the country, some remnants of their foundation as rebels has permeated modern society, with leadership [unwilling to make changes](https://www.reuters.com/article/idINIndia-33259820080427)(But the Maoists still command a rebel army, have refused to renounce violence and speak of a “people revolt” if they are stopped from taking power, posturing that has unnerved opposition parties about their commitment to democratic ideals.). This has caused strife among opposition parties and it will be difficult to form a coalition and strike a balance.
1.4.1.2.4.1.1.5. Con: These groups were largely not opposed to US foreign policy when they were legitimized by the US. Hamas, on the other hand, [has threatened attacks](http://www.nbcnews.com/id/15617830/ns/world_news-mideast_n_africa/t/hamas-calls-muslims-attack-us-targets/#.WSdBL2iGNeU) against the US.
1.4.1.2.4.1.1.5.1. Con: Hamas has not yet targeted US citizens, proving that their threats are little more than rhetoric \([p. 194](https://books.google.de/books?id=IOoBZvdNrIkC&printsec=frontcover&source=gbs_ge_summary_r&cad=0#v=onepage&q=%22Thus%20far%2C%20Hamas%22&f=false)\).
1.4.1.2.4.1.1.6. Pro: Northern Ireland managed to form a government in 2007 between the Democratic Unionist Party and Sinn Fein - [both](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Democratic_Unionist_Party)(On 10 November 1986, a rally was held in which DUP politicians Paisley, Robinson and Ivan Foster announced the formation of the Ulster Resistance Movement \(URM\). This was a loyalist paramilitary group whose purpose was to "take direct action as and when required" to bring down the Agreement and defeat republicanism. Recruitment rallies were held in towns across Northern Ireland and thousands were said to have joined. The following year, the URM helped smuggle a large shipment of weapons into Northern Ireland, which were shared out between the URM, the Ulster Volunteer Force \(UVF\) and the Ulster Defence Association \(UDA\). Most, but not all, of the weaponry was seized by police in 1988. In 1989, URM members attempted to trade Shorts' missile blueprints for weapons from the apartheid South African regime. Following these revelations, the DUP said that it had cut its links with the URM in 1987.) of which have historic [paramilitary](https://www.theguardian.com/politics/2020/feb/16/sinn-fein-election-success-tainted-past) links. This suggests that former terrorist organizations can be integrated into government more easily after peace has been established.
1.4.1.2.4.1.1.6.1. Con: Sinn Féin and the DUP were deadlocked in negotiations over the formation of a power sharing government for [approximately three years](https://www.theguardian.com/politics/2020/jan/11/northern-ireland-assembly-reopens-three-years-after-collapse). This suggests that the ability of factions to find common ground does not necessarily last.
1.4.1.2.4.1.1.7. Pro: A similar solution was implemented in Lebanon, where the conflicting parties entered an [inter-religious power sharing agreement](https://blogs.wsj.com/briefly/2015/08/27/things-to-know-about-lebanons-government/). This has allowed the various religious and ethnic groups within Lebanon to live peacefully together.
1.4.1.2.4.1.1.7.1. Con: Because of its sectarian divisions, Lebanon is a country that is notorious for its [political instability](https://www.europeanforum.net/headlines/lebanon-economic-crisis-rooted-in-political-divisions). If anything, it is an example of the problems that states with long-standing ethnic and religious divisions suffer.
1.4.1.2.4.1.2. Pro: Keeping hostilities going and even going to war periodically with Israel ensures the survival of Hamas. In order to go to war, Hamas needs to be in control of territory within Palestine, for which purpose it will [hold on to Gaza](https://www.bbc.com/news/world-middle-east-13331522)(Under its charter, it is committed to the destruction of Israel. \[...\] Hamas originally had a dual purpose of carrying out an armed struggle against Israel - led by its military wing, the Izzedine al-Qassam Brigades - and delivering social welfare programmes. \[...\] But since 2005, when Israel withdrew its troops and settlers from Gaza, Hamas has also engaged in the Palestinian political process. \[...\] Since then, militants in Gaza have fought four major conflicts with Israel, which along with Egypt has maintained a blockade on the strip to isolate Hamas and to pressure it to stop attacks.).
1.4.1.2.4.1.2.1. Pro: Hamas [fears](https://www.gatestoneinstitute.org/4707/what-does-hamas-want) that Palestinians will eventually tire of a military approach to the conflict. A war with Israel leads to countless deaths of innocent Palestinians; this fuels Palestinian hatred for Israel and paints Hamas as soldiers fighting for the Palestinians.
1.4.1.2.4.1.2.2. Con: If Palestinians were to have a stable state of their own, going to war would become far less attractive. This suggests that Hamas would very likely either have to moderate itself, or cease to have popular support.
1.4.1.2.4.1.3. Con: The designation of "[terrorist organization](https://www.state.gov/j/ct/rls/other/des/123085.htm)" is an arbitrary distinction that does not necessarily reflect the manner of violence, the scale of violence, or the threat to the United States. The designation is based only on political concerns.
1.4.1.2.4.1.3.1. Pro: Hamas is a terrorist organisation in part because it is not a government. No democratically elected government is seen as a terrorist organisation and Hamas would be no different.
1.4.1.2.4.1.3.2. Con: Hamas, or at the very least their military wing, is responsible for [suicide bombings](https://www.theguardian.com/world/2008/feb/06/israelandthepalestinians.international) as well as [rocket and mortar attacks](https://www.bbc.com/news/world-middle-east-32053999) [and kidnappings](https://www.cnn.com/2014/06/15/world/meast/west-bank-jewish-teens-missing) against the state of Israel. This is more than political.
1.4.1.2.4.1.3.3. Pro: The US government has [yet to declare](https://historianandrew.medium.com/why-isnt-the-kkk-designated-a-terrorist-organization-73732ad40bc7) the KKK a terrorist organization. Their rules for acknowledging terrorist groups seem to be arbitrary at best, and knowingly deceitful at worst.
1.4.1.2.4.1.4. Pro: Hamas decided to [contest](http://www.ynetnews.com/articles/0,7340,L-4844196,00.html) the upcoming municipal elections in the West Bank, indicating a clear interest in ruling the area long term.
1.4.1.2.4.1.4.1. Pro: In 2015, 39% of Palestinians in Gaza said they would [vote for Hamas](https://www.middleeastmonitor.com/20150610-poll-hamas-popularity-up-in-gaza-west-bank/), more than any other political group. This would make it a strong political actor in the region.
1.4.1.2.4.1.4.2. Pro: In 2021, 53% of Palestinians [supported](https://www.aljazeera.com/news/2021/6/15/gaza-protests-against-israeli-right-wing-march-through-jerusalem)(The poll found that 53 percent of Palestinians believe Hamas is “most deserving of representing and leading the Palestinian people”, while only 14 percent prefer Abbas’s Fatah party.) the group.
1.4.1.2.4.1.5. Pro: Hamas was [founded](https://fas.org/irp/world/para/docs/880818a.htm) with the explicit purpose of destroying the state of Israel - ruling Gaza gives Hamas the foothold in Palestine it needs to be able to launch attacks against Israel.
1.4.1.2.4.2. Pro: Hamas and Fatah have [fundamentally different approaches](https://www.theatlantic.com/international/archive/2014/04/a-brief-history-of-the-fraught-relationship-between-fatah-and-hamas/361178/) to the state of Israel. Hamas believes the state does not have the right to exist, and Fatah believes it does, choosing to attempt political solutions instead.
1.4.1.2.4.2.1. Con: Past behavior and prioritisation may be indicative of what Hamas and Fatah are likely to do; however, future co-operation cannot be ruled out entirely.
1.4.1.2.4.2.2. Pro: Hamas and Fatah's multiple past attempts to work together have resulted in failure. Even when deals are brokered by Egypt, the groups [struggle](http://america.aljazeera.com/articles/2015/6/19/palestinian-political-crisis-deepens-with-collapse-of-unity-government.html) to put their differences aside.
1.4.1.2.4.2.3. Pro: While President Mahmoud Abbas has declared security cooperation with Israel as [sacred](http://www.timesofisrael.com/abbas-vows-to-uphold-sacred-security-coordination-with-israel/), Hamas has [vowed](http://www.timesofisrael.com/hamas-vows-to-stop-west-bank-security-cooperation-with-israel/) to end that cooperation.
1.4.1.2.4.3. Con: Both Hamas and Fatah realise that they need to work together, and have agreed to form a new [National Council](http://www.independent.co.uk/news/world/middle-east/fatah-and-hamas-agree-to-form-unity-palestinian-government-to-end-election-gridlock-moscow-russia-a7533696.html) in order to hold elections.
1.4.1.2.4.4. Con: Hamas is taking measures to become a [more moderate and open political group](http://www.aljazeera.com/news/2017/05/hamas-accepts-palestinian-state-1967-borders-170501114309725.html) - this indicates that Hamas could work together with Fatah and the Palestinian Authority.
1.4.1.2.4.4.1. Con: In the past, Hamas has [violently clashed with Fatah](http://www.aljazeera.com/news/middleeast/2011/05/2011549435141647.html) to establish control over key areas. Clearly, the group has little intention to share power.
1.4.1.2.4.4.2. Con: In 2007, [Hamas expelled Fatah from Gaza](https://www.aljazeera.com/features/2017/10/12/hamas-and-fatah-how-are-the-two-groups-different)(Hamas has been the de facto ruler in the Gaza Strip since 2007, after defeating President Mahmoud Abbas’ long dominant Fatah party in parliamentary elections.\n\nHamas then pushed Fatah out of Gaza when the latter refused to recognise the result of the vote.\n\nHamas and Fatah have ruled the occupied Palestinian territories of the Gaza Strip and the West Bank respectively ever since.) after refusing to accept the election results. Since then, the two governments have been operating separately in Gaza and the West Bank, respectively.
1.4.1.2.5. Pro: Although ISIS is a relatively new presence in Palestine, [7% of Palestinians](http://www.pcpsr.org/en/node/636) and 13% in the Gaza Strip perceive ISIS as representing true Islam. This could enable ISIS to gain a foothold in Palestine.
1.4.1.2.6. Con: The risk of conflict resulting from Israel's withdrawal from Palestine is anticipated; therefore, preemptive steps to mitigate adversity can be planned and taken prior to withdrawal.
1.4.1.3. Pro: Given that unwavering support for Israel is primarily the [result of strong, organized lobbying](https://books.google.co.kr/books?id=2iUdyQs_NhYC&printsec=frontcover&dq=The+Israel+Lobby+and+American+Foreign+Policy&hl=en&sa=X&ved=0ahUKEwiP6LCW2c_TAhUMbrwKHfvZBH0Q6AEIJTAA)(p. 335f) on US politicians, such a decision would show the ability of US decision makers to remain independent.
1.4.1.3.1. Pro: In terms of funding provided to members of Congress, the Pro-Israel lobby ranks [among the top 30](https://www.opensecrets.org/industries/mems.php), far above any other country-specific lobby group in the US.
1.4.1.3.1.1. Pro: Funding provided by the Pro-Israel lobby was steadily increasing from 2002-2018; but, in 2020 it exploded, more than [doubling contributions from 2018](https://www.opensecrets.org/industries/totals.php?cycle=2020&ind=Q05).
1.4.1.3.2. Pro: The Pro-Israel lobby ranks among [the top five most influential lobby groups](http://www.washingtonpost.com/wp-dyn/content/article/2005/05/18/AR2005051802143.html) in American politics, alongside national organizations such as the NRA and the American Association of Retired Persons \(AARP\).
1.4.1.3.3. Con: The pro-Palestinian lobby is poorly organized, making the pro-Israel lobby seem stronger than it is in reality.
1.4.1.3.3.1. Pro: [Cursory Google searches](https://www.google.com/search?q=pro+palestinian+lobby+in+US&client=firefox-b-d&ei=qskHYYTNBIzgkgXVwoeQAg&start=0&sa=N&ved=2ahUKEwiEyp2nkZLyAhUMsKQKHVXhASI4ChDy0wN6BAgBEDY&biw=1368&bih=663) about the pro-Palestinian lobby provide very little information and are dominated by the pro-Israel lobby; [websites are down](http://www.aaper.org/)(The American Association for Palestinian Equal Rights website), and [Wikipedia articles are unfinished](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/American_Association_for_Palestinian_Equal_Rights).
1.4.1.3.3.1.1. Pro: Google's own employees have [formally requested](https://mashable.com/article/google-employee-letter-palestine) the search engine to be more forthcoming in recognizing the Palestinian struggle.
1.4.1.3.3.2. Con: The two are not mutually exclusive; the pro-Israel lobby can be considered strong regardless of the relative power, or lack thereof, of the pro-Palestine lobby.
1.4.1.4. Pro: Recognition of Palestine could improve the image of the US in the Arab world.
1.4.1.4.1. Pro: The Palestinian conflict colors public perception of the US in the Arab world.
1.4.1.4.1.1. Con: US recognition would be unlikely to actually alleviate the plight of the Palestinian people, so anger at the US for perpetuating the conflict up to the present day would persist.
1.4.1.4.1.2. Pro: The citizens of major US allies including Saudi Arabia and Egypt, see the occupation of Palestinian territories as a [highly problematic issue.](https://www.brookings.edu/blog/order-from-chaos/2021/05/16/a-separate-peace-what-the-gaza-crisis-means-for-arab-regimes/)(“Once official statements signaled that the Saudi government was weighing in firmly on the side of Palestinians, I started to see considerably more pro-Palestinian statements on Saudi Twitter,” he told me.\n\nPalestine arouses passions. It always has, and it always will. It is one of the last remaining issues that can rally broad and genuine support across Arab borders. This is why messaging must be carefully managed by regimes. Transnational solidarity — whether in the form of pan-Arabism or Islamism — is a threat. It can’t easily be controlled. And so the goal is to limit and constrain it. For various regimes, then, the reemergence of fellow feeling toward the Palestinians is a problem. The timing isn’t great either. Just last year, Emirati and Saudi columnists like Abdelrahman Al-Rashed were\ncalling the Abraham Accords “a great step that serves the Palestinian people first, and the UAE and the Arabs second,” although he\nhad trouble sustaining this position for long.)
1.4.1.4.1.2.1. Con: Given that the majority of the Arab world, including Saudi Arabia and Egypt, [aren't democracies](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Democracy_Index), the beliefs of private citizens are largely irrelevant compared to government priorities in regional security and economic interests.
1.4.1.4.1.2.1.1. Con: Even dictatorships are receptive to popular will to some extent. Complete disregard for popular opinion always leads to instability.
1.4.1.4.1.2.1.2. Pro: Israel [opened](http://www.huffingtonpost.com/samuel-ramani/why-israel-is-strengthening_b_11946660.html) its first diplomatic mission in the United Arab Emirates \(UAE\) three months after it stopped bombing Gaza in 2015. The Gulf states have signed covert deals with the Israeli defence contractors to gain access to the IDF’s prized military technology. This is used to secure oil wells. Economic interests trump the demand for a Palestinian state.
1.4.1.4.1.2.1.3. Con: While it might be that popular perception is not as important for state actors to the extent that they are non-democratic, it still influences many other aspects of national relations, since a nation is far more than simply its state.
1.4.1.4.1.2.1.4. Con: The fact that these countries have backdoor relations with Israel indicates that these relations are important for their regional security and economic interests. Being able to establish a more open relationship is in their interests; these countries will therefore care about whether public opinion permits an open relationship.
1.4.1.4.1.2.1.4.1. Con: Pressuring Israel for a peace deal will likely alienate it as Israel does not want to recognise an independent Palestine. This risks destroying whatever gains have been made through backdoor and covert diplomacy.
1.4.1.4.1.2.2. Pro: Recognizing Palestine could garner support for the US in these countries.
1.4.1.4.1.2.3. Pro: Egyptians in particular believe that "normalization with Palestine’s enemy is a [betrayal of the Palestinian cause](https://www.al-monitor.com/originals/2019/01/egypt-israel-peace-cultural-normalization.html)(“The Egyptian intelligentsia deter any attempts of public normalization with Israel. Egyptian citizens believe normalization with Palestine’s enemy is a betrayal of the Palestinian cause, which is central in Egyptians’ interests.”), which is central in Egyptians’ interests.”
1.4.1.4.1.2.4. Con: A study found that people in Jordan, Lebanon, and Iraq ascribe [little importance](https://foreignpolicy.com/wp-content/uploads/2018/12/8a1be-2018SBYFINALWEB.pdf)(Table 2, p. 7) to the Palestinian issue.
1.4.1.4.1.3. Pro: In the Arab world, the Palestinian issue is [predominantly responsible for the prevailing attitudes](http://www.pewresearch.org/2005/11/10/arab-and-muslim-perceptions-of-the-united-states/) towards America.
1.4.1.4.1.3.1. Pro: All Arab countries [recognise](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/International_recognition_of_the_State_of_Palestine) Palestine as a state.
1.4.1.4.1.4. Con: The [roots of anti-Americanism](https://www.pewresearch.org/2005/11/10/arab-and-muslim-perceptions-of-the-united-states/) in the Arab world are far deeper than just the recognition of Palestine.
1.4.1.4.1.4.1. Pro: Anti-Americanism is [unlikely to immediately disappear](https://www2.kenyon.edu/Depts/Religion/Fac/Adler/Politics/Rubin-article.htm) from the Arab world, following formal recognition of Palestine.
1.4.1.4.1.4.2. Pro: US policies are [largely responsible](https://www.pewresearch.org/2005/11/10/arab-and-muslim-perceptions-of-the-united-states/)(Anti-Americanism in the region is driven largely by aversion to U.S. policies, such as the war in Iraq, the war on terrorism, and U.S. support for Israel, in addition to the general perception that the U.S. fails to consider the interests of countries in the region when it acts in the international arena.) for anti-Americanism.
1.4.1.4.1.4.3. Con: Though recognition of Palestine is a key issue and would improve the standing of the United States in the eyes of the Arab world.
1.4.1.4.1.5. Con: The recognition of Palestine is not as crucial of a factor as some believe with regards to the public perception of the United States.
1.4.1.4.1.5.1. Pro: Perception of the United States has [improved slightly](https://www.pewresearch.org/2005/11/10/arab-and-muslim-perceptions-of-the-united-states/)(America’s favorability rating has increased significantly in Lebanon, Jordan, and Morocco. Indeed, more Moroccans now hold a positive view of the U.S. \(49%\) than a negative one \(44%\).) in the Arab world; yet the official US government stance on Palestine has remained the same.
1.4.1.4.1.6. Pro: Given the US's history of [intense opposition](http://edition.cnn.com/2016/12/28/politics/ben-rhodes-veto-un-resolution-palestinian-state-obama/) to recognising Palestinian statehood, a decision this unprecedented and of this magnitude would have a massive impact on Arab perceptions of the US.
1.4.1.4.2. Pro: As recognition of Palestine would be perceived as a step in opposition to Israel's stated interests, this is likely to be perceived positively throughout the Middle East.
1.4.1.4.2.1. Pro: Few people in major Middle Eastern countries have positive opinions on Israel; they do not see the country as a contributor to peace and stability in the region, or view relations with Israel as important \([pp. 5, 7, 8](https://d3n8a8pro7vhmx.cloudfront.net/aai/pages/12021/attachments/original/1481751962/SBY2016_FINAL.pdf?1481751962)\).
1.4.1.4.3. Pro: A favourable image of the US allows for a better relationship between the US and Arab countries to form, which could lead to better trade agreements and intelligence sharing.
1.4.1.4.3.1. Con: If there are pragmatic benefits to be gained through cooperation, Middle Eastern states will cooperate with the US regardless of "perception" of the US' morality as an actor.
1.4.1.4.3.2. Pro: The US conducts operations in several countries in the Middle East, which they could do more easily if Arab countries had a more positive image of the US. Willingness to help and cooperate would likely be higher if the attitude towards the US were more positive.
1.4.1.4.3.2.1. Pro: In their operations in Iraq, the US military [relied heavily](https://www.pri.org/stories/2017-01-31/iraqi-translators-who-served-us-military-are-desperate-exemption-trumps-travel) on assistance from local translators. The willingness of translators to cooperate, and of the local population to tolerate people who cooperate with the US military, was dependent on public perception of the US.
1.4.1.4.4. Con: Any improvement of America's reputation in the region will be limited as the Israel-Palestine question is only one of many issues that determine how America is seen.
1.4.1.4.4.1. Pro: Negative [stereotypes](http://www.pewglobal.org/2011/07/21/chapter-2-how-muslims-and-westerners-view-each-other/) about Westerners as 'selfish', 'violent' or 'greedy' help to perpetuate Anti-Americanism.
1.4.1.4.4.2. Pro: The US supports corrupt autocracies in the region and thus [fuels](http://www.huffingtonpost.com/steve-koppman/endless-us-support-for-di_b_6821136.html) anti-Americanism.
1.4.1.4.4.2.1. Pro: In non-democratic countries supported by and allied with the US, such as Iraq, the United Arab Emirates and Jordan, the lack of representative government is seen as the primary obstacle to peace and stability in the region \([p. 11](https://d3n8a8pro7vhmx.cloudfront.net/aai/pages/12021/attachments/original/1481751962/SBY2016_FINAL.pdf?1481751962)\).
1.4.1.4.4.3. Pro: The US has a track record of military interventions in the Middle East which have negatively shaped perceptions.
1.4.1.4.4.3.1. Pro: The presence of US soldiers alienates the local population.
1.4.1.4.4.3.1.1. Pro: The [habits](https://www.cfr.org/backgrounder/saudi-arabia-withdrawl-us-forces) of US soldiers radicalize some locals as they drink alcohol and behave outside social norms, as was observed in Saudi Arabia.
1.4.1.4.4.3.1.2. Pro: US military bases and soldiers are a magnet for [terrorist attacks](https://www.cfr.org/backgrounder/saudi-arabia-withdrawl-us-forces), risking the lives of those nearby. In the 1990s, the base in Saudi Arabia was moved because of this.
1.4.1.4.4.3.2. Pro: A military presence is interpreted by some as an all out [war against Islam](https://theintercept.com/2016/10/11/us-military-operations-are-biggest-motivation-for-homegrown-terrorists-fbi-study-finds/). For individuals that link their identity to Islam, this can be seen as an attack on themselves.
1.4.1.4.4.3.3. Pro: The violence and death caused as a result of these military interventions leads to resentment towards the US.
1.4.1.4.4.3.3.1. Pro: [News coverage](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/July_12,_2007_Baghdad_airstrike) of massacres or collateral murder, such as the Baghdad airstrikes in 2007, antagonizes bystanders and supports radical thinking against the US.
1.4.1.4.4.3.3.2. Con: American interference in the region is generally not seen by public opinion as one of the most severe obstacles to peace and stability in the region - not even in countries directly affected by it like Iraq \([p. 11](https://d3n8a8pro7vhmx.cloudfront.net/aai/pages/12021/attachments/original/1481751962/SBY2016_FINAL.pdf?1481751962)\).
1.4.1.4.4.3.4. Con: By now, the United States has withdrawn from the countries where it intervened with ground troops in the recent past: [Iraq](https://www.aljazeera.com/news/2021/12/9/iraq-official-says-us-combat-mission-in-the-country-has-ended) and [Afghanistan](https://edition.cnn.com/2021/08/30/politics/us-military-withdraws-afghanistan/index.html). It, therefore, stands to reason that this factor will become less relevant in the near future.
1.4.1.4.4.4. Con: Surveys show that American culture and political values are generally seen as positive, whereas American policies in the Middle East evoke opposition - with the policies towards Palestine being among the prime sources \([p. 15](http://politics.as.nyu.edu/docs/IO/4737/chiozza_f04.pdf)\).
1.4.1.4.5. Pro: Recognizing Palestine would improve America's standing among the people of Palestine.
1.4.1.4.5.1. Con: The Palestinians know their side of the conflict is legitimate. Unless the US de-recognises Israel at the same time as recognising Palestine, it won't gain any particular credit from the Palestinians for recognising what is perceived by Palestinians as reality.
1.4.1.4.5.2. Con: Palestine has barely 4.5 million citizens and [an economy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_countries_by_GDP_\(nominal\)) the size of Burkina Faso's. It is hardly relevant for the United States as a partner or market.
1.4.1.4.5.3. Con: America should not recognise Palestine, as even if their standing improves, it is less important than other outcomes.
1.4.1.4.5.4. Pro: Internal and external accords, laws, and policies require the US to [intervene and improve](https://www.state.gov/u-s-relations-with-palestinian-territories/)(Since the signing of the Oslo Accords in 1993, the United States has been the largest provider of assistance to Palestinians in the West Bank and Gaza Strip, providing more than $7.6 billion in economic development and security funding—in addition to humanitarian assistance. U.S. foreign assistance for the Palestinian people serves important U.S. interests, including providing critical relief to those in great need, fostering economic development, and supporting Israeli-Palestinian security cooperation. Economic and humanitarian assistance programs improve the lives of millions of Palestinians by providing immediate relief and advancing development across sectors such as health, infrastructure, economic growth, private sector development, and civil society. In administering assistance for the West Bank and Gaza Strip, the United States complies with applicable requirements under U.S. law, including the Taylor Force Act.) the lives of Palestinians. Negative perceptions of the US among Palestinians can make this delivery of assistance and support more challenging.
1.4.1.4.5.5. Pro: Palestine has many natural resources, which are currently being [exploited by Israelis](https://www.ohchr.org/en/NewsEvents/Pages/DisplayNews.aspx?NewsID=24349&LangID=E). Improving perceptions of the US among Palestinians could facilitate the establishment of businesses that benefit the local people \(e.g., job creation\) as well as the US economy.
1.4.1.4.6. Con: Any benefit to US-Arab relations would be negligible at best and at worst it would be seen as a betrayal of one of their key regional allies, Israel.
1.4.1.4.6.1. Pro: US allies in the Middle East are more concerned about their own socio-economic conditions and security than about Israel.
1.4.1.4.6.2. Pro: Israel's enemies around the world \(including Hamas and the PA\) will not be pacified by recognition, or even the creation of a Palestinian state - only by the destruction of the Jewish one.
1.4.1.4.6.2.1. Pro: Hamas and other vocal enemies of Israel could hardly sell more amicable relations to their domestic audiences and supporters after decades of hateful rhetoric towards Israel and threats of destruction.
1.4.1.4.6.3. Con: America shouldn't be concerned about the reaction in Israel.
1.4.1.4.6.3.1. Pro: Israel does not behave as an ally to the United States.
1.4.1.4.6.3.1.1. Pro: Israel has a history of spying on the US, the most notable example being espionage by the ex-intelligence analyst [Jonathan Pollard](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jonathan_Pollard).
1.4.1.4.6.3.1.2. Pro: The Israeli Prime Minister [went to the US congress](https://www.timesofisrael.com/netanyahu-spat-in-our-face-white-house-officials-say/) to undermine the President of the United States.
1.4.1.4.6.3.1.3. Pro: Israel's [diplomatic efforts against the most important multilateral deal](https://www.reuters.com/article/us-usa-israel/israels-netanyahu-draws-rebuke-from-obama-over-iran-speech-to-congress-idUSKBN0LZ0BS20150303) led by Obama were not consistent with an alliance.
1.4.1.4.6.3.2. Pro: While one might expect one of America's closest allies to play a supportive role in times of conflict, Israel has been a strategic burden in the past.
1.4.1.4.6.3.2.1. Con: This singular instance from a quarter of a century ago is hardly representative of the United States' relationship with Israel as a whole.
1.4.1.4.6.3.2.2. Pro: During the Gulf War in 1990-1991, the US government had to [intentionally prevent](http://users.ox.ac.uk/~ssfc0005/Israel%20and%20the%20Conflict.html) Israel from joining the coalition against Iraq because its participation might have led to more Arab support for Iraq or possibly even have caused some Arab countries to leave the coalition altogether.
1.4.1.4.7. Con: Some nations in the Arab League have diplomatic ties with both the US and Israel.
1.4.1.4.7.1. Pro: Egypt's relations with Israel are the [best they have been in history](http://www.aljazeera.com/indepth/features/2016/11/egypt-israel-relations-highest-level-history-161107083926863.html).
1.4.1.4.7.1.1. Pro: Israel and Egypt cooperate on regional security concerns such as Hamas and terrorist groups in the Sinai peninsula.
1.4.1.4.7.1.1.1. Con: While that may have been true in the past, more recently Egypt has actually sought to [improve relations with Hamas](https://www.reuters.com/article/us-palestinians-egypt-sinai-idUSKBN16010C) in order to secure the Sinai peninsula.
1.4.1.4.7.1.1.1.1. Pro: Hamas officials are [regularly invited to Egypt](https://www.reuters.com/article/us-palestinians-egypt-sinai-idUSKBN16010C) and the two keep communication channels open.
1.4.1.4.7.1.1.2. Pro: Since al-Sisi came to power in 2013, security cooperation between Egypt and Israel has [reached unprecedented levels](https://www.atlanticcouncil.org/blogs/menasource/lessons-from-israel-and-egypts-lukewarm-peace/).
1.4.1.4.7.1.1.2.1. Pro: Increased [ISIS attacks in the Sinai peninsula](https://www.haaretz.com/at-least-50-egyptian-soldiers-killed-in-sinai-terror-attacks-1.5374819) have forced Israel and Egypt to cooperate more closely.
1.4.1.4.7.1.2. Pro: Egypt's calls for peace between Israel and Palestine is widely considered one of the most likely solutions to resolve the conflict.
1.4.1.4.7.1.2.1. Pro: [Egypt was largely responsible for brokering peace](https://www.france24.com/en/live-news/20210520-israel-confirms-unconditional-gaza-ceasefire-agreed-with-hamas) in the ["Sword of Jerusalem" vs. "Guardian of the Walls"](https://www.washingtoninstitute.org/policy-analysis/sword-jerusalem-vs-guardian-walls-gaza-and-next-lebanon-war) conflict in 2021.
1.4.1.4.7.1.2.2. Pro: Egypt is putting pressure on both sides to [broker a long-term peace deal](https://www.egypttoday.com/Article/1/105932/Egypt-calls-for-urgent-move-to-resume-Palestine-Israel-peace).
1.4.1.4.7.1.3. Pro: Egypt is Israel's [closest regional partner](http://www.mesi.shisu.edu.cn/_upload/article/71/cf/e7e731dc4b948dad8285d988bbd7/09601a46-3756-4fc6-8638-a8b0efa1d51c.pdf)(Since recognizing Israel as a state, Egypt has had the closest relationship with Israel in the region. Under the presidency of Mubarak, the relationship between the two countries evolved and broadened. Egypt as one of the important Arab countries of the Middle East and Islamic world plays a crucial role in international scene and relationship among nations) \(p. 93\).
1.4.1.4.7.1.3.1. Pro: Egyptian officials held a number of [meetings with Israeli businessmen](https://www.atlanticcouncil.org/blogs/menasource/lessons-from-israel-and-egypts-lukewarm-peace/) in 2021, showing their relationship is growing even stronger.
1.4.1.4.7.1.4. Pro: Historically, Egypt permitted flights to Tel Aviv under a one-plane airline called Air Sinai, which did not bear the Egyptian flag. In March 2021, they announced that EgyptAir would absorb Air Sinai and that Tel Aviv-Cairo [flights would be tripled](https://www.atlanticcouncil.org/blogs/menasource/lessons-from-israel-and-egypts-lukewarm-peace/)(There are other examples of improving Israeli-Egyptian relations. For years, the route between Tel Aviv and Cairo was flown by Air Sinai—a one-plane airline that did not even bear the Egyptian flag—and not EgyptAir. However, in March 2021, it was announced that EgyptAir would fly the route under its name and triple the number of daily flights.).
1.4.1.4.7.1.5. Con: Despite the close government relationship with Israel, the Egyptian people are wholly [against normalizing ties with Israel](https://www.al-monitor.com/originals/2019/01/egypt-israel-peace-cultural-normalization.html).
1.4.1.4.7.2. Pro: There exists a '[moderate axis](https://www.middleeastmonitor.com/20140723-israeli-general-the-moderate-axis-is-helping-us-fight-hamas/)' of [Middle Eastern nations](http://www.aljazeera.com/indepth/features/2016/11/egypt-israel-relations-highest-level-history-161107083926863.html), including Egypt, Turkey, Saudi Arabia and several of the Gulf states, as well as Jordan, that have offered Israel a wide margin of flexibility to pursue the war on Hamas. Public calls for peace are accompanied by backdoor diplomacy.
1.4.1.4.7.2.1. Pro: These nations [perceive](https://www.nytimes.com/2014/07/31/world/middleeast/fighting-political-islam-arab-states-find-themselves-allied-with-israel.html?_r=0) Hamas to be an Islamist threat that could destabilise their own countries. Iran's support and funding of Hamas has effectively made these nations prioritise the destruction of the group over the recognition of a Palestinian state.
1.4.1.4.7.2.2. Pro: The Gulf states [fear](http://www.huffingtonpost.com/samuel-ramani/why-israel-is-strengthening_b_11946660.html) Hamas' link with the Muslim Brotherhood, which they believe is backed by Iran.
1.4.1.4.7.3. Pro: In 2020, [four Arab League nations](https://foreignpolicy.com/2020/12/21/arab-ties-israel-diplomacy-normalization-middle-east/), the United Arab Emirates, Sudan, Bahrain, and Morocco, signed agreements to normalize ties with Israel.
1.4.1.4.7.3.1. Con: The 2020 agreements between Arab nations and Israel were less about the latter, or peace in the region, and more regarding the [benefits](https://foreignpolicy.com/2020/12/21/arab-ties-israel-diplomacy-normalization-middle-east/)(The decision by four Arab countries to forge ties with Israel in 2020 was not about peace, love, or understanding. The United Arab Emirates, Sudan, Morocco, and \(to a lesser extent\) Bahrain were all motivated by narrow interests—including the promise of either advanced weapons or diplomatic favors from the United States.), and political and militaristic favors offered by the United States.
1.4.1.5. Con: If the United States were to distance itself from Israel, this could be interpreted as abandoning a close ally. In turn, it could have severe repercussions for other close allies causing the interlinked system of alliances to suffer.
1.4.1.5.1. Con: Although the US and Israel share several close allies, it is possible for the US to denounce Israel for its actions while also reaffirming its relationships with other common allies.
1.4.1.5.1.1. Con: When the United States recognized China in the 1970s, this was perceived as a de-facto abandonment of Taiwan. Even though the US reaffirmed its commitment to other allies, several of them were shocked and opted for less reliance on America in their security affairs \([p. 710](http://www.theoverholtgroup.com/media/Articles-China/PresidentNixons-Trip-to-China-and-Its-Consequences-Asian-Survey-jstor.pdf)\).
1.4.1.5.1.2. Con: The US has consistently [reaffirmed](http://thehill.com/blogs/floor-action/senate/212617-senate-passes-resolution-in-support-of-israel) its [support](https://www.wsj.com/articles/in-speech-to-aipac-donald-trump-affirms-support-for-israel-1458605471) for Israel. A move like this would indicate that public US affirmations of support are worth little, and do not necessarily indicate underlying US policy.
1.4.1.5.2. Pro: [Trump's actions to undermine NATO](http://www.npr.org/2016/07/23/487151465/casting-doubt-on-u-s-commitment-to-mutual-defense-donald-trump-unsettles-nato-al) cast doubt on US loyalty and commitment to longstanding alliances. Betraying Israel by recognising Palestine would reinforce and deepen this distrust.
1.4.1.5.3. Pro: President Obama [doubled down](http://www.npr.org/templates/story/story.php?storyId=91150432) on an "unshakeable commitment to Israel's security." Recognizing Palestine could be interpreted as a weakening of this commitment to American allies.
1.4.1.5.3.1. Con: The US can recognise Palestine without compromising its commitment to Israel's security - defence pledges and aid deals will still remain.
1.4.2. Pro: Public opinion in the US supports this step: [more Americans](http://www.gallup.com/poll/189626/americans-views-toward-israel-remain-firmly-positive.aspx) support an independent Palestinian state than oppose it.
1.4.2.1. Con: [Two thirds of Americans](http://www.gallup.com/poll/189626/americans-views-toward-israel-remain-firmly-positive.aspx) sympathize more with Israel than with Palestine; only 15% think the other way around. This makes the recognition of Palestine against Israel's explicit preference hard to sell.
1.4.2.1.1. Pro: The public attitude towards Israel gives American politicians little incentive to support positions that run counter to Israeli interests. In fact, support for Israel has been labeled as "cheap talk," giving politicians large benefits with minimal risk \([p. 20](https://www.jstor.org/stable/pdf/10.2979/israelstudies.19.3.1.pdf)\).
1.4.2.1.2. Pro: The [vast majority](http://www.pewresearch.org/fact-tank/2016/05/23/5-facts-about-how-americans-view-the-israeli-palestinian-conflict/) of Republican voters sympathize more with Israel than with Palestine and do not consider a peaceful two-state solution viable. Politicians in Republican-dominated US politics have little to gain from defying this.
1.4.2.1.3. Con: Surveys indicate that the American public would be in support of less amicable and supportive relations with Israel.
1.4.2.1.3.1. Pro: Six out of ten Americans believe that the United States gives too much or even far too much foreign aid to Israel \([p. 6](https://www.irmep.org/09302014_USFATI.pdf)\).
1.4.2.1.3.2. Con: However, less amicable and supportive relations are not the same thing as unilaterally recognising Palestine at the expense of American-Israeli relations.
1.4.2.1.3.3. Pro: Almost half of all Americans support the unprecedented step of imposing sanctions on Israel in reaction to new settlements in Palestine \([p. 21](https://www.brookings.edu/wp-content/uploads/2016/12/cmep_20161202_public_opinion_poll.pdf)\).
1.4.2.1.4. Con: Sympathising with Israel is not mutually exclusive to establishing a Palestinian state. The American public can blame Hamas for its aggressive actions but still believe that the Palestinian people deserve a state.
1.4.2.1.5. Pro: In the same vein, only a very small minority [of 6%](https://www.brookings.edu/research/american-attitudes-on-the-israeli-palestinian-conflict/) would like to see the Trump government lean towards the Palestinian side in this conflict.
1.4.2.1.5.1. Con: This is only because the majority of voters want the Trump administration to lean towards [neither side](https://www.brookings.edu/research/american-attitudes-on-the-israeli-palestinian-conflict/), so this does not indicate a general attitude of support for Israel.
1.4.2.1.6. Pro: Almost half of all Americans - and a majority of Republican voters - believe that the Jewish people are God's chosen people. This makes policies perceived as going against Israeli interests hard to sell \([p. 9](https://www.brookings.edu/wp-content/uploads/2016/07/2015-Poll-Key-Findings-Final-1.pdf)\).
1.4.2.2. Con: While this is currently the case, [public support](http://www.gallup.com/poll/189626/americans-views-toward-israel-remain-firmly-positive.aspx) for Israel has been increasing, while support for a Palestinian state is decreasing; given that the current margin in favor of a Palestinian state is small, it is likely to disappear in the future.
1.4.2.2.1. Con: Policies are not based upon expected future voter preferences, but current voter preferences. Given that, the US should recognise Palestine as a state since a majority of the population supports it.
1.4.2.3. Pro: The US is one of the world's most influential actors. If it were to officially recognize Palestine, it could serve as a powerful source of inspiration for other allies and nations to push harder for an independent Palestinian state.
1.4.2.3.1. Pro: By being the first major Western country to [recognize](http://www.theperspective.se/?p=882) Palestine, Sweden led the way for a number of others, including France, the United Kingdom, and Spain to do the same. US recognition could have an even more significant impact, given its international reputation.
1.4.2.3.2. Con: The United States is too late to serve as an international role-model, given that [70.5%](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/International_recognition_of_the_State_of_Palestine) of nations already recognize Palestine.
1.4.2.3.3. Pro: American influence in Palestine is expanding; in 2021, President Biden moved to [restore relations with Palestinians](https://apnews.com/article/joe-biden-world-news-israel-united-nations-a5f546bf188f808ba29f381d76d44729) by reestablishing economic development and humanitarian aid programs.
1.4.2.3.3.1. Pro: The Biden administration made it clear that it supports a "[mutually agreed two-state solution](https://apnews.com/article/joe-biden-world-news-israel-united-nations-a5f546bf188f808ba29f381d76d44729)(“Under the new administration, the policy of the United States will be to support a mutually agreed two-state solution, one in which Israel lives in peace and security alongside a viable Palestinian state,” he said.\n\nMills said peace can’t be imposed on either side and stressed that progress and an ultimate solution require the participation and agreement of Israelis and Palestinians.)."
1.4.2.4. Con: The ignorance of the American people could cause them to support unethical policies that could do more harm than good.
1.4.2.4.1. Pro: Studies from the 1990s indicate that Americans are [less informed](http://journals.sagepub.com/doi/abs/10.1177/1081180X96001002003) about foreign policy issues and world affairs than citizens of major European countries and Canada.
1.4.2.4.2. Pro: Many Americans lack basic geographic knowledge about the world and especially the Middle East.
1.4.2.4.2.1. Con: Poor geographic knowledge does not necessarily translate into a lack of knowledge about the pertinent issues required to form informed opinions.
1.4.2.4.2.1.1. Con: The Israel-Palestine conflict is a battle over geographic territory. Thus, it is unlikely that the average American with limited geographic knowledge about the Middle East can form an informed opinion over the territory dispute.
1.4.2.4.2.2. Con: Most Americans cannot properly identify [US states](https://www.rferl.org/a/1068259.html) on a map. This does not mean that they should not have or share their opinions on current affairs happening in their own country.
1.4.2.4.2.3. Pro: Americans are bad at geography in general, not just when it comes to the Middle East, because their school [curricula](https://www.rferl.org/a/1068259.html)("Geography is not consistently taught in the United States, that's one of the problems," Garcia said. "Pretty much after the 7th grade here in the United States, geography isn't taught.") do not give this subject much importance.
1.4.2.4.2.4. Pro: In a [2016 survey of American college students](https://drive.google.com/file/d/0B2AUpoucQL4jQXhzOWt4QjBfMFk/view?resourcekey=0-uRyVrcvDjlY_IaOwzEc6rg)(p. 11), seven out of ten were unable to properly identify Israel, despite the fact that it was highlighted on a map along with three other Middle Eastern countries.
1.4.2.4.2.4.1. Pro: These numbers are persistent and represent not only students. As of 2006, three out of four Americans [couldn't locate Israel or Iran on a map](https://www.nationalgeographic.com/roper2006/pdf/FINALReport2006GeogLitsurvey.pdf)(p. 25) of the region. Two thirds couldn't find major theaters of US engagement like Iraq or major allies like Saudi Arabia.
1.4.2.4.2.4.2. Pro: Only half of the students were able to [pinpoint countries of major relevance](https://drive.google.com/file/d/0B2AUpoucQL4jQXhzOWt4QjBfMFk/view?resourcekey=0-uRyVrcvDjlY_IaOwzEc6rg)(p. 11) for US foreign policy like Iraq and Iran.
1.4.2.4.2.4.3. Pro: The map used in the survey had actually redrawn the border, removing the West Bank; the missing chunk should have been a strong clue as to which country was Israel.
1.4.2.4.3. Con: Nearly all Americans believe [foreign policy is important](https://www.cfr.org/news-releases/americans-lack-knowledge-international-issues-yet-consider-them-important-finds-new)(“More than 80 percent agree it is important to teach foreign policy in high school and nearly 90 percent agree it is important to do so in college.” \n \n“In addition, 70 percent of those polled agree that international issues affect their daily lives.” \n \n“Majorities of Americans think it is extremely or very important to teach geography in elementary and middle school, high school, and college.”) enough to be taught in high school or college.
1.4.2.4.4. Pro: Americans are particularly uninformed about the international aid provided by the US government.
1.4.2.4.4.1. Pro: [Only a third](https://scholar.harvard.edu/dtingley/publications/public-opinion-and-foreign-aid-review-essay)(p. 392) of Americans have ever heard of USAid, their country's own organization for international development. Even among college graduates this number only increases to 54%.
1.4.2.4.4.2. Pro: Only one in twenty Americans knows that the United States spends about [1% of its GDP on foreign aid](http://www.kff.org/global-health-policy/poll-finding/data-note-americans-views-on-the-u-s-role-in-global-health/); the average estimate is 26%.
1.4.2.4.5. Con: Greater knowledge about foreign policy issues is unlikely to change public opinion, which is often rooted in [sentiments](https://greatergood.berkeley.edu/article/item/why_is_it_so_hard_to_change_peoples_minds)(Our opinions are often based in emotion and group affiliation, not facts.) rather than facts.
1.4.2.5. Pro: [Two thirds](https://www.brookings.edu/research/american-attitudes-on-the-israeli-palestinian-conflict/) of all Americans - and even almost half of all Republican voters - believe America should either support or at least not block a UN resolution that recognizes Palestine as a state.
1.4.2.5.1. Pro: The US historical pattern of [vetoing nearly every UN Security Council resolution unfavorable to Israel](https://www.aljazeera.com/news/2021/5/19/a-history-of-the-us-blocking-un-resolutions-against-israel) demonstrates that even an abstention would be a de facto endorsement of the resolution.
1.4.2.6. Con: Even if citizens desire an action to be taken, it may not be ethical for a government to deliver it.
1.4.2.6.1. Pro: This is particularly true when the desired action entails interference in the affairs of other countries.
1.4.2.6.1.1. Con: Ironic, considering the United States is the [country that most interferes](https://www.usatoday.com/story/news/politics/elections/2020/09/04/u-s-interferes-more-elections-than-russia-meddling-author-says/5700657002/) with the internal affairs of other sovereign nations.
1.4.2.6.2. Con: Some governments are not motivated by ethical decision making; they are more concerned with optics and protecting their domestic priorities.
1.4.2.7. Pro: History makes it abundantly clear that [citizens](https://www.bbc.co.uk/bitesize/guides/zfj8xyc/revision/2) make social change possible by spurring the government to take action.
1.4.2.7.1. Pro: In 2019, citizens across [185 countries](https://www.theguardian.com/environment/2019/sep/21/across-the-globe-millions-join-biggest-climate-protest-ever)(In the estimated 185 countries where demonstrations took place, the protests often had their individual targets; from rising sea levels in the Solomon Islands, toxic waste in South Africa, to air pollution and plastic waste in India and coal expansion in Australia.\n\nBut the overall message was unified – a powerful demand for an urgent step-change in action to cut emissions and stabilise the climate.\n\nThe demonstrations took place on the eve of a UN climate summit, called by the secretary general, António Guterres, to inject urgency into government action to restrict the rise in global temperatures to 1.5C, as agreed under the 2015 Paris agreement.) came together to raise their voices and call for governmental action against climate change.
1.4.2.7.2. Pro: In the United States, changes in [public opinion](https://socialistworker.org/2017/06/14/how-our-protests-won-marriage-equality)(This sea change in popular consciousness put pressure on politicians and judges, altering altered the landscape in which legal campaigns were taking place.\n\nCourt battles were important to winning marriage equality, but it was the pressure from below, created by masses of ordinary people participating in a grassroots movement, that drove the struggle forward to victory.) toward the LGBTQ community preceded legislation that protected marriage equality.
1.4.2.7.3. Pro: In Ireland, abortion rights were secured largely as a result of [campaigns](https://medium.com/\@twmerrigan/ireland-abortion-rights-activism-referendum-constitution-c6cf02ed1b81) championed by women.
1.4.2.7.4. Con: Even if the desired changes are unequivocally desirable, ethical, and justified, the public may lack the depth and breadth of knowledge that the government possesses to foresee and mitigate the unanticipated adverse consequences that could result from hastily implementing the required changes.
1.4.2.7.4.1. Con: The government possessing knowledge does not always mean that they will act on it; sometimes public pressure is necessary for change to occur.
1.4.2.7.5. Con: Governments have taken admirable steps toward positive social change even when public opinion was unfavorable.
1.4.2.7.5.1. Pro: The racial [desegregation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_desegregation_busing_crisis) of schools was undertaken by the government despite brisk opposition from the public.
1.4.2.7.5.1.1. Pro: According to Howard Zinn, "[a radical historian](https://scholarworks.wmich.edu/cgi/viewcontent.cgi?article=3583&context=jssw)(We now have enough actual experience of social change in the South to say confidently that you first change the way people behave by legal or extralegal pressures of various kinds, in order to transform the environment which is the ultimate determinate of the way people think.)," by implementing changes that facilitate social progress, such as racial desegregation, governments can create positive changes in public attitudes \(pp. 44-45\).
1.4.2.7.5.1.2. Con: Desegregation amid [unfavorable public opinion](https://www.history.com/this-day-in-history/violence-in-boston-over-racial-busing)(In Boston, Massachusetts, opposition to court-ordered school “busing” turns violent on the opening day of classes. School buses carrying African American children were pelted with eggs, bricks, and bottles, and police in combat gear fought to control angry white protesters besieging the schools.) posed safety threats to Black children.
1.4.2.7.5.2. Pro: To help resolve the Mexican peso crisis, [President Clinton](https://www.politico.com/story/2019/01/31/this-day-in-politics-jan-31-1995-1129932)(Mexico repaid the loan three years ahead of schedule, along with $500 million in interest. This event was marked by a celebration at the White House on Jan. 16, 1997, presided over by Clinton and Robert Rubin, the Treasury secretary. The return of the funds also released Mexico from the tight economic controls that had been imposed by Washington.\n\n“Two years ago, helping our friend and neighbor in a time of need was quite controversial,” Clinton noted. “Some said that we should not get involved, that the money would never be repaid, that Mexico should fend for itself,” he added. “'They were wrong. Today, the American people can be proud that we did the right thing by Mexico and the right thing for the United States, and the right thing to protect global prosperity.”) loaned their neighbor country 20 billion USD. Although this move was met with sharp [criticism and disapproval](https://courses.lumenlearning.com/atd-baycollege-americangovernment/chapter/the-effects-of-public-opinion/)(In 1995, despite public opposition, Clinton guaranteed loans for the Mexican government to help the country out of financial insolvency. He followed this decision with many speeches to help the American public understand the importance of stabilizing Mexico’s economy.), the outcomes were positive for both the parties involved.
1.4.2.7.5.3. Con: In democracies, governments and representatives are elected based on the [majority vote](https://courses.lumenlearning.com/atd-baycollege-americangovernment/chapter/the-effects-of-public-opinion/)(Congress is likely to be aware of public opinion on issues. Representatives must continually raise campaign donations for bi-yearly elections. For this reason, they must keep their constituents and donors happy. Representatives are also likely to change their voting behavior if public opinion changes. Senators have a longer span between elections, which gives them time to make decisions independent of opinion and then make amends with their constituents. Changes in public opinion do not affect senators’ votes, but they do cause senators to lose reelection.). Therefore, it is unlikely that elected governments will make decisions that are diametrically opposed to those of the public.
1.4.2.7.5.4. Con: Resistance and backlash from dissenters can cause governments to backtrack their decisions. Such a move can be detrimental to the concerned parties, which is what happened with the [recriminalization of homosexuality](https://timesofindia.indiatimes.com/india/supreme-court-makes-homosexuality-a-crime-again/articleshow/27230690.cms) in India.
1.4.2.7.6. Pro: Informed citizens are able to [improve policy-making](https://www.centreforpublicimpact.org/insights/citizen-views-better-policymaking); politicians enact policies that reflect public pressure and actually improve lives and society at large.
1.4.2.7.7. Con: The [government](https://courses.lumenlearning.com/atd-baycollege-americangovernment/chapter/the-effects-of-public-opinion/), especially the judicial branch, should be neutral and objective, rather than giving in to public opinion.
1.4.2.7.7.1. Pro: In [2020](https://www.hks.harvard.edu/faculty-research/policy-topics/democracy-governance/us-supreme-court-v-american-public-opinion), all major SCOTUS decisions were in line with public opinion, indicating that it is in some way adherent to social expectations.
1.4.3. Con: Recognition may improve Palestinian perceptions of the US, but it will alienate Israel - a US ally.
1.4.3.1. Con: Israel is far too [dependent](http://www.belfercenter.org/publication/israels-dependence-united-states-existential) on the US to destroy relations.
1.4.3.1.1. Pro: Israel's trade is [highly dependent](http://atlas.media.mit.edu/en/profile/country/isr/#Destinations) on the United States: 37% of its exports go to America, 14% of its imports come from there. No other country plays an equivalent role for Israel's trade.
1.4.3.1.1.1. Pro: In fact, Israel exports [more](http://atlas.media.mit.edu/en/visualize/tree_map/hs92/export/isr/show/all/2015/) to the United States than to its eleven next largest trade partners combined.
1.4.3.1.2. Pro: No other country sends as many tourists to Israel as the United States; American tourists make up [one quarter](https://www.csmonitor.com/1983/0615/061543.html)(''Tourism is the primary source of foreign currency for Israel,'' explains Geoffrey Weill, director of public relations at the Israel Ministry of Tourism office in New York. And he adds, ''While Americans make up a quarter of our tourist traffic, they contribute one-third of the dollars.'') of all tourism arrivals in Israel and contribute to one-third of tourism revenue.
1.4.3.1.2.1. Con: [Twenty-eight UN member states](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/International_recognition_of_Israel#Present_situation) do not recognize Israel and do not permit their citizens to enter the country, limiting the number of people that can actually visit Israel.
1.4.3.1.2.2. Con: The US is [one of the most populous countries](https://www.worldometers.info/world-population/population-by-country/) in the world; the number of arriving tourists is bound to be high in any country visited by Americans.
1.4.3.1.2.3. Pro: In the past, American tourists have [shunned](http://www.cbsnews.com/news/us-tourism-to-france-perks-up/) countries they perceived to act in opposition to US interests.
1.4.3.1.2.3.1. Con: A variety of [religious and cultural sites](https://www.washingtonpost.com/news/acts-of-faith/wp/2017/12/06/questions-about-jerusalem-you-were-afraid-to-ask/) in Israel are important to Christians, Jews, and Muslims; many Americans will have [reasons](https://www.npr.org/2019/08/22/753493910/tourism-to-israel-is-on-the-rise-with-more-u-s-evangelical-christians-visiting?t=1638883243770) to visit Israel regardless of U.S. official policies.
1.4.3.1.3. Con: [Israel's status as a nuclear power](http://www.rense.com/general26/historw.htm) allows the country to be independent of the whims of major powers like the United States.
1.4.3.1.3.1. Con: Nuclear weapon use is [strictly regulated, if not prohibited](https://www.un.org/disarmament/wmd/nuclear/tpnw/), under most circumstances. At best, they are effective deterrents against states, not terrorist organizations like Hamas and Hezbollah, which are Israel's main threats.
1.4.3.1.4. Con: Israel has a [large conventional arms industry](http://www.spiegel.de/international/world/defense-industry-the-business-of-war-in-israel-a-988245.html). As a result, Israel's security is not dependent on good relations with the US.
1.4.3.1.4.1. Pro: Israel's defense industry is actually [undermined by US aid](http://forward.com/news/breaking-news/350424/israel-arms-industry-sees-big-hit-from-buy-american-provisions-in-38b-aid-d/) which forces it to "buy American". By restricting the amount that can be spent domestically, Israel's defence industry faces layoffs and closures.
1.4.3.1.4.2. Pro: Dependence on US aid has [institutionalized](https://townhall.com/columnists/jeffjacoby/2016/09/05/israel-doesnt-need-american-foreign-aid-n2213875) Israeli reliance on air power and ever-more-advanced technology, at the expense of focusing more intensively on ground maneuvers and the unique threat posed by enemies waging asymmetric warfare. Israel would be better off without this aid.
1.4.3.1.5. Pro: Israel receives a significant portion of its GDP in [foreign aid](https://www.bbc.co.uk/news/57170576) from the United States.
1.4.3.1.5.1. Con: Israel can hardly be said to be militarily dependent on the US.
