Even excluding America's military aid, it spends [one and a half times](https://www.sipri.org/databases/milex) as much on its military than all of its neighbors combined; the share of its GDP that it spends on the military is [the highest](https://www.sipri.org/sites/default/files/Trends-world-military-expenditure-2016.pdf) among all the world's major armies \(p. 2\).
1.4.3.1.5.2. Con: Israel's dependency is shrinking. Whereas the size of its economy [has tripled](http://data.worldbank.org/country/israel) over the last two decades, the size of aid payments has stayed the same. The [share](https://fas.org/sgp/crs/mideast/RL33476.pdf)(pg.23) of US aid among Israel's GDP thus sunk from about 3% to 1%.
1.4.3.1.5.3. Pro: U.S. military aid for Israel has been designed to maintain Israel’s “[qualitative military edge](https://fas.org/sgp/crs/mideast/RL33222.pdf)(pg.1)” \(QME\) over neighbouring militaries. This is vital to its regional security.
1.4.3.1.5.4. Pro: US aid accounts for [20% of Israel's defence budget and 40% of the IDF budget](http://www.belfercenter.org/publication/israels-dependence-united-states-existential). Israel is therefore heavily dependent on the US to maintain its defences.
1.4.3.1.6. Pro: The US supports Israel diplomatically, allowing it more freedom than unsupported states.
1.4.3.1.6.1. Pro: The US has repeatedly voted against all other members of the UN Security Council, vetoing resolutions that would have criticized Israel, including those on [settlement](https://unispal.un.org/DPA/DPR/unispal.nsf/0/F97C162F6A30647205256531005B4E15) [expansions](http://www.securitycouncilreport.org/un-documents/document/IP%20S2011%2024.php), [assassinations](http://www.securitycouncilreport.org/un-documents/document/IP%202004%20240.php), violating the [Geneva Convention](https://unispal.un.org/DPA/DPR/unispal.nsf/5ba47a5c6cef541b802563e000493b8c/b35c281bef2fa8f00525651b003675d3?OpenDocument), attacking UN supplies, [and killing UN workers](https://unispal.un.org/DPA/DPR/unispal.nsf/0/87CD207B928B40D885256C950067EF41).
1.4.3.1.6.2. Pro: Damaging its relationship with the US would isolate Israel in the international community. This isolation could set in motion a [diplomatic avalanche](http://www.timesofisrael.com/left-alone-at-un-israel-can-ignore-but-not-avoid-diplomatic-fallout/) that will ultimately weaken Israel’s position in negotiations with the Palestinians.
1.4.3.1.6.2.1. Con: Israel's diplomatic position is quite strong following the [Abraham Accords](https://www.state.gov/the-abraham-accords/); these opened up trade with previously hostile neighbours and cemented Israel as a regional power player.
1.4.3.1.6.3. Pro: The United States has adopted a "[don't ask, don't tell](http://www.80bola.com.nuclearfiles.org/menu/key-issues/nuclear-weapons/issues/proliferation/israel/Israel%20crosses%20the%20threshold.pdf)" attitude towards Israel's nuclear program - a privilege which no other officially non-nuclear state enjoys.
1.4.3.1.6.3.1. Pro: Without tacit American acquiescence, the international community might call into question Israel's nuclear program and attempt to pressure the country into signing the Nuclear Non Proliferation Treaty.
1.4.3.1.6.3.1.1. Pro: There has been [international pressure](http://www.jpost.com/Middle-East/Israel-Under-Pressure-To-Give-Up-Chemical-Nuclear-Weapons-326452) on Israel to give up its nuclear weapons - without the support of the US, this international pressure may increase and force Israel to give up its nuclear weapons.
1.4.3.1.6.3.1.2. Con: The outsized [power](http://www.yourarticlelibrary.com/international-politics/impact-of-nuclear-weapons-on-international-relations/48526/) that any nuclear power has in international relations would likely continue to insulate Israel from any pressures to end their nuclear weapons program.
1.4.3.1.6.4. Con: American diplomatic support for Israel has [never been unequivocal](https://sethfrantzman.com/2016/12/24/abstaining-from-history-heres-all-the-un-resolutions-on-israel-the-us-abstained-on/). The US has supported, abstained from and vetoed UN resolutions criticizing Israel in the past.
1.4.3.1.6.4.1. Con: Until December 2016, out of 226 UN Security Council resolutions related to Israel since 1948, the US has [abstained](https://sethfrantzman.com/2016/12/24/abstaining-from-history-heres-all-the-un-resolutions-on-israel-the-us-abstained-on/) from less than two dozen of them. It has only voted against Israel a handful of times.
1.4.3.1.6.4.2. Con: Even when the US was supposed to play a neutral role - for example during the negotiations of the Oslo Accords in 1993 and in Camp David in 2000 - it de-facto [sided with Israel](https://www.lrb.co.uk/v28/n06/john-mearsheimer/the-israel-lobby).
1.4.3.1.7. Con: It would be politically unviable for the US to completely cut off its aid to Israel, as [most US voters](http://www.gallup.com/poll/189626/americans-views-toward-israel-remain-firmly-positive.aspx) are staunchly pro-Israel, or would oppose cutting off aid. Given this, Israel still has plenty of room to be intransigent and aggressive in reaction to the recognition of Israel.
1.4.3.1.7.1. Con: Israel could be made to feel its dependence on the United States even without a complete cut-off of relations. In 2004, the American government [threatened](http://www.meforum.org/926/at-what-cost-israel-china-ties) to exclude Israel from the F-35 jet program, reducing its capacity to update its jets.
1.4.3.1.7.2. Con: [46%](https://www.brookings.edu/research/american-attitudes-on-the-israeli-palestinian-conflict/) of Americans support imposing sanctions on Israel in response to settlement-building.
1.4.3.1.7.3. Pro: American citizens' views of Israel have remained steadily positive since [2001](http://www.gallup.com/poll/189626/americans-views-toward-israel-remain-firmly-positive.aspx), despite occasional Israel aggression against Palestine. While many might think some sanctions are acceptable, cutting off aid completely would likely be a step too far in the eyes of pro-Israel Americans.
1.4.3.2. Pro: Israel tends to [respond harshly](http://www.independent.co.uk/news/world/middle-east/un-security-council-vote-resolution-settlements-west-bank-east-jerusalem-israel-netanyahu-a7493996.html) when the international community moves against it, which could cause problems for the US.
1.4.3.2.1. Pro: Recognising a Palestine which does not accept Israel as a Jewish state could cause Israel to lash out and accuse the United States of tacit support for anti-Semitism.
1.4.3.2.2. Con: If the United States were to recognize Palestine, it is unlikely that Israel would position itself against not only the majority of the international community but also its most important ally by becoming more aggressive towards Palestine.
1.4.3.2.2.1. Pro: If America were to recognize Palestine, it would defy its close ally's interests whilst also refusing to act against the interests of other countries it is less invested in economically and diplomatically. This would seem unfair.
1.4.3.2.2.1.1. Pro: The USA [publically supports](https://www.dailymail.co.uk/news/article-2831586/We-not-favor-independence-President-Barack-Obama-reiterates-U-S-position-Tibet-China.html) the Chinese annexation of Tibet.
1.4.3.2.2.1.2. Pro: Out of respect to India, the US [does not recognize](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kashmir_conflict#United_States_positions_on_the_Kashmir_conflict) the independence of Kashmir even though it is far less invested in diplomatic ties with them than with Israel.
1.4.3.2.3. Pro: Recognition of a Palestinian state prior to an agreement undermines existing negotiations between the Palestinians and Israelis. This will likely alienate Israel from any discussions of a two-state solution.
1.4.3.2.3.1. Pro: If the US recognises the Palestinian state, Israel could be provoked to act aggressively against Palestine, which could result in worsened conditions for Palestinians.
1.4.3.2.3.1.1. Con: Palestine does not pose a [military threat](https://imeu.org/article/comparison-of-millitary-strength-of-israel-and-the-palestinians) to Israel, so the need for aggressive action is minimal, if not non-existent.
1.4.3.2.3.1.1.1. Con: While Palestine does not possess the military capacity to destroy Israel, the threat of terrorist attacks and mortar fire from groups such as Hamas still exists.
1.4.3.2.3.1.1.1.1. Pro: -> See 1.1.4.5.1.3.
1.4.3.2.3.1.1.1.2. Pro: In one study, more than one-third of Israelis reported [prior exposure to terrorism](https://www.iirp.edu/images/conf_downloads/sXYpZw_Mally_-_Shechory_Bitton_and_Esther_Friedman_final.pdf)(Table 1.3), and about half had a relative who had previously been exposed to terrorist attacks. Such experiences may account for self-reported fear of terrorism among Israeli participants, particularly when compared to Swedish participants.
1.4.3.2.3.1.1.1.2.1. Con: In the cited study, the [correlation](https://www.iirp.edu/images/conf_downloads/sXYpZw_Mally_-_Shechory_Bitton_and_Esther_Friedman_final.pdf)(p. 10) between prior exposure to terrorist attacks and fear of terrorism was statistically non-significant.
1.4.3.2.3.1.1.2. Con: Though Palestine may not currently pose a military threat to Israel, they still [consider](http://www.mintpressnews.com/palestinian-statehood-poses-threat-israel/200249/) Palestine to be an inherent threat to their own existence. Because Israel fears Palestine, they could feel it vital to strike against Palestine before they become strong enough to pose an actual military threat.
1.4.3.2.3.1.1.3. Pro: Unlike Israel, [Palestine](https://imeu.org/article/comparison-of-millitary-strength-of-israel-and-the-palestinians) has no air force, navy, tanks, nuclear, chemical, or biological weapons, ballistic missiles, or space technology.
1.4.3.2.3.1.2. Pro: Recognition would constitute a big step towards increasing Palestine's chances to become an independent state. Israel does not want this to happen and would want to prevent this while it's still possible.
1.4.3.2.3.1.2.1. Pro: Recognition of Palestine has prompted retaliation from Israel in the past.
1.4.3.2.3.1.2.1.1. Pro: Israel suspended a payment of [$127 million](https://www.amnestyusa.org/press-releases/retaliation-against-palestines-welcome-accession-to-icc-must-stop/) due to the Palestinian authorities, as a response to Palestine's accession to the ICC a day after the statute was signed.
1.4.3.2.3.1.2.1.2. Pro: In response to the UN's recognition of Palestine, Israel confiscated [£75 million](http://www.telegraph.co.uk/news/worldnews/middleeast/israel/9717397/Israel-exacts-retaliation-for-Palestinian-statehood-vote-as-it-confiscates-75m-in-revenue.html) that it was supposed to pay Palestine and announced that it would build 3000 new settlers' home in areas that the Palestinians had earmarked as part of a future state.
1.4.3.2.3.1.2.2. Pro: By many accounts, the current PM, Bennett has an [even stronger](https://www.aljazeera.com/news/2021/6/17/will-bennett-be-worse-than-bibi) anti-Palestine rhetoric than his predecessor. US recognition of Palestine would increase their threat to Israel, which would be followed by harsher sanctions against Palestine, thereby gaining Bennett more support from voters.
1.4.3.2.3.1.2.2.1. Pro: The [rally-round-the-flag](http://www.jstor.org.proxy.mah.se/stable/3649343?Search=yes&resultItemClick=true&searchText=anatomy&searchText=of&searchText=a&searchText=rally&searchText=effect:&searchText=George&searchText=W&searchText=Bush&searchUri=%2Faction%2FdoBasicSearch%3Fwc%3Don%26amp%3Bacc%3Don%26amp%3Bprq%3Danatomy%2Bof%2Bthe%2Brally%2Beffect%26amp%3Bfc%3Doff%26amp%3BQuery%3Danatomy%2Bof%2Ba%2Brally%2Beffect%253A%2BGeorge%2BW%2BBush%26amp%3Bso%3Drel%26amp%3Bhp%3D25&refreqid=search%3Af88037627ed90e32fb48fe293779dc21&seq=1#page_scan_tab_contents) effect is a sudden increase in approval ratings following periods of international crisis or war. Though often applied to [US presidents](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rally_%27round_the_flag_effect), a leader of Israel could gain support from more patriotic voters, should they attack Palestine.
1.4.3.2.3.1.3. Con: Israel has fought at least three wars in Palestine in the last decade and regularly conducts air and artillery [strikes](https://www.bbc.co.uk/news/world-middle-east-57138996) against Gaza. It is difficult to see how they could act more aggressively.
1.4.3.2.3.2. Pro: The Israeli government has [emphasized in the past](https://www.alaraby.co.uk/english/news/2016/11/7/israel-rejects-french-peace-initiative-again), and the Israeli public has stated in [surveys](http://www.pcpsr.org/sites/default/files/Table%20of%20Findings_English%20Joint%20Poll%20Dec%202016_12Feb2017.pdf)(pg.7), that the preferred method of engaging with the Palestinians is through bilateral talks. Thus, the involvement of and pressure from third actors will likely be received negatively.
1.4.3.2.3.2.1. Con: Recognition does not constitute involvement in the talks. Thus, it is fully compatible with bilateral talks between Israel and Palestine.
1.4.3.2.3.3. Pro: The right wing establishment in Israel is thoroughly [opposed](https://www.i24news.tv/en/news/israel/diplomacy-defense/137396-170211-minister-says-israel-faces-historic-opportunity-to-nix-two-state-solution) to the creation of a Palestinian state. Unilateral action by the US will likely push it further away.
1.4.3.2.3.4. Con: US recognition of Palestine might get Israel back to the negotiation table by [signaling disapproval](https://www.brookings.edu/blog/order-from-chaos/2021/06/11/america-must-rethink-its-unique-and-contradictory-advocacy-of-israels-jewishness/) of current Israeli policies on the peace process. This can encourage the Israeli public to [question its government's stance](https://www.vox.com/2014/7/24/5929705/us-israel-friends), as that is leading to increasing [international isolation](https://www.globaltimes.cn/page/202105/1223731.shtml).
1.4.3.2.4. Con: Israel is already largely isolated in international public opinion, but so far has not seen this as a reason to change its policies.
1.4.3.2.4.1. Pro: -> See 1.4.1.1.1.
1.4.3.2.4.2. Pro: Israel has few other allies and is generally not seen favourably abroad. In the [BBC's 2013 popularity ranking](http://www.bbc.com/news/world-europe-22624104), it is on one of the last ranks, just ahead of North Korea.
1.4.3.2.5. Pro: Israel [previously](https://www.independent.co.uk/news/world/middle-east/un-security-council-vote-resolution-settlements-west-bank-east-jerusalem-israel-netanyahu-retaliatory-measures-new-zealand-senegal-a7493996.html) reacted poorly when the UN condemned settlements; ambassadors were withdrawn from every country that voted in favour of the resolution.
1.4.3.3. Pro: US recognition of Palestine would require [800,000](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Population_statistics_for_Israeli_settlements_in_the_West_Bank) Israelis to withdraw from the West Bank and cost Israel a vast some of money, given that the evacuation of 8,000 settlers from Gaza cost Israel [$9 billion](https://www.haaretz.com/1.4916471). This expense would have major ramifications for diplomacy between the two nations.
1.4.3.3.1. Pro: Elsewhere, the cost of resettlement of 100,000 settlers in Israel has been estimated to be [around $10 billion](https://www.timesofisrael.com/billions-spent-on-settlements-since-israel-captured-west-bank/). Since the total number of settlers is multiple times of that, resettling all of them would cost enormous amounts of money.
1.4.3.3.2. Con: The problem could be mitigated by land swaps through which Israel keeps territory with major settlements.
1.4.3.3.2.1. Pro: Independent proposals based on the situation in 2011 estimate that swaps involving merely 5% of Palestinian territory and no dislocation of Palestinians could bring about 80% of settlers onto Israeli territory \([p. 11](https://www.inss.org.il/wp-content/uploads/2019/01/2-2011-Imagining-the-Border-options-for-resolving-the-Israeli-Palestinian-Territorial-Issue-David-Makovsky-3-11.pdf)\).
1.4.3.3.2.1.1. Pro: In order to reduce the amount of territory annexed by Israel, other options would exchange a mere [3.7% of Palestinian territory](https://www.inss.org.il/wp-content/uploads/2019/01/2-2011-Imagining-the-Border-options-for-resolving-the-Israeli-Palestinian-Territorial-Issue-David-Makovsky-3-11.pdf)(p. 11) and still be able to bring almost 70% of settlers onto Israeli territory.
1.4.3.3.2.1.2. Con: There has been considerable expansion of settlements since 2011, and more [constructions of settlements](https://www.theguardian.com/world/2017/jan/24/israel-announces-2500-more-west-bank-settlement-homes) promised by the current government. This renders plans based on the situation in 2011 irrelevant.
1.4.3.3.2.1.3. Pro: [Almost 80%](https://www.washingtonpost.com/news/worldviews/wp/2014/12/22/map-the-spread-of-israeli-settlements-in-the-west-bank/?utm_term=.e3d69a333cee) of settlers live within the Israeli [West Bank barrier](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israeli_West_Bank_barrier), which could be used as a line to mark areas for land swaps.
1.4.3.3.2.1.3.1. Con: The Israeli West Bank Barrier is [illegal](http://www.reuters.com/article/us-palestinians-israel-barrier-idUSL0714340920080707) under international law, built on Palestinian territory, and an arbitrarily defined border. There is no reason why this barrier should be used as the border to decide land swaps.
1.4.3.3.2.1.3.2. Con: It is unlikely that Palestinians would be willing to accept this barrier - which they oftentimes refer to as an "[apartheid wall](https://web.archive.org/web/20080307023217/http://news.bbc.co.uk/newswatch/ukfs/hi/newsid_6040000/newsid_6044000/6044090.stm)" - as a permanent border.
1.4.3.3.2.1.4. Con: Land swaps will mean some Palestinians will either end up living in Israel, where they are likely to face [discrimination](https://www.adalah.org/uploads/oldfiles/upfiles/2011/Adalah_The_Inequality_Report_March_2011.pdf)(p. 13), or they will be forced to relocate, which is unfair towards them.
1.4.3.3.2.1.4.1. Con: A number of [independent plans](https://www.inss.org.il/wp-content/uploads/2019/01/2-2011-Imagining-the-Border-options-for-resolving-the-Israeli-Palestinian-Territorial-Issue-David-Makovsky-3-11.pdf)(pp. 7-9) for land swaps have been proposed under which no Palestinian villages would be annexed and no Palestinians displaced.
1.4.3.3.2.1.4.2. Pro: Even if land swaps were fair and would put an end to all settlements, a [solid majority](http://www.pcpsr.org/sites/default/files/Table%20of%20Findings_English%20Joint%20Poll%20Dec%202016_12Feb2017.pdf)(p. 3) \(65.4%\) of Palestinians oppose the idea.
1.4.3.3.2.2. Pro: [About half](http://www.pcpsr.org/en/node/678) of all Israelis support in principle the idea of land swaps to retain Israeli control over territory with major settlements.
1.4.3.3.2.3. Con: The sheer number of settlements, as well as the distribution throughout almost the [entirety of the West Bank](https://www.washingtonpost.com/news/worldviews/wp/2014/12/22/map-the-spread-of-israeli-settlements-in-the-west-bank/?utm_term=.4c135f3b8781), would make this an incredibly difficult task.
1.4.3.3.2.3.1. Pro: In Gaza, only about 8,500 Jewish settlers had to be relocated. In contrast, the number of settlers in West Bank who would need to be relocated is about [50 times greater](https://www.reuters.com/article/us-israel-gaza-disengagement-insight-idUSKCN0QF1QQ20150810).
1.4.3.3.2.3.2. Con: In 2013, the Arab League [endorsed](https://www.dawn.com/news/1025928/arab-league-moderates-stance-supports-land-swaps) the idea of mutually agreed-upon land swaps indicating that, though difficult, land swaps are possible.
1.4.3.3.2.4. Con: Land swaps are simply a negotiating tactic used by Israelis to [legitimise](http://www.aljazeera.com/indepth/features/2017/03/israel-false-narrative-land-swaps-170312095110936.html) the ongoing expansion of settlements.
1.4.3.3.2.5. Con: The only land swap map put forward by Israel so far [prejudices](http://www.aljazeera.com/palestinepapers/2011/01/2011122114239940577.html) Palestinian contiguity, water aquifers, and the viability of Palestine. Mutually agreeable land swaps are likely to be impossible.
1.4.3.3.2.5.1. Pro: Israeli Arabs have [previously](https://www.aljazeera.com/indepth/features/2014/01/israeli-arabs-reject-proposed-land-swap-2014112142628945331.html) [refused](https://www.jns.org/israeli-arabs-reject-becoming-citizens-of-palestinian-state-as-suggested-in-mideast-peace-plan/) land swaps as they oppose being transferred under Palestinian authority.
1.4.3.3.2.5.2. Pro: Palestinian authorities and communities have rejected land swaps on numerous occasions in the past.
1.4.3.3.2.5.2.1. Pro: Mahmoud Abbas of the Palestinian Authority has [stated](https://www.inss.org.il/wp-content/uploads/2019/01/2-2011-Imagining-the-Border-options-for-resolving-the-Israeli-Palestinian-Territorial-Issue-David-Makovsky-3-11.pdf)(p. 6) that land swaps must be based on land of equal size and value, yet Israel still hasn't committed to this principle. This alone dooms the possibility of agreeing on land swaps.
1.4.3.3.2.5.2.2. Pro: Hamas has declared its [opposition](http://jfjfp.com/?p=42804) to land swaps.
1.4.3.3.2.5.3. Con: In the 2000 Camp David peace talks, both sides [agreed](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2000_Camp_David_Summit#Territory) to a solution: adjusting pre-1967 borders so that the largest settlements are under Israel's control in exchange for more land for Palestine elsewhere. Withdrawal from other, much smaller settlements was considered to, consequently, be easy.
1.4.3.4. Con: The United States would not lose much by alienating Israel.
1.4.3.4.1. Con: Israel is a [prolific](https://www.sipri.org/research/armament-and-disarmament/arms-transfers-and-military-spending/arms-production) exporters of arms. In the past, the US was able to influence the targets of these exports, for example by blocking sales [to China](http://www.washingtonpost.com/wp-dyn/content/article/2005/06/27/AR2005062700351.html). If this leverage was lost, the US could be vulnerable.
1.4.3.4.2. Pro: Even if the US were to alienate Israel, they may spend less on aid, freeing up funds that the US could spend elsewhere.
1.4.3.4.2.1. Pro: The US has spent almost $100 billion on Foreign Military Financing \(FMF\) since 1985 \([p. 22](https://fas.org/sgp/crs/mideast/RL33476.pdf)\).
1.4.3.4.2.1.1. Con: [FMF payments](https://www.dsca.mil/foreign-military-financing-fmf) are meant to enable foreign governments to purchase American military products and services. The money therefore comes back home and supports the US economy.
1.4.3.4.2.1.2. Pro: Israel is allowed to convert about a quarter of FMF military aid into shekels to spend at home \([p. 2](https://fas.org/sgp/crs/mideast/RL33222.pdf)\). Such expenditure therefore does not wholly benefit the US.
1.4.3.4.2.1.2.1. Con: The FMF provision that allows Israel to spend 26% of military aid domestically is being [phased out](http://www.cnbc.com/2016/09/15/big-us-military-aid-package-to-israel-has-strings-attached.html), requiring Israel to spend all military aid within the US by 2021.
1.4.3.4.3. Pro: Israel is not a top partner for the US.
1.4.3.4.3.1. Pro: Israel is not even among the [top-20](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_the_largest_trading_partners_of_the_United_States) of America's trade partners measured in trade volume.
1.4.3.4.3.2. Pro: Israel is not even among the [top 20](http://travel.trade.gov/view/m-2016-I-001/index.asp) in terms of the national origins of tourists visiting the United States. Countries of comparable size, like Sweden and Switzerland, outrank it.
1.4.3.4.3.3. Pro: 37% of Americans believe that Israel has too much influence on their politics; a portion significant enough to influence geopolitical decision-making \([p. 4](https://www.brookings.edu/wp-content/uploads/2016/07/2015-Poll-Key-Findings-Final-1.pdf)\).
1.4.3.4.3.4. Con: In a [Republican-dominated](https://www.theguardian.com/us-news/2020/dec/15/gerrymandering-republicans-map-charts-states) era of US politics, the opinions of Republican voters are most influential. The majority of them believe that Israel has the right amount of influence \([p. 4](https://www.brookings.edu/wp-content/uploads/2016/07/2015-Poll-Key-Findings-Final-1.pdf)\).
1.4.3.5. Pro: A deterioration in Israel-US relations will jeopardize America's operations and presence in the region.
1.4.3.5.1. Pro: The US [relies](http://www.jewishvirtuallibrary.org/u-s-israel-intelligence-collaboration) on Israel for crucial intelligence about Hamas, Hezbollah, and al-Qaeda and its affiliate groups in the region \([p. 11](https://cdn.cfr.org/sites/default/files/pdf/2011/10/Israel_strategic_US_assest_report.pdf)\). Deterioration of relations could put this intelligence cooperation at risk.
1.4.3.5.1.1. Con: Al-Qaeda is [no longer](http://www.cbc.ca/news/world/al-qaeda-irrelevant-since-bin-laden-s-death-1.1165060) a relevant threat to the US.
1.4.3.5.1.1.1. Con: Even if al-Qaeda as an organization may have become irrelevant, the ideology, attitudes, and recruiting tactics that underlie it persist in [other organizations](https://www.brookings.edu/testimonies/comparing-al-qaeda-and-isis-different-goals-different-targets/), such as ISIS.
1.4.3.5.1.1.2. Pro: Jihadist terrorist attacks against US targets \(abroad and domestic\) by ISIS and al-Qaeda have [drastically declined](https://www.newamerica.org/international-security/reports/terrorism-america-18-years-after-911/what-is-the-threat-to-the-united-states/) since their peak in 2015.
1.4.3.5.1.1.3. Pro: By many accounts, the biggest security threat to the United States is [white supremacy](https://www.newamerica.org/international-security/reports/terrorism-america-18-years-after-911/what-is-the-threat-to-the-united-states/)(The most likely threat to the United States comes from terrorists inspired by a mixture of ideologies including jihadist, far-right, and idiosyncratic strains, radicalized on or via the internet, and taking advantage of the availability of weapons, particularly semi-automatic firearms, in the United States. While ISIS’ inspirational power has lessened in recent years, white supremacist extremism is increasingly inspiring deadly violence.).
1.4.3.5.1.1.4. Con: While ISIS is a bigger threat to US interests overseas, al-Qaeda is [still a relevant threat](https://www.brookings.edu/testimonies/comparing-al-qaeda-and-isis-different-goals-different-targets/)(Al Qaeda and its affiliates remain a threat to the U.S. homeland, while the Islamic State’s danger is more to the stability of the Middle East and U.S. interests overseas. Much of their rivalry involves a competition for affiliates, with both trying to spread their model and in Al Qaeda’s case to ensure its operational relevance. For now the Islamic State’s focus is primarily on Iraq and Syria and to a lesser degree on other states in the Muslim world, particularly Libya. In the United States and in Europe it may inspire “lone wolves,” but it is not directing its resources to attack in these areas, and security services are prepared for the threat. Al Qaeda is weaker and less dynamic than the Islamic State, but the former remains more focused on attacking the United States and its Western allies.) to the US homeland.
1.4.3.5.1.1.4.1. Pro: Al-Qaeda's hatred of the US and their demonstrated willingness to commit terror attacks makes them inherently dangerous, regardless of its current state. As long as al-Qaeda exists, it could return to relevancy and threaten the US again.
1.4.3.5.1.1.4.1.1. Pro: Al-Qaeda has begun to build affiliate networks and [branches in Arab Africa](https://www.bbc.co.uk/news/world-asia-48056433), carrying out attacks across the continent and demonstrating that they are still a very relevant threat to the world.
1.4.3.5.1.1.4.1.2. Con: Since the 9/11 attack, the US has developed adequate [capabilities to predict and ensure](https://www.nytimes.com/2021/04/13/us/politics/afghanistan-terrorism-threat.html)(No one can predict whether Al Qaeda will bounce back or how quickly. But some officials believe that the United States is unlikely to be caught unaware of a renewed Qaeda threat, pointing to U.S. counterterrorism capabilities and intelligence collection built up over the past two decades.) national security, regardless of the level of threat al-Qaeda poses.
1.4.3.5.1.2. Con: Intelligence about Hamas and Hezbollah is of relevance for the US only insofar as it helps to protect Israel. Neither organization targets America.
1.4.3.5.2. Con: Countries like Saudi Arabia, Egypt, Qatar, Kuwait or the UAE find it difficult to [side with the US](https://www.wsj.com/articles/SB116433750279531793) publicly on Iran unless "Washington pressures Israel on a peace initiative". If anything, recognition increases regional cooperation with the US.
1.4.3.5.2.1. Con: The US is [seeking](http://www.timesofisrael.com/us-looks-to-form-arab-alliance-against-iran-report/) to form an anti-Iran coalition with Arab states that would share intelligence with Israel as well. A peace deal is not required for Arab nations to cooperate with the US when their interests align.
1.4.3.5.2.2. Con: The US already [shares intelligence](http://www.reuters.com/article/us-usa-saudi-yemen-exclusive-idUSKBN0N129W20150411) and [sells weapons](http://www.reuters.com/article/us-usa-saudi-defense-congress-idUSKCN11R2LU) to Saudi Arabia, independent of the situation in Palestine. Regional cooperation and a Palestinian peace deal are not linked.
1.4.3.5.2.3. Con: Saudi Arabia, Qatar and the UAE have a strong anti-Iran position [due to sectarian tensions](http://www.spiegel.de/international/world/saudia-arabia-iran-and-the-new-middle-eastern-cold-war-a-1090725.html). The US does not need to pressure them for support.
1.4.3.5.3. Con: Israel has [no US military bases](http://www.politico.com/magazine/story/2015/06/us-military-bases-around-the-world-119321), whereas other regional players with poor historic relations with Israel do. A deterioration in the Israeli-US relationship would not affect US' capacity to project power regionally.
1.4.3.5.3.1. Con: Israel might not have any US military bases but they certainly have [US civilians joining their military](https://www.thedailybeast.com/1000-americans-are-serving-in-the-israeli-army-and-they-arent-alone). Alienating Israel could force those citizens to have to choose a side.
1.4.3.5.4. Pro: Israel is [strongly opposed](http://nationalinterest.org/feature/israels-master-plan-crush-irans-nuclear-program-13392) to the Iran nuclear deal. If Israeli-US relations deteriorate as a result of US recognition of Palestine, Israel may launch a pre-emptive strike against Iran, raising the possibility of a regional war.
1.4.3.5.4.1. Pro: The threat of Iran acquiring a 'break-out' weapon after ten years, when the Iran Nuclear deal expires, may lead Israel to [strike](http://www.ocregister.com/2015/07/26/why-israel-will-hit-iran-after-obamas-gone/) Iran, especially if it feels it is losing US support and must protect itself.
1.4.3.5.4.2. Con: Amos Yadlin, the former head of IDF Intelligence, [claimed](http://www.timesofisrael.com/ex-idf-intel-chief-strike-on-iran-likely-wont-spark-regional-war/) that it was highly unlikely that a missile strike by Israel would lead to a regional war, primarily because Iran was aware of Israel's ability to destroy it in an all out war. This in turn would threaten the survival of the Iranian regime.
1.4.3.5.4.3. Con: The Israeli military and intelligence community supports the Iran nuclear deal.
1.4.3.5.4.3.1. Con: The Israeli political and security establishments are [split](http://nationalinterest.org/feature/netanyahu-idf-are-split-the-iran-nuclear-deal-15368?page=2) on their attitude towards the Iran deal. Despite the security establishment's acceptance of the Iran nuclear deal, Netanyahu could still order an attack on Iran.
1.4.3.5.4.3.2. Pro: Official Israeli statements on Iran are nothing but political rhetoric. Multiple Israeli security officials, including Israeli Chief of the General Staff Lieutenant General Gadi Eizenkot, have [stated](https://www.theatlantic.com/international/archive/2016/03/iran-nuclear-deal-israel/472767/) that Iran's nuclear threat has been pushed back by at least 10-15 years, if not eliminated.
1.4.3.5.4.3.3. Pro: The Israeli security establishment has [warned](http://www.al-monitor.com/pulse/originals/2017/01/israel-netanyahu-trump-security-iran-deal-nuke-agreement.html) Netanyahu to not touch the Iran nuclear deal. They assessed that destroying the nuclear deal will unite the Iranian people behind the regime, and possibly even push it to pursue an all out nuclear option.
1.4.3.5.4.4. Pro: Israel [was close to](http://www.jpost.com/Israel-News/Politics-And-Diplomacy/Peres-bombshell-I-stopped-an-Israeli-strike-on-Iran-469112) preemptively striking Iran in the past. A falling out with the United States might embolden Israel to do so next time - and thereby torpedoing America's politics in the region, for example the 2015 nuclear deal with Iran.
1.4.3.5.5. Pro: Israel could sell sensitive military technology that either the US shares with it or it creates itself in retaliation for US recognition \([p. 12](https://sgp.fas.org/crs/mideast/RL33222.pdf)\).
1.4.3.5.5.1. Pro: Washington insisted that Israel agree to stop selling problematic weapons and military technology to China and deprive itself of both a major market for its world-class military exports and a source of influence with Beijing. Without this pressure, Israel would resume selling weapons to China \([p. 9](https://cdn.cfr.org/sites/default/files/pdf/2011/10/Israel_strategic_US_assest_report.pdf)\).
1.4.3.5.5.2. Pro: Israel is a world leader in the development of unmanned aerial systems, for both intelligence collection and combat, and it has shared with the U.S. military the technology, the doctrine, and its experience regarding these systems \([p. 10](https://cdn.cfr.org/sites/default/files/pdf/2011/10/Israel_strategic_US_assest_report.pdf)\). America's ability to gather intelligence could be restricted if Israel decided to cut of trade in military technology.
1.4.3.5.5.3. Con: Presumably, the US would stop sharing sensitive technology with Israel if the latter started selling it as a form of retaliation for the recognition of Palestine.
1.4.3.5.5.4. Con: Due to Israel's reliance on American support for equipping its military, it is unlikely that Israel would endanger this support by going against its supplier's interests.
1.4.3.5.5.4.1. Pro: All airplanes and nearly all helicopters of the [Israeli Air Force](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israeli_Air_Force#Aircraft) were bought from the US. With an eye on its international position, it is unlikely that Israel would be able to procure military technology on this level from elsewhere.
1.4.3.5.5.4.2. Pro: The US also provides [vital defense technologies](http://www.belfercenter.org/publication/israels-dependence-united-states-existential) that Israel would not have access to otherwise.
1.4.3.5.5.5. Con: Israel did not retaliate against the other [138 countries](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/International_recognition_of_the_State_of_Palestine) that recognized Palestine as a state, hence it is unlikely that it would retaliate against its closest ally and greatest source of [foreign aid](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel%E2%80%93United_States_relations).
1.4.3.5.5.5.1. Pro: A few of these countries, like [Iran](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Israel_relations#Increasing_tensions_\(1989%E2%80%93present\)) and [Syria](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel%E2%80%93Syria_relations), are open enemies of Israel. Nonetheless, Israel did not retaliate against them when they recognized Palestine. It seems unlikely that Israel would then retaliate against its greatest ally and foreign aid source.
1.4.3.5.5.6. Pro: Israel has not been above using blackmail against the US to get what it wants. In 1973, during the Yom Kippur War, its cabinet reportedly engaged in "nuclear blackmail", by demanding an emergency airlift of arms and supplies from the US, depicting self-defense with nuclear weapons as the likely alternative \([pp. 225-240](https://archive.org/details/Sampson_Option/page/n233)\).
1.4.3.5.5.6.1. Con: Although often-repeated, this narrative of "nuclear blackmail" [has been called into question](https://www.armscontrolwonk.com/archive/206909/israel-nuclear-weapons-and-the-1973-yom-kippur-war/#_ftn5) as it was never confirmed by named sources in public.
1.4.3.5.5.7. Pro: Israel has a track record of selling US arms to third countries without authorization. This was the case when Israel transferred arms to [Sub-Saharan Africa](https://www.files.ethz.ch/isn/134521/SIPRIBP1110.pdf)(pp. 8-10), [China, and Taiwan](https://www.researchgate.net/publication/233197238_Israel%27s_Military_Transfers_to_China_and_Taiwan)(pp. 80-83).
1.4.3.5.5.7.1. Con: If Israel already has an established track record of selling arms to third parties without authorisation, then it seems unlikely that the recognition of Palestine will meaningfully change the state of affairs.
1.4.3.5.5.8. Con: Selling sensitive military technology would hurt Israel as much as the US, as Israel shares many of the same enemies. This would make intentional leaking of technology unlikely.
1.4.3.5.5.8.1. Con: While US relations with Russia are at their [lowest point](http://nationalpost.com/news/world/putin-says-u-s-russia-relations-at-lowest-point-since-cold-war-asks-american-business-leaders-to-help-trump/wcm/06d1cab2-109e-4677-88e3-ed3b7a21fc8d) since the Cold War, Israeli relations with Russia are the [warmest](http://www.jpost.com/Israel-News/Despite-Syria-Israel-Russia-relations-are-the-warmest-in-history-485062) they have ever been, despite conflicting goals in Syria.
1.4.3.5.5.8.2. Con: While relations between the US and China are growing [worse](http://www.realclearworld.com/articles/2017/04/06/6_reasons_us-china_relations_are_headed_for_trouble_112279.html) over conflicting priorities of trade and security, Israel and China have [vowed](http://www.scmp.com/news/china/diplomacy-defence/article/2080572/china-and-israel-vow-deepen-relations) to deepen relations.
1.4.3.6. Con: Close association with Israel is a burden so it may serve the US well to weaken ties.
1.4.3.6.1. Con: The [majority of Americans](https://www.brookings.edu/research/american-attitudes-on-the-israeli-palestinian-conflict/) do not perceive Israel as a burden to the United States.
1.4.3.6.1.1. Con: The public is not always aware of the intricacies of international politics, and is thus unlikely to be aware of the cost to their country of such a close association with Israel.
1.4.3.6.1.2. Pro: Even if the actual benefits are hard to quantify, three out of four Americans believe that Israel provides "essential military and intelligence cooperation" for the United States in the region \([p. 38](https://www.brookings.edu/wp-content/uploads/2016/12/cmep_20161202_public_opinion_poll.pdf)\).
1.4.3.6.1.2.1. Con: [Geo-strategic security](https://dbpedia.org/page/Geostrategy)(Geostrategy can function prescriptively, advocating foreign policy based on geographic and historical factors, analytically, describing how foreign policy is shaped by geography and history, or predictively, projecting a country's future foreign policy decisions and outcomes.) policies are not made with public opinion in mind, given they often do not reflect reality.
1.4.3.6.1.2.2. Pro: For decades, the US has been almost entirely dependent on Israel for intelligence regarding [the Middle East](https://www.jewishvirtuallibrary.org/u-s-israel-intelligence-collaboration).
1.4.3.6.2. Con: Israel hosts a large-scale American [war reserve stock](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/War_reserve_stock#War_Reserves_Stock_Allies-Israel) with some $1.8 billion worth of equipment for use in case of armed conflict in the region.
1.4.3.6.3. Pro: The extent and unconditionality of American [support for Israel](https://www.aljazeera.com/news/2021/5/18/short-answer-why-is-the-united-states-so-pro-israel) has been described as going against America's [strategic and moral interests](https://ctmirror.org/category/ct-viewpoints/time-to-reconsider-u-s-s-unconditional-support-for-israel-john/).
1.5. Con: Recognizing Palestine while it is partially ruled by [Hamas](https://www.nytimes.com/2014/10/10/world/middleeast/palestinians-gaza-cabinet-hamas.html) is equivalent to legitimizing a [terrorist organization](https://www.state.gov/foreign-terrorist-organizations/)(10/8/1997 HAMAS).
1.5.1. Con: It is possible to recognize Palestine as a state and simultaneously condemn Hamas as terrorists and illegitimate rulers of the area they control in Gaza.
1.5.1.1. Pro: Hamas is not entirely a terrorist organisation, it's mostly [a political party](https://www.tandfonline.com/doi/abs/10.1080/09546553.2013.733273). Only its armed branch, called [Izz ad Din al Qassam Brigades](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Izz_ad-Din_al-Qassam_Brigades), may be considered as a terrorist organisation.
1.5.1.1.1. Pro: In [January 2006](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2006_Palestinian_legislative_election), Hamas' political party won a plurality in the Palestinian Parliament. Being political in nature and as long as the political arm plays within the democratic and constitutional rules they should be given a chance to be considered.
1.5.1.2. Pro: India [recognizes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/International_recognition_of_the_State_of_Palestine#:~:text=Among%20members%20of%20the%20G20,the%20United%20States\)%20have%20not.)(Among members of the G20 major countries, 9 \(being Argentina, Brazil, China, India, Indonesia, Russia, Saudi Arabia, South Africa and Turkey\) have recognized Palestine as a state) Palestine's statehood, but simultaneously [condemns](https://www.hindustantimes.com/india-news/india-opposes-hamas-rocket-action-against-israel-supports-palestine-101621224892489.html) attacks carried out by Hamas.
1.5.1.3. Pro: China [supports](https://www.aljazeera.com/economy/2021/6/7/chinas-ties-with-israel-are-tested-by-gaza-but-not-sorely)(While it has invested large sums of money in Israel, China has sought to maintain its historic image as a strong supporter of Palestine by taking symbolic stances on certain issues.\n\nIn 2017, China banned its nationals from taking part in illegal settlement building in the occupied West Bank, even as Chinese contractors were busy working on infrastructure projects in Israel.) Palestine whilst maintaining economic links with Israel. This would likely be infeasible if the nation supported Hamas.
1.5.1.4. Con: A [2021 survey](https://apnews.com/article/hamas-middle-east-science-32095d8e1323fc1cad819c34da08fd87) found strong Palestinian support for Hamas \(75%\), which was also voted as the most worthy leader of the Palestinian people. Thus, it is impossible to recognize Palestine and simultaneously invalidate the popular vote.
1.5.1.5. Con: Hamas has been working to establish [an independent Palestinian state](https://www.britannica.com/topic/Hamas). As such, recognition of such a state would inevitably be regarded as an achievement of their expressed objectives.
1.5.1.6. Con: Just because certain countries regard Hamas as a terrorist organization does not mean that this is indeed the case. Instead, such a designation has been regarded as a means to [silence pro-Palestine activism](https://www.aljazeera.com/opinions/2021/11/25/the-uk-government-is-on-the-wrong-side-of-history-again).
1.5.2. Pro: Recognizing Palestine whilst Hamas is control could [send a problematic signal](https://www.law.upenn.edu/live/files/5141-legitimacy-and-complexity-in-terrorist-conflicts--)(One of the main arguments put forward by scholars against engaging with terrorists is that such a course of action would legitimize the terrorists, their goals and, most of all, their means.) to other groups by showing that terrorism can garner US recognition more effectively than diplomatic action \(p. 410\).
1.5.2.1. Con: The US both recognizes a number of entities associated with terrorist organizations and has previously [supported terrorist groups](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_and_state-sponsored_terrorism) to overthrow established governments.
1.5.2.1.1. Pro: Hezbollah [exerts massive amounts of control](http://www.newsweek.com/hezbollahs-latest-conquest-lebanons-cabinet-541487) over Lebanon, however, the US still recognizes Lebanon's statehood.
1.5.2.1.1.1. Con: US recognition of Lebanon predates the founding of Hezbollah, which occurred in [1982](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hezbollah).
1.5.2.1.1.2. Pro: Hezbollah is designated a [Foreign Terror Organisation](https://www.state.gov/j/ct/rls/other/des/123085.htm) by the US.
1.5.2.1.1.2.1. Pro: The US has [enacted sanctions](https://www.aljazeera.com/economy/2020/9/8/us-sanctions-former-lebanese-ministers-over-ties-to-hezbollah)(The United States on Tuesday expanded its sanctions on Lebanon, blacklisting the former transport and finance ministers and accusing them of providing material and financial help to the Iran-backed group Hezbollah, following a powerful blast last month in Beirut that left the country reeling.\n\n“Corruption has run rampant in Lebanon, and Hizballah has exploited the political system to spread its malign influence,” US Treasury Secretary Steven Mnuchin said in a statement, announcing the blacklisting of former Lebanese government ministers Yusuf Finyanus and Ali Hassan Khalil.) against Lebanese officials with connections to Hezbollah.
1.5.2.1.1.3. Con: Whereas Hamas controls the Gaza Strip, the influence of Hezbollah in Lebanon is smaller, and concerns mainly day-to-day affairs. It holds [merely 9%](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lebanese_general_election,_2017) of the seats in parliament, provides only [two out of 30](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lebanese_government_of_December_2016) ministers and neither the Prime Minister nor President.
1.5.2.1.1.4. Pro: Hezbollah is by far the [most influential political organization](https://www.chathamhouse.org/2021/06/how-hezbollah-holds-sway-over-lebanese-state/02-influence-through-state-institutions) in Lebanon.
1.5.2.1.2. Con: -> See 1.4.1.2.4.1.3.
1.5.2.1.3. Pro: The United States recognizes governments which it has classified as [state sponsors of terrorism](https://www.state.gov/j/ct/list/c14151.htm): Syria, Iran, North Korea, and Cuba. These states pose a very real threat to the US, and therefore should be designated as such.
1.5.2.1.3.1. Pro: The USA has also been involved in [state-sponsored terrorism](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_and_state-sponsored_terrorism), regime change and war since its inception, yet that didn't lead other states to call into question American statehood. The same should be the case for Palestine.
1.5.2.1.3.2. Con: It wouldn’t benefit Palestine to be recognized as a [state sponsor of terrorism](https://www.state.gov/j/ct/list/c14151.htm) by the United States.
1.5.2.1.3.3. Pro: Not only would the designation of a state sponsor of terrorism probably be not particularly problematic, it is also unlikely. Even if organizations like Hamas are categorized as sponsors of terrorism, it is hard to imagine that this label would be applied to Palestine as a whole.
1.5.2.1.3.4. Con: America should not accept the establishment of a new state that would be de-facto controlled \(if only in part\) by a terrorist group.
1.5.2.2. Pro: Leaders have previously claimed not to [negotiate](https://www.bbc.co.uk/news/uk-northern-ireland-16366413)("I think that they are revelatory and of genuine historical importance because they give lie to all sorts of assumptions that were made incorrectly about the Hunger Strikes and the relationship between the government and the IRA.\n\n"These documents spell it out large that Mrs Thatcher was involved in negotiations with the IRA."\n\nThe documents contain details of eight phone calls between the MI6 officer and Mr Duddy during the weekend from 4 July to 6 July 1981.) with terrorists to signal the strength of their ideological position, even if that is counter to reality.
1.5.3. Pro: Hamas, which governs part of the current Palestinian territory, [does not recognize](https://www.dw.com/en/hamas-recognizes-1967-borders-rejects-israel/a-38656798) Israel as a state, let alone its Jewish statehood.
1.5.3.1. Pro: In 2017, Ismail Haniyeh was [elected](https://indianexpress.com/article/world/hamas-says-ismail-haniyeh-chosen-as-islamic-groups-leader-4643691/) as the new leader of the Hamas Political Bureau. This illustrates that his view is in line with the official policy of Hamas as an organisation and, therefore, the people who vote for it.
1.5.3.2. Con: Hamas [outlined](http://edition.cnn.com/2006/WORLD/meast/01/29/hamas.interview/) conditions for a truce with Israel before the 2006 elections in Gaza, indicating that it is willing to be pragmatic when it comes to electoral pressures, even if it does not ideologically accept Israel's right to exist.
1.5.4. Con: US recognition of Palestine will improve Israel's security by changing the balance of power in the region. This change is more important than any fear of legitimising Hamas.
1.5.4.1. Pro: Reducing the potential for conflict between Israel and Palestine could weaken regional adversaries of the US and Israel.
1.5.4.1.1. Pro: Better relations between Israel and the Palestinians would weaken Iran, one of the principal adversaries of the United States and Israel, which has long used Hezbollah and Hamas [as proxies](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Israel_proxy_conflict).
1.5.4.1.1.1. Pro: By supporting terrorist groups, Iran [can](https://www.lawfareblog.com/irans-support-terrorist-groups) undermine and intimidate rivals, influence the Israel-Palestine conflict, and project power in regional crises. Weakening Iran's proxies would lessen their ability to carry out these disruptive actions.
1.5.4.1.1.2. Pro: According to ex-Prime Minister Netanyahu, defense analysts in Israel [estimate that](http://www.timesofisrael.com/netanyahu-80-of-security-threats-against-israel-emanate-from-iran/) more than 80% of the country's security problems emanate from Iran.
1.5.4.1.1.3. Con: Recent events involving the US and Iran, such as US withdrawal from the nuclear deal under the [Trump administration](https://www.cfr.org/backgrounder/what-iran-nuclear-deal) and the killing of [Soleimani](https://edition.cnn.com/interactive/2020/01/world/us-iran-conflict-timeline-trnd/), have further compounded conflicts between the two countries. These events have caused direct enmity between the US and Iran; therefore, indirectly weakening Iran by resolving the Israel-Palestine conflict is unlikely to be effective.
1.5.4.1.1.3.1. Pro: Iran is one of the handful of countries without a US embassy; the lack of diplomatic relations between the US and Bhutan, North Korea, and Iran leaves each of the [latter countries](https://edition.cnn.com/2013/05/09/politics/btn-diplomatic-presence/index.html) without an official US government presence.
1.5.4.1.1.4. Pro: Solving the Palestinian conflict is cited as a [precondition](http://world.time.com/2014/02/04/iranian-foreign-minister-lays-out-condition-for-iranian-recognition-of-israel/) by Iran for recognizing Israel. Should America's recognition of Palestine lead to this, one of Israel's biggest foes would possibly take a more conciliatory stance.
1.5.4.1.1.4.1. Pro: It is not clear that Israel requires Iran's recognition - they have shown [superior military capabilities](https://www.reuters.com/article/us-iran-nuclear-scientist-idUSKBN2AA2RC) in their assassination of Iran's top nuclear scientist.
1.5.4.1.1.5. Con: Iran does not depend on the Israeli oppression of Palestinians in order to [exert its influence](https://www.un.org/press/en/2021/sc14668.doc.htm)(Turning to Iran, he expressed concern that it is aiming to become a “nuclear threshold State”, which obstructs the International Atomic Energy Agency \(IAEA\) and violates international agreements. The country is a centre of Shiite hegemony that exports terror around the world. If the Council does not take strong action, that country will command forces such as Hamas and Hezbollah and, protected by its nuclear umbrella, turn its “reign of terror into a hurricane of violence”.) in the region.
1.5.4.1.2. Con: Recognition of statehood does not automatically eliminate the US' security concerns. If Hamas posed a legitimate security threat, the US could get involved in some capacity regardless of Palestinian sovereignty, as it does in other nations around the world.
1.5.4.1.3. Pro: Recognizing Palestine may take away from the factors that motivate terrorism against Israel, reducing pressure on regional security forces.
1.5.4.1.3.1. Con: Going by the declarations of [past Israeli leaders](https://www.nbcnews.com/news/world/temple-mount-tensions-al-aqsa-mosque-rumors-behind-palestinian-unrest-n440811), Israel would prefer to maintain control over the Temple Mount/Al-Aqsa Mosque. This has been a [major motivation](https://www.nbcnews.com/news/world/temple-mount-tensions-al-aqsa-mosque-rumors-behind-palestinian-unrest-n440811) for past Palestinian terrorist attacks.
1.5.4.1.3.2. Con: Even among Palestinian terrorists attacking Israel, there is no uniform or common pattern of motivations. Nationalist and economic grievances alone are seen as insufficient factors for explaining their terrorism \([p. 87](http://www.aldeilis.net/terror/1188.pdf)\).
1.5.4.1.3.2.1. Con: Palestinian liberation features [prominently](http://www.washingtoninstitute.org/policy-analysis/view/teaching-terror-how-hamas-radicalizes-palestinian-society) in Hamas propaganda used for radicalizing Palestinian youth.
1.5.4.1.3.3. Pro: [Coercing](https://books.google.co.kr/books?id=SOlnH3f_dXwC&lpg=PA3&dq=islamic%20terrorism%20motivations&lr&pg=PA3#v=onepage&q&f=false)(Table 6, pg. 43) a foreign military force to withdraw from the terrorist groups' homeland was a strong motivator of most suicide terrorism campaigns between 1980 and 2003. Recognising Palestine might be perceived as a step in this direction.
1.5.4.1.3.4. Pro: Palestinian terrorism against Israel is linked to their [loss of identity](https://www.researchgate.net/publication/236707150_Catastrophe_Memory_and_Identity_Al-Nakbah_as_a_Component_of_Palestinian_Identity)(p. 194) through foreign domination, and the lack of progress in creating a nation. Recognizing Palestine might help to overcome these feelings and signify political progress.
1.5.4.1.3.4.1. Con: Intractable conflicts can result in a sense of [collective victimhood](https://www.corteidh.or.cr/tablas/r23447.pdf)(p. 235) among those affected, and these shared meanings can be the basis for a newly reformulated identity.
1.5.4.1.3.5. Pro: In 2016, more than half of all Palestinians supported armed attacks on Israeli citizens \([p. 5](http://www.pcpsr.org/sites/default/files/poll%2062%20English%20full%20text.pdf)\). Ending the occupation of Palestine might help change these attitudes.
1.5.4.1.3.6. Pro: Decreased pressure on regional security forces may more effectively shield the US from terrorism.
1.5.4.1.3.6.1. Con: The threat that terrorism poses to the US is negligible. Since 2001, only [6 people per year](https://www.businessinsider.com.au/death-risk-statistics-terrorism-disease-accidents-2017-1?r=US&IR=T) were killed by terrorism - a figure more than 10 times smaller than those killed by choking on food.
1.5.4.1.3.6.2. Con: The terrorist organisations that have declared war on the US would continue to fight against it independent of the situation in Palestine.
1.5.4.1.3.6.2.1. Pro: [US presence](http://www.npr.org/templates/story/story.php?storyId=6137678) in Iraq stokes a [threat](https://edition.cnn.com/2021/09/13/politics/dni-avril-haines-terrorist-threat-somalia-yemen-syria-iraq/index.html) of terrorism. This is independent of the Palestinian conflict.
1.5.4.1.3.6.2.2. Pro: Certain [interpretations](http://www.thereligionofpeace.com/quran/023-violence.htm) of Islam encourage killing non-Muslims. These interpretations exist and will be wielded by extremists regardless of US actions.
1.5.4.1.3.6.2.2.1. Pro: [ISIS](https://www.theatlantic.com/magazine/archive/2015/03/what-isis-really-wants/384980/) and [al-Qaeda](http://www.spiegel.de/international/the-future-of-terrorism-what-al-qaida-really-wants-a-369448.html) both want to establish a global caliphate. This goal will remain regardless of how friendly the US is to Palestine.
1.5.4.1.3.6.2.3. Con: The plight of the Palestinians vis-à-vis Israel is a contributing factor towards extremism far beyond these two countries. An American recognition of Palestine would undermine this as the fate of the nation would seem more secure.
1.5.4.1.3.6.2.3.1. Pro: Former senior CIA officials and military commanders believe that the Palestine issue helps al-Qaeda recruit more soldiers \([p. 293](https://hegghammer.files.wordpress.com/2019/07/hegghammer-wagemakers-the-palestine-effect-the-role-of-palestinians-in-the-transnational-jihad-movement.pdf)\).
1.5.4.1.3.6.2.3.1.1. Pro: Osama bin Laden identified the Israel-Palestine conflict and the oppression of Palestinians as one of the central drivers behind the 9/11 terrorist attacks \([p. 73](https://www.tandfonline.com/doi/pdf/10.1080/00396330903168865)\).
1.5.4.1.3.6.2.3.1.1.1. Pro: US support for Israel and perceived animosity toward Islam were repeatedly cited as motivating factors for terror attacks by bin Laden, beginning with his call for [boycott of US goods](https://www.theguardian.com/commentisfree/2007/dec/03/osamabinladenstruepriorities) in the '80s to his [fatwa and jihad declaration](https://is.muni.cz/el/1423/jaro2010/MVZ203/OBL___AQ__Fatwa_1996.pdf)(p. 2) against the US in the '90s.
1.5.4.1.3.6.2.3.1.1.2. Con: Bin Laden only developed contacts with Palestinian organizations in the late 1990s, resulting from new connections to Lebanon and Usbat al-Ansar \([p. 192](https://books.google.de/books?id=IOoBZvdNrIkC&printsec=frontcover&source=gbs_ge_summary_r&cad=0#v=onepage&q=%22Thus%20far%2C%20Hamas%22&f=false)\).
1.5.4.1.3.6.2.3.1.1.3. Con: When US Special Forces raided the Osama bin Laden compound in Pakistan in 2011, they absconded with documents revealing internal debates about how the organisation should continue to [exploit](https://consortiumnews.com/2012/05/27/how-al-qaeda-exploits-palestine-cause/) the Palestinian cause in order to increase recruitment.
1.5.4.1.3.6.2.3.1.1.4. Pro: In an interview, Osama bin-Laden's mother described her son as being "concerned, sad, and frustrated about the situation in Palestine" during his teenage years \([p. 76](https://burocraufabc.files.wordpress.com/2014/03/aula-7-wright-2007-em-inglc3aas.pdf)\).
1.5.4.1.3.6.2.3.1.1.5. Pro: Upon seeing Ariel Sharon's visit to the Temple Mount in 2000, bin Laden hurried Mohamed Atta, the pilot of the first plane that crashed into the World Trade Center, to accelerate their preparations for the 9/11 attacks \([p. 18](http://govinfo.library.unt.edu/911/staff_statements/staff_statement_16.pdf)\).
1.5.4.1.3.6.2.3.1.2. Pro: In arguably its most important ideological statement, the “Declaration of the World Islamic Front for Jihad against the Jews and the Crusaders” \(February 1998\), al-Qaeda listed Palestine [third](https://fas.org/irp/world/para/docs/980223-fatwa.htm)(Third, if the Americans' aims behind these wars are religious and economic, the aim is also to serve the Jews' petty state and divert attention from its occupation of Jerusalem and murder of Muslims there. The best proof of this is their eagerness to destroy Iraq, the strongest neighboring Arab state, and their endeavor to fragment all the states of the region such as Iraq, Saudi Arabia, Egypt, and Sudan into paper statelets and through their disunion and weakness to guarantee Israel's survival and the continuation of the brutal crusade occupation of the Peninsula.) on a list of reasons why jihad against America is justified \(after the US military presence in Saudi Arabia and the sanctions regime against Iraq\).
1.5.4.1.3.6.2.3.1.3. Con: -> See 1.4.3.5.1.1.
1.5.4.1.3.6.2.3.2. Pro: Statelessness has led some Palestinians to take part in transnational jihad, and act as ideologues for the jihadi movement \([p. 294](https://hegghammer.files.wordpress.com/2019/07/hegghammer-wagemakers-the-palestine-effect-the-role-of-palestinians-in-the-transnational-jihad-movement.pdf)\). If a Palestinian state were to be established, they would have a home, reducing their incentive to act aggressively.
1.5.4.1.3.6.2.3.2.1. Con: The available evidence does not suggest that Palestinians are overrepresented amongst transnational jihadi networks \([p. 296](https://hegghammer.files.wordpress.com/2019/07/hegghammer-wagemakers-the-palestine-effect-the-role-of-palestinians-in-the-transnational-jihad-movement.pdf)(A recent study found that only 7 of 280 individuals hailed as fallen martyrs on jihādī websites were Palestinian. There are all kinds of problems with the above-mentioned data, but what exists suggests that Palestinians are not strongly overrepresented in trans-\nnational jihādī networks.)\). This suggests that Israeli occupation is not a decisive factor in motivating Palestinians to turn to militancy.
1.5.4.1.3.6.2.3.2.2. Pro: [Abdallāh ʿAzzām](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Abdullah_Yusuf_Azzam), known as the 'Godfather of Jihad', was responsible for spearheading the effort to bring Muslim foreign fighters to Afghanistan in the 1980s. He was radicalised in Palestine and participated in paramilitary operations against Israel.
1.5.4.1.3.6.2.3.3. Con: Regardless of whether the US recognises Palestine, it is unlikely to change their general support for Israel. This motivation would thus still exist.
1.5.4.1.3.6.2.3.4. Pro: Studies on Muslim terrorists in Western countries indicate that a motive for terrorism is the belief that Islam is oppressed by the West. Recognizing Palestine might be a step towards changing this perception \([p. 7](https://www.usip.org/sites/default/files/resources/SR236Venhaus.pdf)\).
1.5.4.1.3.6.2.3.4.1. Con: Despite anti-Semitic and anti-Zionist motivations, ISIS has not directed any [attacks](https://www.nytimes.com/interactive/2016/03/25/world/map-isis-attacks-around-the-world.html) towards Israel. This shows that Israel is not a primary target nor is the Palestinian cause a serious ideological motivation for Islamic terrorist groups.
1.5.4.1.3.6.2.3.4.1.1. Con: Abu Bakr al-Baghdadi, leader of ISIS, has [invoked](https://www.brookings.edu/opinions/palestine-still-key-to-stability-in-the-middle-east/) the Palestinian cause in his crusade against the Jews and Americans.
1.5.4.1.3.6.2.3.4.1.2. Pro: The US and the UK have a world-class intelligence and security apparatus, yet still have been unable to prevent ISIS attacks in their countries. It is unlikely that Israel deters ISIS, rather that ISIS itself is not interested in attacking Israel.
1.5.4.1.3.6.2.3.4.2. Pro: The 1993 World Trade Center attack was targeted at the Jewish population of New York and aimed to compel the US to cut all ties with Israel \([p. 289](https://hegghammer.files.wordpress.com/2019/07/hegghammer-wagemakers-the-palestine-effect-the-role-of-palestinians-in-the-transnational-jihad-movement.pdf)(Yousef later said he chose New York City because of its large Jewish population, and in letters sent to newspapers before the attack he stated three demands, the first two of which were an end to all US aid to Israel and an end to US diplomatic relations with Israel.)\).
1.5.4.1.3.6.2.3.4.3. Pro: US administration officials have admitted that the Palestinian conflict [increases](http://america.aljazeera.com/opinions/2015/12/to-defeat-isil-the-israeli-palestinian-conflict-must-be-resolved.html) the appeal of ISIS recruiting tools.
1.5.4.1.3.6.2.3.5. Con: Contemporary Islamic terrorism in the West is not committed by the victims of the Palestinian conflict nor people who show sympathy to the victims. Terrorists use the plight of fellow Muslims and religion [as a guise](https://www.theguardian.com/news/2017/apr/13/who-are-the-new-jihadis) for already existing radicalization and nihilism.
1.5.4.1.3.6.2.3.5.1. Con: Terrorist recruiters highlight the oppression and deprivation experienced by the groups they supposedly represent \([p. 3](https://www.ojp.gov/pdffiles1/nij/grants/208552.pdf)(Perceived injustice, need for identity and need for belonging are common vulnerabilities among\npotential terrorists. \[...\] Recruitment efforts do appear concentrated in areas where people feel most deprived and dissatisfied.\nRelationships are critical. Effective recruiters create and exploit a sense of urgency and imminence. \[...\] Effective leaders of terrorist organizations must be able to: \[...\] manipulate incentives \(and purposive goals\) for followers; deflect conflict to external targets.)\). Therefore, regardless of their true motives, [terrorist organizations](https://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pmc/articles/PMC6109790/)(The main finding of the research was that there was an indirect effect of perceived oppression on violent disinhibition through radical intentions in the Muslim sample, \[...\] the conjunction of the loss of significance and radical intentions seems to strongly exacerbate the likelihood of a process of violent disinhibition for those who are considered to be in marginal contexts.) may use the plight of Palestinians to recruit or gain popularity among civilians.
1.5.4.1.3.6.2.3.5.2. Pro: Empirical findings suggest that there is [no correlation](https://www.cato.org/sites/cato.org/files/pubs/pdf/working-paper-56-update.pdf)(\[W\]e find no empirical evidence to suggest that increases in the share of immigrants from abroad is significantly correlated with higher rates of terrorism. These results hold for immigrants from both Muslim majority and conflict-torn countries of origin.\n\n\(p. 12\)) between immigration, including from conflict-torn Muslim countries, and terrorism.
1.5.4.1.3.6.2.4. Con: Reducing the threat of Palestinian terror in the US, however minor, makes the world safer.
1.5.4.1.3.6.3. Con: It is unlikely that Palestinian organizations commit acts of terror in the US; therefore, they should not be a focus of US diplomatic relations and foreign policy.
1.5.4.1.3.6.3.1. Con: Palestinians have been linked to groups that directly oppose and threaten US interests and allies \(e.g., [ISIS](https://www.europarl.europa.eu/doceo/document/E-8-2015-005120_EN.html)(Whilst Palestinian forces have arrested ISIS supporters, the Hamas-controlled Palestinian government is not openly fighting the Islamic State. Furthermore, Palestinian terrorists are adopting some of the methods employed by ISIS. The similarities relate not only to propaganda but also to the methods of terrorist attacks. This was the case in the attack on a synagogue in Jerusalem on 18 November 2014, when knives were used in accordance with the calls of ISIS spokesman Abu Muhammad al Adnani.)\).
1.5.4.1.3.6.3.2. Pro: There is little evidence that international terrorist organisations willing and capable of striking the US, like al-Qaeda, are linked to Palestinian groups \([p. 63](https://books.google.co.kr/books?id=bQHXJ4JzxV4C&pg=PT3&lpg=PT3&dq=0-374-17772-4&source=bl&ots=APimckevjw&sig=iq9yYeg467Yc6VnXh-YNhuozdSA&hl=en&sa=X&ved=0ahUKEwjG7tjIobfUAhWCgbwKHeWAAcUQ6AEIJjAB#v=onepage&q=0-374-17772-4&f=false)\).
1.5.4.1.3.6.3.2.1. Con: [Ma’sadat al-Mujahideen](http://www.independent.co.uk/news/world/middle-east/israel-fires-haifa-jerusalem-terror-palestinian-militant-group-ma-sadat-al-mujahideen-mount-carmel-a7439271.html) is a Palestinian Salafist group with links to al-Qaeda. It claims to have started a number of fires in Israel, including the 2016 Haifa blaze that led to the evacuation of 60,000 people.
1.5.4.1.3.6.3.2.2. Con: [Army of Islam](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Army_of_Islam_\(Gaza_Strip\)) is a militant group that operates in the Gaza Strip. It draws inspiration from and is likely linked to al-Qaeda.
1.5.4.1.3.6.3.2.3. Con: Hamas has [loose ties](http://www.weeklystandard.com/the-hamas-al-qaeda-alliance/article/558605) with al-Qaeda: Hamas members receive training from their camps and often try to recruit fighters for their cause from there.
1.5.4.1.3.6.3.2.4. Pro: Despite threatening to, Hamas has not joined al-Qaeda's global jihad. Hamas sees itself as a [local resistance organization](http://www.washingtoninstitute.org/policy-analysis/view/could-hamas-target-the-west) and has limited its operations to targeting Israelis in Israel, the West Bank, and the Gaza Strip.
1.5.4.1.3.6.3.2.4.1. Con: Al-Qaeda has a [history](http://www.jpost.com/Opinion/Op-Ed-Contributors/Al-Qaida-and-Palestinian-jihadists-The-Hamas-connection-339782) of conducting attacks in Israel by recruiting and sending in foreign fighters. After al-Qaeda started losing ground in Afghanistan, Bin Laden marked Palestine as a top priority. Al-Qaeda does not need to be linked to Palestinian organisations to operate there.
1.5.4.1.3.6.3.2.4.1.1. Pro: The shoe bomber, Richard Reid, trained by al-Qaeda in Afghanistan, traveled to Israel in 2001 to [scout out](http://content.time.com/time/world/article/0,8599,203478-1,00.html) locations for potential bombings.
1.5.4.1.3.6.3.2.4.2. Pro: Hamas and al-Qaeda's interactions were negligible during the '90s and '00s \([pp. 285-286](https://hegghammer.files.wordpress.com/2019/07/hegghammer-wagemakers-the-palestine-effect-the-role-of-palestinians-in-the-transnational-jihad-movement.pdf)\).
1.5.4.1.3.6.3.2.4.2.1. Pro: Al-Qaeda has [consistently](http://www.washingtoninstitute.org/policy-analysis/view/the-war-of-words-between-hamas-and-al-qaeda) condemned the Hamas leadership whenever they have run for elections or tried to work with Fatah in a unity government; their support for Hamas exists only when the latter adopts a military approach to the Palestinian conflict.
1.5.4.1.3.6.3.2.4.3. Pro: There is little to no evidence connecting the central leadership of al-Qaeda with attacks in Israel or on other Jewish targets. These attacks, therefore, demonstrate that Israel is not a priority for al-Qaeda \([p. 291](https://hegghammer.files.wordpress.com/2019/07/hegghammer-wagemakers-the-palestine-effect-the-role-of-palestinians-in-the-transnational-jihad-movement.pdf)\).
1.5.4.1.3.6.4. Pro: Currently, the Palestinian conflict allows secularists and Islamists \([pp. 107-114](https://www.cmi.no/publications/file/4875-questioning-the-secularreligious-cleavage-in.pdf)(\[I\]nstead of keeping its secularism as an alternative to the religious Hamas, Fatah aligned its rhetoric and policies with the increasingly religious Palestinian electorate \[...\] while Hamas was established as a religious-nationalistic liberation movement with absolutist territorial claims, it has since developed into a more pragmatic political party with a less pronounced focus on religion.)\) to converge and form a common picture of the [US as a foe](https://www.washingtoninstitute.org/policy-analysis/anti-americanism-due-what-us-or-what-us-does)(An analysis of such trends reveals the central role that the Israeli-Palestinian conflict has played in shaping Arab and Muslim attitudes toward the United States. When citizens of Arab and Muslim countries look at U.S. policy on issues such as democracy or Iraq, they often see it through the painful prism of America's traditional support for Israel. The centrality of the Israeli-Palestinian conflict in Arab public opinion does not mean that Arabs care about Palestine more than about their own pocketbooks or their own countries. Nevertheless, they do place great importance on supporting Palestinians, just as many American Jews passionately support Israel.). By stymieing the conflict, the US is safer.
1.5.4.1.3.7. Con: Palestinian terrorism persists because [non-violent activism is unacknowledged](https://www.brookings.edu/blog/order-from-chaos/2021/05/18/dont-take-the-narrow-view-of-whats-happening-in-gaza/) by the international community. Thus, Palestinians have learned that only violence will draw international attention to their plight.
1.5.4.1.4. Con: If Israel believed that getting along with the Palestinians would pay dividends in terms of weakening their other adversaries, they'd already do so.
1.5.4.1.5. Con: Even if the US recognizes Palestine, there is no guarantee that Israel will. This limits progress in ameliorating the conflict and stabilising the region.
1.5.4.1.6. Pro: Recognising Palestine might bring more co-operation between the [PNSF](https://ecfr.eu/special/mapping_palestinian_politics/national_security_forces_nsf/) and the [IDF](https://www.idf.il/en/who-we-are/).
1.5.4.1.6.1. Pro: The Palestinian Authority [withdrew](https://www.iss.europa.eu/sites/default/files/EUISSFiles/Alert_12_Israel_and_Palestine.pdf)(Shortly before this, Palestinian Authority \(PA\) President Mahmoud Abbas threatened to end Israeli-Palestinian security cooperation in response to a new Knesset law which retroactively legalised some 4,000 Israeli settler houses built on private Palestinian land. Consequently, one of the cornerstones of the Oslo Accords now appears to be under real threat.) their co-operation with Israeli security forces in 2017, after the Knesset legalised Israeli settler homes on Palestinian land. If Palestine was recognised as a state by the US, this may make them feel more secure in their regional status \(p. 1\).
1.5.4.1.6.1.1. Pro: Before the withdrawal, the USA [funded](https://www.aljazeera.com/opinions/2016/3/9/what-palestinian-israeli-security-cooperation)(With the help of security assistance over the past eight years, the United States has helped the Palestinians build effective and professional forces that have resulted in a more stable, less violent West Bank.) the Palestinian security forces heavily, reducing crime.
1.5.4.1.6.1.2. Con: It is unlikely that US recognition would effectively ameliorate tensions between the two security forces due to the history of [lone wolf attacks](https://www.aljazeera.com/opinions/2016/3/9/what-palestinian-israeli-security-cooperation)(Recently though, with the rise of lone-wolf attacks and skirmishes between the Israeli military and Palestinians, security is becoming more fragile, but not due to a lack of effort from PA security forces.) from Palestinian members against Israelis.
1.5.4.1.6.2. Con: Palestinians often [do not trust](https://www.aljazeera.com/opinions/2016/3/9/what-palestinian-israeli-security-cooperation)(But it’s not all good news. More than 80 percent of Palestinians see the PA as corrupt. In addition, despite improvements, the PA security forces have continued to violate human rights including cases of torture and infringements on free speech \(PDF\).\n\nIn one recent example, the PA arrested journalist Salim Sweidan on questionable charges like “the publication of articles harmful to Palestinian national unity”. He was released four days later on $1,400 bail and an online apology, but still faces a court date on March 12 according to a conversation with Sweidan.\n\nAs Yezid Sayigh, a senior associate at the Carnegie Middle East Centre noted, “enhanced technical capability and growing professionalism do not guarantee the rule of law,” and in fact has only led to further authoritarianism.) their security forces meaning that there is little capacity to reduce high tensions in the community.
1.5.4.1.7. Pro: Recognizing Palestine could reduce political collateral damage in neighboring countries.
1.5.4.1.7.1. Pro: Algeria broke diplomatic ties with Morocco, citing Morocco's [normalization of relations with Israel](https://www.aljazeera.com/news/2021/8/25/morocco-algeria-diplomatic-ties-wildfires-hostile-actions)(Other criticism ranged from reported remarks by Morocco’s UN ambassador in mid-July to recent comments by Israel’s foreign minister on an historic visit to Morocco as part of both countries’ normalisation of ties.) as one of the "hostile actions" causing the fallout.
1.5.4.1.7.1.1. Con: Blaming Israel is the convenient route; their spat is largely regarding the [Moroccan occupation of Western Sahara](https://www.theafricareport.com/69335/morocco-algeria-western-sahara-conflict-shows-signs-of-escalation/).
1.5.4.1.7.2. Pro: A number of countries in the Middle East and North Africa [do not accept Israeli passports](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israeli_passport#Countries_that_do_not_accept_Israeli_passports); US recognition of Palestine could help normalize Israeli diplomacy with some of those countries.
1.5.4.1.7.3. Con: Some of the [most powerful countries](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/International_recognition_of_the_State_of_Palestine)(Among the G20, 9 countries \(Argentina, Brazil, China, India, Indonesia, Russia, Saudi Arabia, South Africa and Turkey\) have recognized Palestine as a state while 10 countries \(Australia, Canada, France, Germany, Italy, Japan, South Korea, Mexico, the United Kingdom and the United States\) have not.) in the world - many of which are allies of the US - do not recognize Palestine. The US cannot prioritize collateral damage in other countries over their immediate relationships with old allies.
1.5.4.2. Con: US recognition may lead to Israel recognising a Palestinian state and withdrawing from the occupied territories. This would heavily endanger Israeli security.
1.5.4.2.1. Con: US recognition does not entail unilateral Israeli withdrawal from Palestinian territories.
1.5.4.2.2. Con: Israel's withdrawal from the Palestinian territories would help to reduce tensions in the region and thus contribute to Israel's security.
1.5.4.2.3. Pro: A key Israeli Labor leader, Yigal Allon, author of the Allon plan, has [argued](https://www.jewishvirtuallibrary.org/israel-studies-an-anthology-jewish-settlement-in-israel) that "military bases were necessary in the West Bank hill country and along the Jordan River for purposes of defense." Supporting an independent Palestine would mean Israel would have to relinquish those bases.
1.5.4.2.4. Pro: The occupied Golan Heights [provide](https://www.researchgate.net/publication/268274252_Israeli_Control_of_the_Golan_Heights_High_Strategic_and_Moral_Ground_for_Israel)(p. 9) Israel with "important intelligence gathering capabilities" and are of vital strategic importance.
1.5.4.2.4.1. Pro: The current border along the watershed line – the hills in the Eastern part of the plateau – is the best defense line against a conventional military attack from the east \([p. 4](https://www.researchgate.net/publication/268274252_Israeli_Control_of_the_Golan_Heights_High_Strategic_and_Moral_Ground_for_Israel)\).
1.5.4.2.4.2. Pro: Occupation of the Golan Heights protects the civilians in Haifa from Syrian, Hezbollah and Iranian rocket fire. The Golan Heights also make protection of civilians in the "Finger of the Galilee" possible \([p. 8](https://www.researchgate.net/publication/268274252_Israeli_Control_of_the_Golan_Heights_High_Strategic_and_Moral_Ground_for_Israel)\).
1.5.4.2.5. Pro: Israel fears that a military withdrawal from the West Bank could lead to an [Islamist takeover of the area](http://www.jpost.com/Opinion/What-would-happen-if-Israel-withdrew-from-the-West-Bank-and-ended-the-siege-of-Gaza-442855), similar to what happened in the Gaza Strip.
1.5.4.3. Pro: Recognition might help Palestine make progress in establishing its own security apparatus that can help to curtail terrorism and other attacks against Israel.
1.5.4.3.1.
